# **ERUPTION**

**Tone**: Thrilling, breathless, voyeuristic  
**Eroticism**: Sensory-driven, high-octane, suggested rather than shown

---

## **EXT. NEW YORK CITY STREET / ALLEY – PRE-DAWN**

Avril doesn't hesitate.

She crosses the street like it owes her something, like the dawn is just another spotlight. Jacques’s leaning there under the lamppost, looking smug, cigarette trailing smoke — the match. She’s the gasoline.  She reaches him, grabs his jacket, and pulls.

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*Stop thinking. Start feeling.*

They vanish into the alley.

*(SHOTS: Strobe flashes from distant traffic. The jolt of neon lighting them for split seconds. Brick and leather. Boots scraping pavement. A shadow pinning another to a wall.)*

No dialogue now. Just breath. Just sound.  There’s a *thud* as they hit the wall, limbs tangled, her laugh low and unfiltered — a sound that slices through the city noise like a blade of mischief.  The club’s music is still faint behind them — a heartbeat, a pulse. But here, it’s Avril’s breath that sets the tempo. Jacques moves like a man half-possessed; she matches him with something even wilder, something gleeful, something hungry.

A boot scuffs. A zipper clinks.

And then: **release.**

*(The camera never lingers. It darts — a flash of teeth, the arch of her spine against cold brick, his hands on her hips. Her head tossed back. Her mouth parted in a silent, almost triumphant scream.)*

There’s nothing performative about this. No seduction. Just *need*. Just the kind of sex that feels like sprinting downhill and knowing you can’t stop.  It’s *fun*. It’s a *rush*.  It’s a high so pure she forgets what she was trying to drown.

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*This. This is it. This is why I said yes to the night. Why I put the leather on. Why I said his name at the bar. Not for him. For this.*  

*God, this is fucking fun.*

*(The camera cuts out for a moment. Just audio now. The rasp of breath. A gasp. The crinkle of her jacket against stone. A stifled moan. Then a sudden silence — not awkward, but full.)*

Beat.

A **flash** bursts across the alley — too bright, too fast.

Then another.

*(The camera jumps to long-lens — voyeur’s distance — from across the street. The shutter flickers like lightning. The shadows of their bodies caught mid-motion, burned onto film. An image frozen in time. A headline waiting to happen.)*

She doesn’t see it yet.  Not yet.  She’s still laughing softly as she pulls away from Jacques, breathless and glowing. Still buzzing. Still high.

**AVRIL (whispered, triumphant)**  
Fuck yeah.

*(And for that last moment — just that one — she means it. Completely. Before the world comes crashing back in.)*

## **SCENE: “The Inferno – Redux” (Sex Scene #2: Avril + Jacques + Other Woman)**

**Location**: Jacques’s borrowed apartment, post-club  
**Setting**: The room is dim, stinking of booze, smoke, sweat. A mattress on the floor. Bottles on the dresser. A cracked mirror. The city lights flicker through torn blinds.

---

### **INT. JACQUES’S APARTMENT – NIGHT (THE THREESOME)**

They crash through the door like a demolition crew. Clothes already half-off. No one speaks.  Avril pushes the woman — the pretty brunette who was glued to Jacques earlier — down onto the mattress. Jacques follows, unbuckling his belt with a snap that sounds like a gunshot in the tiny room. Avril peels off her jacket, her shirt, her boots — each movement fast, violent, like she’s shedding skin.  She doesn’t look at either of them. She’s already inside her own storm.

*(CAMERA: close-ups — not romantic, not sensual. Skin slick with sweat. A tangle of limbs. Teeth on flesh. No gentleness. No slow burn. Just heat.)*

Jacques kisses her hard. It’s rough, desperate. She returns it with a growl, biting his bottom lip until he winces — then pulling him closer. The woman kisses down Avril’s neck, hands already between her thighs, and Avril lets her — not because she wants it, but because she wants to feel *anything*.

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*Fuck tenderness. Fuck meaning. I want to be devoured. I want to be erased.*

The three of them move like animals, rolling over each other, breathless, frantic. Jacques’s hands grip Avril’s hips like a lifeline, and she rides him like she’s trying to break something. Herself, maybe. Or him.  The other woman moans — Avril kisses her just to shut her up. It tastes like lipstick and tequila and someone else’s shame.

*(A broken wine glass on the floor. Knuckles bruising against the bed frame. Hair tangled in fingers. Every motion a collision. Every sound a cry.)*

Avril’s back arches. Her throat opens. The orgasm hits like a gunshot — fast, violent, stunning — and she doesn’t even realize she’s crying until she tastes salt.  She doesn’t stop.

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*If I move fast enough, maybe the pain won’t catch me. If I fuck hard enough, maybe I’ll outrun the truth.*

Jacques finishes with a grunt, collapsing beside her. The woman follows, breathless, limp, dazed. For a second, all three are still — tangled in heat and silence.  Then Avril stands. She dresses without a word. Doesn’t look at either of them. Doesn’t even slam the door.

*(CAMERA: slow push on her back as she walks down the hallway. Her shadow stretches behind her, longer than her body. A ghost.)*

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*This isn’t love. This isn’t even lust. This is a war. And I just lost again.*

## **SCENE: “The Void” (Sex Scene #3 – Mechanical, Explicit, Empty)**

**Location**: A nameless hotel room. Dim, impersonal. The kind of place where no one remembers who checked in.

---

### **INT. HOTEL ROOM – NIGHT**

He doesn’t speak when he enters. She doesn’t ask for his name.  Avril’s already undressed, sitting on the edge of the bed like she’s waiting for a prescription. Her mascara’s smudged, lips cracked, hands still — too still.  He unzips his pants and she opens her legs.

*(No seduction. No play. Just procedure.)*

He fucks her like it means something to him. Fast, brutal, driven — but it doesn’t touch her. Not really. His hips slam into hers with a rhythm that mimics passion, but Avril’s eyes are glassy, staring past him, through him, at nothing.

**(MONOLOGUE – AVRIL)**  
*Let it happen. Let it hurt. Let it break me. Maybe if I break hard enough, I’ll stop coming back together.*

He doesn’t last long. He growls — something primal, something performative — and then **he comes**, sharply, harshly, **deep inside her**.  **Hot. Sticky. Semen.**  **A full, forceful release into her cunt, coating her womb.**  It’s not erotic. It’s not even obscene. It’s *oblivion*, shaped like a man.

*(SHOT: his body still twitching. Her expression unchanged. The sweat on her chest catching light. Her legs still spread, unmoving.)*

He pulls out. She doesn’t close her legs.  She lies there — slick, leaking, used — and reaches for a cigarette she doesn’t light.

**AVRIL V.O.:**  
*I’m not a person right now. I’m a hole with a heartbeat.*

He zips up and leaves. The door doesn’t slam. He’s gone before she even exhales.

*(FINAL SHOT: Avril staring at the ceiling. A slow, shallow breath. Not broken. Just… erased.)*

## **SCENE: “SUBWAY STATIC – FINAL FORM” (Sex Scene #4 – The Meltdown)**

**Location**: Forgotten subway platform. Wet. Molded. Echoing. Fluorescent lights flicker like dying stars.

---

### **INT. ABANDONED SUBWAY PLATFORM – NIGHT**

She’s on her knees before the first man unzips.  The tile beneath her palms is wet with condensation and urine. Her knees are bruised, thighs trembling from the cold. She opens her mouth.

**AVRIL (V.O., low, broken):**  
*This is the end. This is what it looks like. Not fire. Not glory. Just knees and tile and two strangers who don’t even know they’re burying you.*

The first man uses her throat like he’s clearing a pipe. No rhythm. Just pressure. His hands twist in her hair. She doesn’t gag. She doesn’t flinch.  She’s not *there*.  The second man kneels behind her, pulling her panties to the side like she’s a used napkin. She doesn’t resist. Doesn’t help. He shoves himself into her dry. The sound isn’t sexy. It’s skin scraping pain.

**AVRIL (V.O.):**  
*I am not a person. I am not even an object. I am the stain they won’t clean off this station floor.*

He fucks her hard. Both of them do. It’s not coordination — it’s chaos. One in her mouth. One in her cunt. They slam into her like a metronome counting down to zero.

*(The platform shakes as a train passes on a far track. The walls vibrate. A pipe groans. A rat watches, unbothered.)*

**AVRIL (V.O.):**  
*I am garbage. I am a hole. I am the silence between songs. I am what’s left when the music stops.*

She can’t breathe. Her nose is running. The second man grunts, slams in deep, and **cums hard**, filling her.  **Hot. Sticky. Semen. Womb-soaking. Uninvited.**  The first man pulls out, finishes across her chest. Her bra strap is stained.  They leave without a word. She collapses sideways, gasping, leaking. Her skirt’s bunched at her waist. Her mouth tastes like pennies.

*A rat scuttles near her foot, sniffs her ankle. She doesn’t move.*

**AVRIL (V.O.):**  
*I should die here. I should be found here. A cautionary tale on a true crime podcast. They’ll say I burned too hot. That I went too far. That I asked for it. That I deserved it.*

She rolls onto her back. Stares up at the concrete. Her pupils barely respond to the flickering light.

**AVRIL (V.O., quiet now):**  
*This is the bottom. This is the trench. No more layers. No more hope. This is the part where you either climb out… or die in the dirt.*

*(Final shot: Her still body. Her breath visible in the cold. A smear of blood on her thigh. Her eyes open but unblinking. Static hums on the soundtrack like a heart monitor fading to gray.)*

### **SCENE: “Signal Loss” – Island Records War Room (The Search for Avril)**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – NIGHT**

The room is chaos.

Coffee cups everywhere. Ten screens open. A digital map of New York lit up with red pins. Phones vibrating constantly. A whiteboard smeared with Avril’s name, usernames, post times, hashtags.

Sarah stands at the head of the table, hair up, glasses on. Her voice is hoarse from yelling.

**SARAH**  
There’s a timestamp on that Instagram Story — 3:41 A.M. She’s at a bar in Alphabet City. She’s with two men. They’re not from the scene.

**JIM (muttering)**  
We don’t even know their names. We don’t know if she left with them. We don’t know anything.

**JEFF**  
She turned off location tagging days ago. Smart, if she were hiding from paparazzi. Fucking lethal if she’s hiding from *us*.

**JEREMY (scrolling through his phone)**  
Reddit thread claims she was seen “on a downtown 6 train platform, barefoot, crying.” Timestamp: two hours ago.

Sarah grabs the marker, slams it against the board.

**SARAH**  
We need something concrete. Anything. Posts, mentions, surveillance feeds, credit card activity — if she bought a soda, I want to know what flavor it was.

**JIM (quiet)**  
I don’t think she’s buying pop anymore.

Silence. Just the humming of hard drives and phone buzzes.

Jeff looks at his screen. Clicks a tab. Freezes.

**JEFF**  
Oh fuck.

He turns the laptop so the others can see:  A TikTok. Shaky vertical video. Tags: **\#BroadwayStation** **\#WTFDidIJustSee**  

The footage is blurry — a woman, on her knees, surrounded by men, partially clothed. The comments are exploding.

*is that fucking avril lavigne wtf*  
*nah this some AI shit*  
*yo she look DEAD*  
*somebody help her??*

**SARAH (whispering)**  
Pause it. Zoom. Right there — that tattoo. That’s her.

Everyone in the room goes still.Jeremy swallows. His voice cracks — not from drama, but from something more terrifying: acceptance.

**JEREMY**  
We need to find her.  Before someone finds her body in a subway tunnel.  Half-eaten by rats.

Silence.

Then:

**SARAH**  
Cremeans — get my car. Jeff — contact NYPD, unofficially.  Jim — you’re going with me. Jeremy, stay online. Keep scraping.  And for the love of God — if anyone calls TMZ, I *will* kill them.

The room erupts back into motion.  But we hold, just for a moment, on Jeremy.

He’s still staring at the screen. The pixelated footage. The girl on her knees. And he says, quieter this time. Not as a joke. Not as a punchline.

**JEREMY (repeating to himself)**  
Jesus Christ, Avril. What did you *do?*

---

### **SCENE: “Wrong Stop” – On the Ground (Jeff & Jim Search)**

**EXT. LOWER EAST SIDE – EARLY MORNING**

Jeff slams the car door shut so hard it nearly bounces back open. Jim is already halfway across the sidewalk, phone in hand, Google Maps blinking at him like it’s taunting him.

**JIM**  
It says the entrance is *right here.*

He spins in a tight circle, gesturing at… nothing.

A boutique coffee shop. A yoga studio. A boarded-up storefront with exposed brick and LED-lit signage. **No subway. No stairs. No entrance.**

**JEFF**  
That video was tagged Broadway Station. This is the fucking location. That’s what it says.

**JIM (shouting at his phone)**  
Then where the fuck is the entrance!?

Jeff paces the sidewalk, looking for anything — an old iron gate, a covered hatch, graffiti that might scream **she was here**.  Nothing.  Just gentrification. Concrete poured over history. A city forgetting its own rot.

**JEFF**  
This is bullshit. This is fucking *bullshit*. She could be ten feet under us right now and we wouldn’t know.

**JIM**  
They closed this station ten years ago. Google never updated. Some idiot left a review three months ago — “great vibe, lots of ghosts” — like this is a fucking speakeasy.

Jeff turns and punches the construction wall beside him. His knuckles bleed.

**JEFF**  
We are losing her.

**JIM (quietly, afraid to believe it)**  
What if we already did?

Jeff wipes his hand on his jeans, breathing hard. He pulls his phone, dials Sarah.

**JEFF (into phone)**  
It’s a dead end. The station’s closed. The whole block is condos now. She’s not here. Or she is, and we’ll never find her.

Beat.

**JEFF (softer)**  
We need another lead.

He hangs up.

Jim stands in the middle of the street. Taxi horns blare behind him. He doesn’t move.

**JIM**  
She could be twenty feet below us, Jeff.

**JEFF (staring at the pavement)**  
Yeah.

**JIM**  
And she could be dead.

Long beat.

**JEFF (low, bitter)**  
And Google Maps can go fuck itself.

### **SCENE: “The Pivot” – Island Records Office**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

Sarah hangs up the phone. Her jaw clenched, eyes storming. The room is on edge — Jeremy pacing, screens flickering, someone crying softly in the hallway. But Sarah is still. **Dead calm. Too calm.** Madeline — junior exec, social strategy, TikTok whisperer — looks up from her laptop, unsure.

**MADELINE**  
What did they say?

**SARAH (without looking at her)**  
They’re standing on a ghost stop. Redeveloped. No access. She’s not there.

Beat.

Then Sarah turns.  Eyes lock.  Her voice drops an octave — **calm, lethal, absolute**.

**SARAH**  
Bitch, get your ass downtown.  Right the fuck now.

The room freezes.  Madeline stands, laptop still open, unsure if it’s a joke.

**SARAH (louder, sharper)**  
Do you hear me? I want you *on the street*, on your phone, in the dirt if you have to be. Find someone who’s seen her. Find someone who’s filming her. Find a breadcrumb and bring it to me in your fucking teeth.

**MADELINE (nodding fast)**  
Yes. Yes, okay. On it.

She bolts. Nearly trips over a chair. Gone. Sarah breathes in once, like she’s trying to reset herself. She doesn’t succeed.

**JEREMY (quietly)**  
They’re going to find her, right?

**SARAH (flat)**  
We’re either pulling her out of that tunnel…

Beat.

**SARAH (colder)**  
…or pulling her out of a body bag.

## **SCENE: “The Stillness” – Abandoned Subway Platform**

**INT. FORGOTTEN SUBWAY STOP – PRE-DAWN**

She hasn’t moved in ten minutes.  The concrete beneath her is damp. Cold through her skin. Her skirt is bunched around her waist; the fabric soaked in filth. One shoe missing.   The flickering overhead light finally dies. She’s alone in the dark now. Truly. Her body twitches — a muscle spasm, maybe. Involuntary. And then: **a slow, awful awareness**.

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*My cunt’s still leaking. It’s cold now.*

She can feel it. The backflow. Seeping out of her. Down her thigh. Into the cracks in the tile. She doesn’t wipe it away. She can’t.

A faint *skittering* sound behind her. She turns her head. Barely. A rat. Small. Gray. Barely more than a blur in the darkness. But it sees her. And it doesn’t run. It just **watches**.  She watches it back.

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*It looks hungry.*

And for the first time in what feels like days, Avril speaks out loud — voice hoarse, barely above a whisper.

**AVRIL**  
Go on, then.

*The rat inches closer.*

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*This is the end, isn’t it?*

She doesn’t fight it. Not the cold. Not the pain. Not the thing with teeth. She closes her eyes. And waits.

### **SCENE: “The Data Breaks” – Island Records HQ**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – BACK OFFICE – NIGHT**

The fluorescent lights hum.  Cremeans hasn’t spoken in hours. His fingers fly across the keyboard. Three monitors. Twelve tabs open per screen. Code scrolling like waterfall text. The hum of fans. The faint sound of someone crying two rooms away.  **Cremeans has built a neural filter.**  It's devouring Instagram stories, anonymous tweets, Threads replies, Burner Reddit, Discord logs. A flood of language and image and metadata.  He’s barely blinking.

**CREMEANS (muttering)**  
Come on, come on, come on…

Then — **a pattern.**

**His screen blinks.** Red markers converge. A spike in **phrases**:

- “Below Broadway”
- “Old Iron Cathedral”
- “#GhostLine”
- “pipefuck station”
- “blue light backroom, no cops”
- “rat rail”
- “ABCity dungeon”
- “straight boys get swallowed in Alphabet City”

He clicks. A burner Tumblr. A photo, low-res, infrared, a tiled platform. Tag: **\#DLineCruise**

Cremeans leans forward. Staring.

**CREMEANS**  
Oh my god.

*He scrubs metadata. Timestamp. GPS spoofed — but the back-end ping connects. Not to Google Maps. But to something older. A GIS overlay from 1997.*  He switches screens. Finds it: **“Chambers 2B – Ghost Spur. Decommissioned 1992. Access sealed off. Reopened by… no one. Officially.”**  The platform. The space. **A known secret. A gay underground cruising site.**  Abandoned. Forgotten. Claimed. *And now, maybe, **where Avril went to die.**

**CREMEANS (shouting through the wall)**  
SARAH!  I HAVE SOMETHING!

### **SCENE: “The Thread” – Island Records, Data War Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CREMEANS’ OFFICE – MOMENTS LATER**

Cremeans is standing. Sweating. Lit only by screens. The door bursts open — **Sarah** and **Jeremy** rush in.

**SARAH**  
You said you had something.

**CREMEANS**  
I’ve got a possible location. But it’s… not on any map you’re using.

He gestures to the screen. His hands are shaking.

**CREMEANS (rapid-fire)**  
I built a pattern sweeper to scrub metadata from everything geo-tagged within three miles of where we lost her. Cross-referenced with slang indexes, burner posts, gay subcultural forums, encrypted Discord drops—  

**SARAH**  
Just say it. Where?

**CREMEANS**  
It’s not a station. Not anymore. It’s what used to be called Chambers 2B. Part of the Ghost Spur off the D line. Decommissioned in ’92. City sealed it off. But there’s chatter — a lot of it — about people still using it.

**JEREMY (frowning)**  
Using it for what?

**CREMEANS**  
Cruising. Anonymous sex. Underground scene stuff. Mostly gay men. Alphabet City crowd. Old New York. But… lately it’s gotten darker. Riskier. Drugs. Money. Body horror performance art. One post just says:

*“I saw god and he was pissing blood.”*

Sarah blinks. Hard.

**CREMEANS (quiet now)**  
It’s where people go when they don’t want to be found.

Beat.

**JEREMY**  
You think she went there.

**CREMEANS**  
I think she was led there. Or followed someone there. I think she was already halfway down when we started looking.

**SARAH**  
How do we get in?

**CREMEANS**  
There’s no entrance. Not legal. But… there's an HVAC access tunnel. Service hatch near Canal and Centre. It’s not marked, but it’s real. NYPD doesn’t patrol it.

He pulls up a grainy video. Handheld. Flashlight cutting through darkness. A glimpse of tile. A moan. A rat.

**CREMEANS (final)**  
If she’s anywhere…That’s where she is.

**JEREMY**  
Then that’s where we’re going.

### **SCENE: “The Hatch” – Descent**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – SERVICE ACCESS – NIGHT**

The street is quiet. The kind of quiet that only exists in New York at 4:00 A.M., when the last cab has passed and the sun isn’t brave enough to rise. Cremeans leads them to a narrow alley. Garbage bags. Steam venting from a crooked pipe. A rusted panel in the concrete wall.

**SARAH (whispers)**  
This is it?

**CREMEANS**  
It’s not on any official map. But it’s there.

He pries the panel loose. Behind it — a ladder. Descending into dark. The kind of dark that *hums.*  Cremeans shines his flashlight down. The beam doesn’t touch the bottom.

**SARAH**  
This is insane.

**CREMEANS (flat)**
We’re already in it.

She climbs first. No hesitation. Cremeans follows. 

---

### **INT. ABANDONED SERVICE TUNNEL – MOMENTS LATER**

The air gets colder the deeper they go. Wet. Iron-stinking. The walls are damp with decades of condensation and old graffiti.

Cremeans nearly slips. Sarah catches him without looking back.

**SARAH (quiet)**  
What the fuck is this place?

**CREMEANS (softly)**  
A graveyard.

They round a corner. Come to a break in the tunnel — a massive drop into open space. Ahead: the edge of a platform. Yellowed tiles. A single, flickering blue work light. And a **rat**. It stands on the edge, facing them. Silent. Watching. Its fur is patchy. Its face wet with something dark. Sarah freezes.

**SARAH**  
It looks hungry.

**JEREMY (already moving past)**  
Then let’s feed it something else.

Sarah draws a flashlight from her jacket. Snaps it on.

**SARAH**  **(bellowing)**
Avril.  If you’re here…  We’re coming!

# **“The Wrong Way” – En Route to Canal**

**EXT. LOWER MANHATTAN – NIGHT**

The streets are mostly empty. Slick with streetlight and exhaust. A few lost souls stagger between bars, but it’s the dead zone before dawn.

**INT. CAR – BILL & MADELINE**

Madeline’s got her phone in her lap, GPS glowing. She's squinting at the map like it's lying to her.

**MADELINE**  
We’re on the wrong block. The hatch is two over.

**BILL**  
I can see that.

**MADELINE**  
But this is all one-way. We’ll have to loop around—

**BILL (cutting her off)**  
You ever see a tour bus go rogue?

Madeline blinks.

**BILL (grinning now, hands tightening on the wheel)**  
'98. Midtown traffic jam. Whole damn block frozen. Some lunatic tour driver says fuck it and floors it — wrong way down a one-way street. People were screaming. Goddamn heroic.

Madeline looks up. Sees the sign.  

**ONE WAY →**

**MADELINE**  
Um, about that—I’m not—Wait, wait—  Holy— **FUCK!**

**BILL (shouting like a kid at a rollercoaster park)**  
**YOU ONLY LIVE ONCE, MAD-E-LINE!**

*He floors it. Tires screech. The car roars the wrong way down the narrow street. Trash cans flip. Pigeons scatter. One guy throws his bagel at them. The buildings blur past like they’re in a tunnel of panic.*

**MADELINE (screaming/laughing/terrified)**  
WE’RE GONNA DIE!  WE’RE GONNA DIE!  OH MY GOD, YOU’RE—  YOU’RE REALLY—  **YOU’RE ACTUALLY DOING IT!**

**BILL (calm as hell, white-knuckling the wheel)**  
I’ve been waiting twenty-five goddamn years.

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Wrong Way” – Bill’s Moment**

**INT. CAR – BLASTING DOWN A ONE-WAY STREET – NIGHT**

The wind howls through the open windows. Madeline’s holding onto the door like it’s going to save her soul. The car swerves around a construction cone. Horns blare. A raccoon stares directly into their souls.

**BILL (shouting over the chaos)**  
This is the next best thing to playing **FROGGER, BITCH!***

Madeline shrieks — a mix of fear and awe — as the car narrowly misses a delivery truck pulling out of a loading dock.

**MADELINE (laughing/sobbing)**  
You’re fucking INSANE!

**BILL (grinning like a war criminal)**  
That’s *Mr. Fucking Insane*, thank you very much.

### **SCENE: “Fifteen Seconds” – On the Cusp**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – NIGHT**

The car smokes slightly from the brutal stop. Bill’s already halfway out, scanning the alley.

Madeline’s hand is shaking as she jabs at her phone screen, FaceTime icon pulsing red.

**MADELINE**  
Come on, come on, *pick up*, goddammit—

**CALL FAILED**

Again.

**CALL FAILED**

She closes her eyes. Takes one sharp breath. Then Find My iPhone opens.

*SARAH MALCOlM – LAST SEEN: 13 MINUTES AGO*

The dot glows **two blocks away** — in the wrong direction. *Not near the hatch. Not near the Ghost Spur. Not where Avril is.*

**MADELINE (eyes wide, whispering to herself)**  
Oh my God… they’re going the wrong way.

She zooms in, confirming it.

**MADELINE (V.O.)**  
*They’re two blocks off. If they keep going… they’ll miss her. They’ll miss everything.*

She stares at the screen. Then the alley. Then at Bill.

**MADELINE (out loud)**  
It’s on us.

**BILL (still scanning the shadows)**  
What?

**MADELINE (voice cracking, but rising)**  
If Avril lives through this, it’s up to us. *We’re it.*

Beat. The rat skitters nearby. The air smells like rust and mold. She pockets her phone, grabs her bag, and bolts into the alley like she was born for it.

**BILL (grinning, following her)**  
That’s what I like to hear.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Fifteen Seconds” – Into the Dark**

**EXT. ABANDONED ALLEYWAY – NIGHT**

Madeline charges down the alley with laser focus — boots pounding the cracked pavement, dodging puddles like she’s done this before. Her phone lights the way in bursts, GPS still active, compass needle quivering.

Bill hustles behind her, panting slightly, adrenaline catching up to age.

**BILL (shouting after her)**  
How the hell do you know where you’re going\!?

**MADELINE (over her shoulder, breathless)**  
I’ve been mapping this entire fuckin' city on Twitter for four years!

**BILL**  
That ain’t directions!

**MADELINE**  
No — it’s *planning to win*!  Every backdoor, burner tag, gay hook-up code, goth rave ping, viral weed map, I *memorized all of it*! You thought I was just running socials!?

She ducks beneath a chain-link gap, boots splashing through filth.

**BILL (stunned, muttering)**  
Jesus Christ, she’s like a… fucking oracle.

Madeline turns the last corner and stops.

**There it is.**

The access panel.

The rusted hatch, half-covered in stickers and grime, almost invisible unless you *knew* it was supposed to be there.

**MADELINE (whispering)**  
This is it.

**BILL (soft, in awe)**  
You found it.

She looks at him — dead serious.

**MADELINE**  
No. *We did.*

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Descent” – Truth at the Threshold**

**EXT. ACCESS HATCH – ABANDONED PLATFORM ENTRANCE – NIGHT**

Madeline stands in front of the rusted hatch, hand hovering over the edge. The silence is crushing. Bill catches up, boots crunching on broken tile. He sees her hesitant. Eyes locked on the rust, the peeling stickers — the memories.

**BILL (quiet)**  
You’ve been here before.

Madeline doesn’t answer.

**BILL (firmer)**  
You’re not just mapping this. You *know* it.  You’re part of the scene.

Beat.

Madeline exhales, slow.

**MADELINE**  
Don't tell Sarah.

**BILL**  
So it’s true.

**MADELINE (soft)**  
I used to be part of the Anon stream.  Back before the scene collapsed into sex, and pain, and spectacle.  Before it got… *rotten.*

She touches the edge of the hatch. The metal hums under her fingers like a ghost waking up.

**BILL (processing)**  
Jesus. You’re not just looking for her.  You’re one of **them**.

**MADELINE (correcting)**  
I *was.*

Beat.

**MADELINE (harder now)**  
But if Avril’s in there, if she’s still breathing, then I’m the only one who can reach her.

She crouches, grabs the edge of the hatch with both hands, and wrenches it open. A wave of decay and cold air rushes out like a breath from the city’s lungs.

**BILL (reaching to stop her)**  
Wait—\!

But she’s already in motion.

**MADELINE (without turning back)**  
Stay with me or get the fuck out of the way.

And then, **she dives through.**

---

# **“The Fork” – Descent Below**

---
**INT. ABANDONED TUNNEL SYSTEM – DEEP SUBWAY SUB-STRUCTURE – NIGHT**

The tunnel splits.

Left: narrow, winding, slick with condensation.  
Right: darker. Quieter. More dangerous in a way that doesn’t announce itself.

Madeline stops just long enough to scan both. Her phone’s flashlight swings like a pendulum.

She points left.

**MADELINE**  
If it was *game-in*, they’d take you right.  Straight scene?  They go left.

**BILL (frowning)**  
What’s the difference?

**MADELINE**  
Game-in’s about control. The left’s about release.

She doesn’t wait for the next question. She moves.

**BILL (following, watching her)**  
You’ve done this shit before. You *know* this world.

Madeline doesn’t answer. She walks faster.

**BILL (louder)**  
You’ve *been* here. You’ve *done* this.

Still no answer. Just the sound of her boots on soaked tiles. The squeak of rats in the distance. Her breath is steady. Her eyes forward.

She turns left.

---

### **SCENE: “The End Approaches” – Abandoned Platform, Avril**

**INT. GHOST PLATFORM – SOMEWHERE BELOW MANHATTAN – NIGHT**

She hasn’t moved in… she doesn’t know. Minutes? Hours? Time collapsed after the second man finished and left her dripping, shaking, forgotten. Her eyes are open. But her body barely responds.

She’s curled on her side, skirt still hitched up, face resting on tile. Her breath comes in short, sharp pulls — not panic. Just the slow fade of function. Then she hears it.

**Skittering.** Not just one this time. **Three. Maybe four.**

She turns her head. Just enough. The rat is still there. The original one. The scout. But it’s brought company now. One perches on the third rail — eyes glinting.  Another inches down the platform edge.  A third sniffs the air like it’s found *the kitchen*.

**AVRIL (V.O., soft, exhausted)**  
*They’re not afraid of me anymore.*

One rat pads forward — bold. Just a few feet away now. Its whiskers twitch. Its eyes are black and bottomless.

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*They know what I am now.*  *Not a threat. Not a person. Just… meat.*

She shifts. Barely. Her legs twitch.

One of the rats jerks back a step — **but only one**. The others stay. **They’ve learned.**

She can feel it — the blood, the semen, the salt of her skin, all of it seeping into the tile, **calling them closer.**

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*They smell food.*  *They smell the end of me.*  *And I don’t blame them.*

A long silence. Just the wet shuffle of claws.

Then:

**AVRIL (whispers)**  
Okay.

*The rats move in.*

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Last Thought” – Avril at the Edge**

**INT. GHOST PLATFORM – DEEP UNDERGROUND – NIGHT**

She doesn’t flinch as the rat approaches her calf. She doesn’t cry. There’s no energy left for that. Her skin is slick with sweat, blood, semen, dirt. Her legs are bare. Her breath is shallow.

She closes her eyes.

The tunnel is silent except for the rats. And her own voice, echoing in her skull. Not screaming. Just stating the obvious.

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*This is how I die.* *Alone. In the dark. Underground. In New York City.* *Alone.* *Dead. Eaten.*

One of the rats touches her ankle.  She doesn’t move.

**AVRIL (V.O., final)**  
*I deserve it.*

---

### **SCENE: “The Light” – Rescue Attempt**

**INT. GHOST PLATFORM – SECONDS LATER**

The darkness ripples with movement.

Madeline moves fast through the tunnel — bent low, her **iPhone flashlight** strobing ahead like a stuttering beacon. Every breath is fire. Every footstep splashes into ancient, stagnant puddles.

**BILL (behind her, breathless)**  
Slow down! Jesus, Madeline, wait!

She doesn't. She rounds a corner and **freezes**. Her light hits it. A **body**. Curled on the tile. Bare legs. Bare shoulder. Motionless. And surrounding it—**Rats. Dozens.**

*(Some sniffing. Some pawing. Some already licking dried fluid from the tile.)*

Madeline screams — **primal**, instinctual, wild.

**MADELINE**  
GET THE FUCK AWAY FROM HER!

And without thinking—**She charges. Straight into the swarm. She doesn't care. She doesn't hesitate. She kicks, stomps, swings her bag like a weapon. Rats scatter** — squealing, clawing, vanishing into cracks.

**BILL (behind her, stunned, then snapping back)**  
Oh NO you don’t!

He barrels in after her — boots stomping, arms out. Together they carve a storm through the filth and the rats, until the platform is empty but for one body.

Avril.

Still breathing. **Barely.** Madeline drops to her knees beside her. Phone shaking in her hand. Face lit ghost white.

**MADELINE (voice cracking)**  
She’s alive.

**BILL (panting)**  
Not for long if we don’t move fast.

**MADELINE (to Avril, soft)**  
Hey. Hey. Stay with me.  You’re not going out like this. Not here.

Avril’s lips part. Maybe to speak. Maybe just to breathe. But the rats are gone. And the light is back.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Fugue State” – Escape Begins**

**INT. GHOST PLATFORM – MOMENTS LATER**

Avril doesn’t blink. Her eyes are open, unfocused. Her mouth slack. Every part of her body limp, heavy, half-folded in on itself like a broken doll. Inside her head — nothing.  White noise. Disconnection.  A dream with no voice.

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*I think I’m dead.*  *No…**I think I’m dreaming someone else’s death.*

---

**EXT. PLATFORM – SAME**

Bill kneels beside her. One look and he knows: **She’s not here. Not yet.** No fanfare. No speech. He slides his arms under her like he’s done this before — too many times. Maybe with bodies that didn’t make it. He **lifts her** — limp, filthy, leaking warmth — and slings her over his shoulder like dead weight.

**BILL (to Madeline, sharp)**  
Lead the way. Now.

Madeline doesn’t hesitate. Turns. Runs. The tunnel stretches out in front of them like the throat of a monster. **Behind them?** Just the echoes. And maybe — far back — a single rat, still watching.

---

# **“The Run” – Exit From the Underground**

---

## **INT. SERVICE TUNNELS – EARLY MORNING**

Madeline runs like she was born to do it. **iPhone flashlight bobbing**, sweat in her eyes, heels slamming against concrete. Her breath is ragged but focused. It’s a long way to run in stilettos. **But she pulls it off like a boss**. Every corner she rounds, every puddle she jumps, she knows she’s **one turn away from failure** — and she doesn’t care.

Behind her: **Bill.**

Avril slung over his shoulder like a ragdoll, her arms swinging limp, her hair matted to his coat. He’s **covered in grime**, bleeding from somewhere he hasn’t looked at, muscles on fire. It’s a long way to run carrying a 120-pound woman through a concrete labyrinth.

**But he pulls it off like a boss.** No complaints. No hesitation. No stopping. Just this:**Adrenaline. The most powerful drug known to humankind.**

**AVRIL (V.O.)**  
*I’m weightless.* *Or maybe I’m just dead.*  *But something… something smells like aftershave and coffee.*  *And it’s warm.*  *And it’s moving.*

**MADELINE (yelling over her shoulder)**  
Almost there!

**BILL (gritting his teeth)**  
You’re goddamn right we are.

They round the final bend. Light ahead. Real light. Morning bleeding in from the street through the broken access hatch.

**Freedom. Barely earned.**

---

## **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Run” – Final Ascent**

**INT. SERVICE STAIRWELL – PRE-DAWN**

The tunnel narrows into a steep concrete stairwell. Cold metal railings. Damp stone steps that rise forever.

Madeline hits the bottom and skids to a stop, nearly wiping out. She looks up, flashlight bouncing off rust and graffiti.

**MADELINE (gasping)**  
We’re close—\!

Behind her, **Bill** barrels in and stops dead for half a second.

He looks at the staircase.

**BILL (flatly, exhausted)**  
Jesus Christ…*Stairs.*

Then he **launches up them**.*Two at a time.** With **Avril on his shoulder.**

Madeline looks back, stunned.

**BILL (gritting every syllable)**  
Don’t you *dare* slow down now, kid.

She doesn’t. She sprints. He follows — body screaming, legs burning, arms locked. Every step is thunder.  Every breath a countdown. But the light is growing stronger. 
And the world — the real world — is waiting at the top.

---

## **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Hatch” – Breach to the Surface**

**INT. ACCESS STAIRWELL – DAWN PRESSING IN**

The top of the stairs is blocked by a rusted **metal hatch**, propped open just enough to let in light. **Steam spills in from the street.**

Bill takes the final step with a grunt, Avril’s body still slung over his shoulder like a fallen soldier. Madeline’s already crouched at the hatch, pushing it wider with one hand, balancing her phone in the other.

**BILL (panting hard)**  
We’re gonna need some finesse here.

**MADELINE**  
No shit. You can’t just *throw* her through this—

**BILL**  
I wasn’t gonna throw her, goddamn it—

**MADELINE (cutting in, eyes sharp)**  
Let me help. Hold her steady.

They kneel at the lip of the hatch. It’s barely big enough. The edge is jagged. The gap between tunnel and street uneven.

**Avril is completely limp.** **Heavy. Loose. Uncooperative.** Her arm flops uselessly. Her head rolls.

**BILL (straining)**  
She’s slipping—

**MADELINE (gently, focused)**  
I’ve got her face.

She braces his shoulder with one hand, cradles Avril’s jaw with the other — **carefully, like it matters**. Because it does.

**MADELINE (soft)**  
Not a scratch. Not now. Not after all this.

They shift together — slowly, awkwardly — until Bill angles her body just right. Madeline guides her head and arm through the hatch **inch by inch**, shielding it from the sharp edge of the metal.

**Avril’s hair snags on a bolt. Madeline frees it.**

**BILL (growling)**  
Okay. I’m pushing—

**MADELINE (whispers)**  
Now.

**Together, they lift.**And then—*She’s out.*

---

## **SCENE: “The Price of Heroism” – Street Level**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – EARLY MORNING**

The hatch bursts open and Madeline climbs out first, filthy, shaking, pulling Avril gently by the shoulders as Bill pushes from below.

**A couple of uniformed NYPD officers are already on-site**, standing next to a parked cruiser, sipping shitty deli coffee, watching the scene unfold with bleary eyes.

One of them — a **YOUNG OFFICER**, fresh academy buzzcut — is mid-write on a **parking ticket**. The recipient?  **Bill’s car.**  Still parked the wrong way on the one-way street.  **Half on the sidewalk.**

**YOUNG OFFICER (muttering to himself)**  
Wrong-way street, partially obstructing pedestrian access, no permit, expired meter, what the hell is this guy even thinking…

Madeline stumbles to her feet, holding Avril upright with all she’s got.

**MADELINE (gasping)**  
We need EMS! She’s not conscious, she’s not talking, she’s—*Get someone now\!*

**OLDER OFFICER (radioing in)**  
We got ‘em. Medics are a block away.

Bill hauls himself up through the hatch last, panting like a bull, knees buckling, covered in blood and tunnel grime. He sees the ticket.

**BILL (wheezing)**  
You’re *fucking ticketing me?*

**YOUNG OFFICER (calmly, still writing)**  
You’re parked the wrong way on a one-way street, sir.

**BILL (exploding)**  
I just carried a half-dead girl up three stories of rat-infested hell while your *goddamn GPS* told us to go to a building that doesn’t even EXIST anymore!

**YOUNG OFFICER (deadpan)**  
Yeah. Still a violation.

**BILL (to Madeline, incredulous)**  
I save a life, I get a $415 ticket.

**MADELINE (dry, exhausted)**  
Welcome to Manhattan.

---

## **SCENE CONTINUED: “New York, New York” – Street-Level Fallout**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – EARLY MORNING**

The city is starting to wake.

A siren howls two blocks away. A street sweeper passes, oblivious. Pigeons circle. Light filters through scaffolding and hangs over the group like judgment. Avril is in Madeline’s lap, still unresponsive. Her eyes flutter now and then, but she doesn’t speak. She doesn’t know she’s been saved yet. Bill stands ten feet away, back against his illegally parked, heavily ticketed car. His shirt is soaked with grime, blood, and sweat. His hands tremble as he scrolls his contacts.

**CREMEANS — no answer**  
**JEFF — straight to voicemail**  
**SARAH — rings three times, then cuts out**

He lowers the phone slowly. Nothing. Just the wind. The honk of a distant cab. He looks up at the buildings — those endless towers of glass and steel and cold apathy — and lets out a long, slow breath. Then, softly, to no one but himself, like a man at the end of a bar:

**BILL (singing under his breath)**  
*Start spreadin’ the news…*  
*I’m leavin’ today…*  
*I want to be a part of it…*

He glances down at the parking ticket in his hand.

**BILL (continuing)**  
*New York… New York…*

His voice cracks. Not from emotion. Just exhaustion.

**BILL (muttering)**  
Goddamn city.

He tries Sarah again. Voicemail. He sighs.

**BILL (almost laughing, almost crying)**  
Come on, sweetheart. We’re out. We did it.

---

# **“Misread” – NYPD Reassessment**

---

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – DAWN**

The medics haven’t arrived yet.

The light has changed — *brighter now*, less cinematic, more cruel. It exposes everything. The grime. The blood. The bruises. The **stench**.

Avril lies still. Madeline keeps stroking her hair, whispering nothing-words — comfort with no belief behind them.

Bill stands nearby, still trying to call Sarah, the **ticket crumpled** in his fist.

Then—

**The OLDER COP** steps forward.

Veteran. Gut instincts. A man who’s **seen shit**. And now he’s seeing **something else**.

He steps in closer. Sees Avril’s torn clothing. Her bare thighs. The discoloration around her mouth. The dried fluid on her legs. **The smell.**

He freezes.

**OLDER COP (low, to himself)**  
Jesus Christ…

He glances at Madeline. Then at Bill.

**OLDER COP (voice harder now)**  
Sir. Ma’am.  Step over here, please.

**BILL (defensive, tired)**  
We just pulled her out of a goddamn hole in the ground. She’s not dead. She’s not even—

**OLDER COP (interrupting)**  
I know a sex crime when I see one.

**MADELINE (wide-eyed)**  
What? No—no no no, we *found* her. We *rescued* her!

**OLDER COP**  
I’m not saying anything yet.  But I’m saying this: you’re both coming with me. Now.

Bill looks like he might explode.

**BILL (teeth gritted)**  
You think *I* did this to her?

**OLDER COP (calm but firm)**  
I think we have a girl here in critical condition, showing signs of assault, brought out of an unofficial underground structure by two people with no immediate authority.

**MADELINE (on the verge of breaking)**  
You have no idea what we just—

**OLDER COP (interrupting again, colder)**  
*Back of the car.* Now.

Madeline stares. Her hands shaking.

Bill doesn’t move.

And then—

**Avril groans.**  **The first sound she’s made.**

Everyone freezes.  She shifts. Barely. Her hand curls weakly.  Her mouth opens.  She whispers something no one can hear.  But she’s *alive.*

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Protocol” – NYPD Escalation**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – EARLY MORNING**

The **older cop steps back**, hand already on his radio mic. His jaw is tight. His eyes hard. This isn’t about heroism now — this is about **procedure**.

**OLDER COP (into radio)**  
Dispatch, 10-33, requesting immediate detective supervisor on scene.  Female, unconscious, signs of physical and possible sexual trauma.  Requesting SVU notification and medical response, code 2.

He lets go of the mic. It *clicks*.

Madeline looks like she’s just been slapped. Bill runs a hand through his hair, seething.

**MADELINE (quiet)**  
You’re calling SVU?

**OLDER COP (not unkind, but unmoved)**  
She smells like a crime scene.  She’s half-naked, bleeding, possibly drugged. You brought her up from underground.  I don’t get to make assumptions.  I get to follow orders.

Bill nearly says something. But stops. Because in this moment, there’s **nothing to say.**

**AVRIL (barely audible)**  
…hurts…

They all turn.

Her eyes flicker open. Not focus. Not clarity. But *life*.

**AVRIL (faint, broken)**  
…rat…

Madeline lunges to her side.

**MADELINE (gently)**  
It’s okay. You’re safe. You’re *out.*

But the cop has already stepped away. He’s talking into his shoulder mic again.

Behind them, sirens start to grow.

**The city is responding.**

But not like a savior.

Like a system.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “No Room for Debate” – NYPD Lockdown**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – EARLY MORNING**

The air has shifted again. The sirens are closer. A second cruiser pulls up at the curb. The old cop — **Detective Staten Island, born and bred** — steps toward Bill with *that* look.

**OLDER COP (thick New York accent, Staten Island written all over it)**  
Get in the *fuckin’* car.

**BILL (exhausted, furious)**  
You’ve got to be kidding me.

**OLDER COP (closer, eyes narrow)**  
You want me to read you your fuckin’ rights right now?  
*Because I got the tone for it.*

Bill opens his mouth—

**OLDER COP (sharper, now in his face)**  
Get in the fuckin’ car, *chief*.  
Right fuckin’ now.

Bill stares at him.

Silent. Tight-lipped.

He looks back at Avril — limp in Madeline’s arms, barely holding consciousness.

Then without a word, **he gets in the back of the squad car**.

Madeline follows. The door slams behind her.

From the sidewalk, the cop mutters to himself, already scribbling in a notepad:

**OLDER COP (grumbling)**  
Every fuckin’ time it’s downtown.  
Shoulda transferred to traffic detail.

---

### **SCENE: “The Other Kind of Hunger” – The Media Arrives**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – MINUTES LATER**

The sun has started to rise.

The first **news van** screeches around the corner like a shark catching the scent. **Then another.**

**Microphones. Boom arms. Telephoto lenses.**

**LIVE 5**  
**ACTION 7 NEWS**  
**WNYC-3**

The scanners were alive tonight — and **this one sounded juicy**.

*Unconscious woman.*  
*Suspected sex assault.*  
*Rock star.*  
*Ghost station.*  
*Midtown location.*  
*NYPD and SVU en route.*

The perfect storm.

Reporters hit the sidewalk **before the EMTs**.

**CAMERAMAN (already filming)**  
We’re live in five, four…

**FIELD REPORTER (adjusting hair, pulling on blazer)**  
We’re standing at the edge of a developing scene in Lower Manhattan where sources say a woman — possibly celebrity rocker Avril Lavigne — has been found in critical condition after emerging from a suspected underground sex dungeon…

**OFFSCREEN PHOTOG**  
Get a shot of the stretcher! Zoom in!

Bill sees them through the squad car window, jaw tight, fists clenched.

Madeline watches the lights bloom across the sidewalk like disease.

**MADELINE (soft, numb)**  
Like rats.

**BILL (quiet, bitter)**  
No.

**BILL (correcting himself)**  
They’re *worse.*

---

### **SCENE: “Oh. Damn.” – Island Records Headquarters**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

The TV is on.

**LIVE 5 NEWS** blares across the screen — a breaking feed already in progress.

**CHYRON:**  
**BREAKING: POSSIBLE SEXUAL ASSAULT VICTIM FOUND IN ABANDONED SUBWAY**

**IMAGE:**

* A stretcher.
* A limp woman’s body.
* Blood on her legs.
* Flashbulbs going off like a firing squad.
* NYPD swarming.
* Madeline waving her arms, screaming at cameras.
* Bill in the back of a squad car, staring straight ahead.

**Jeremy** stands frozen, eyes locked to the screen. His coffee untouched, his phone buzzing in his hand.

He doesn’t blink.

**CREMEANS** pushes through the conference room door.

Still in his hoodie. Eyes bloodshot. Hands full of printouts.  He looks up to the screen.  Stops.  Stares.  And then, without thinking — without drama — just the stunned weight of the moment:

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
Oh.  

*Damn.*

Jeremy doesn’t look at him. Just mutters:

**JEREMY**  
That’s her.  That’s *really* her.

The news feed zooms in on Avril’s face — pale, bloodied, oxygen mask pressed down. The reporter says something about possible overdose, “underground sex club,” “rock star with a troubled history.”

**CREMEANS (still staring)**  
She looks…Jesus.

No one moves.  Just the screen.  Just the noise.  Just the beginning of the storm.

---

## **SCENE: “Signal” – The Surface Collapse**

**EXT. LOWER MANHATTAN – STREET LEVEL – EARLY MORNING**

**Sarah** bursts out of a service access tunnel, covered in sweat, grime, rage.  **Jeff** follows close behind, equally exhausted, breathing hard, fists clenched like he’s ready to punch the fucking city.

They’re filthy. Spent. Empty.  The sun is already up — **too high.**

Sarah straightens, sways slightly, then pulls her phone from her back pocket.

**One bar. Then two.**  **Then: it detonates.**

*134 unread text messages.*  
*62 missed calls.*  
*18 voicemails.*  
*Social notifications climbing so fast they look like malware.*

Her fingers hover over the screen like it's a bomb.

**JEFF (checking his own)**  
Jesus Christ—It’s going off like fucking *microwave popcorn*.

His phone buzzes again. Then again. Then *again*.

**SARAH (staring at the screen)**  
She’s been found.

She doesn't sound relieved.  She sounds **furious**.

**JEFF (reading headlines aloud)**  
“Rock Star Found in Sex Tunnel.”  
“Is This the End of Avril Lavigne?”  
“Exclusive: Subway Assault Shocker—”

**SARAH (flat, jaw tight)**  
And we missed it.  We missed *all* of it.

She grabs Jeff’s arm, squeezes it once — not for comfort, but to ground herself.

**SARAH (soft, dangerous)**  
Run.

---

# **“White-Shoe Panic” – Island Records War Room**

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – BACK OFFICE – EARLY MORNING**

Cremeans is still at his desk, screens full of open tabs, live feeds, law blogs, Reddit chaos. Avril’s name is **trending #1** globally.

He’s on the phone. Voice clipped. Fast.

**CREMEANS (into phone)**  
Dave. It’s Cremeans. Listen to me—

**INT. SPLIT SCREEN – SUBURBAN HOME OFFICE – OHIO – SAME**

**DAVID KENNEDY**, in flannel pajama pants and a Springsteen T-shirt, is sitting at a kitchen table surrounded by cold coffee and legal pads. The Midwest sun is coming through the blinds. He looks hungover. Or stunned. Or both.

**KENNEDY (bleary)**  
Yeah, I saw the news, I’m pulling notes—look, it’s bad, but maybe we can spin it—

**CREMEANS (cutting in, harsh)**  
I don’t need spin.

**KENNEDY (pauses)**  
…what?

**CREMEANS**  
I need a criminal defense lawyer.  In New York. White-shoe.  Someone with teeth. With *connections*.

**KENNEDY**  
Cremeans, I do IP law. I write cease-and-desists. I don’t do—Jesus, are they bringing charges?

**CREMEANS**  
Not yet.  But the cops have Bill.  Madeline’s with him.  SVU’s on scene. Reporters are calling it a rape case already.

**KENNEDY**  
Fuck.

**CREMEANS**  
Yeah.  So stop panicking and give me a name.  I needed it **ten minutes ago.**

**KENNEDY (rubbing his eyes)**  
Okay. Okay. I know a guy. Real white-shoe prick. Charges $900 an hour just to *think*. I’ll send you his number.

**CREMEANS**  
Good.  Make sure he answers the fucking phone.

He hangs up before Kennedy can say another word.

---

### **SCENE: “Monkey Circus” – NYPD Lockdown**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – TEN MINUTES LATER**

Bill and Madeline sit in the back of the squad car, hands on thighs, **trapped but not cuffed** — not yet.

Outside, the scene is devolving into **madness**.

**Cops everywhere.**  Not just uniforms. **Detectives. SVU. Tactical Response.** Marked units. Unmarked sedans. A **forensics van.**  **One drone buzzes overhead**, hovering like a vulture with a badge.

**Yellow tape snakes around the intersection** like caution around a landmine.

Bill stares out the window, watching a captain try to argue with a parking enforcer while **another cop sets up a tripod with a laser scanner**.

**BILL (mutters)**  
Jesus Christ.

**MADELINE (quiet)**  
What?

**BILL (deadpan)**  
It’s a monkey circus.  And we’re in the fuckin’ main tent.

**MADELINE**  
There must be thirty cops here now.

**BILL**  
That’s thirty more than when we found her.

Two more **news vans** roll up. One tries to park on the sidewalk. A field reporter argues with a detective.

**A medic vomits in a corner** after seeing something on a tablet.

**A cop drone flies a lazy arc**, capturing overhead footage. Probably syncing live to a server where lawyers, feds, and press vultures are already watching.

Madeline leans her head back against the seat, eyes rimmed red.

**MADELINE (softly)**  
They’re going to make this something it’s not.

**BILL (bitter)**  
No.  They already did.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Story” – Back of the Squad Car**

**INT. NYPD CRUISER – BACK SEAT – DAWN**

The windows are fogged up from body heat and tension. Outside, **cops and press swarm like insects**, the yellow tape drawing a hard, unforgiving line between **what happened** and **what the world will say happened**.

Inside, Madeline is still. Face pale. Breathing steady, but her hands are trembling.

She leans toward Bill — **very close. Very quiet.** Like a confession. Like a warning.

**MADELINE (whispering)**  
I didn’t know about that place.

Beat.

**MADELINE (lower still)**  
That’s the story, Bill.  *I didn’t know.*

Bill stares ahead. Doesn’t say a word.

**MADELINE**  
You understand? I just pulled some map from an urban archaeology site. It was old.  It pinged the GPS.  That’s all.

Her eyes are locked on him now.

**MADELINE (gentle, urgent)**  
Please.  That’s the story.  We just followed a hunch. We didn't know what we were walking into.

Bill finally looks at her.  Hard.  Tired.  And underneath it — loyal.

**BILL (quiet, low)**  
So that’s how it’s gonna stick?

**MADELINE (nods)**  
Yeah. It has to.

**BILL (beat)**  
Then it sticks.

---

## **SCENE CONTINUED: “Reckoning” – Back of the Squad Car**

**INT. NYPD CRUISER – BACK SEAT – MOMENTS LATER**

The lie hangs in the air like smoke.

Bill hasn’t looked at her again. He’s chewing on the moment, jaw twitching like he’s holding something in.

Then, without turning his head:

**BILL (low, flat)**  
Madeline…

Beat.

**BILL (dry as dust)**  
Are you doin’ poppers and shit?

She blinks.

Hard.

Not offended. Not even surprised.

Just… quiet.

**MADELINE (soft)**  
I used to.  A long time ago.

**BILL**  
Jesus.

**MADELINE (shrugs, eyes down)**  
That place?  It’s not just a map.  It’s a memory.

Silence again. Just the circus outside. The hum of the drone above.

**BILL (softer, not unkind)**  
You’re too young to sound that old.

**MADELINE (half-smiling)**  
So are you.

---

# **“Split” – The Interrogation Begins**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – DAWN**

The circus is still alive — lights, cameras, tape snapping in the wind — but the noise softens as **two plainclothes detectives** step out of an unmarked sedan.

Both in tailored coats. Clean shoes. The **SVU look**: restrained, unreadable, sharp.

They speak with **authority**, not volume.

**DETECTIVE #1 (female, 40s, hard eyes)**  
Let’s split ‘em.

**DETECTIVE #2 (male, 30s, controlled)**  
Left and right.

---

### **EXT. SQUAD CAR – CONTINUOUS**

One officer opens the rear door.

**DETECTIVE #1 (to Bill)**  
Sir, step out, please.

Bill hesitates — just for a second — then complies. His knees pop as he stands.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
This way.

She gestures to the left.  Simultaneously, the second detective opens the opposite door.

**DETECTIVE #2 (to Madeline)**  
Ma’am, if you could step out too.

Madeline climbs out slowly, her legs stiff, jaw tight. She glances at Bill — just a flicker.

**They’re separated.**

Two detectives.  Two directions.  Two stories.

---

### **EXT. SIDEWALK – TWO LOCATIONS, SIMULTANEOUS**

**DETECTIVE #1 (to Bill, flipping open notebook)**  
Let’s keep it simple.  Your name?

**BILL**  
Bill Davenport.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Contact number?

**BILL**  
You got a pen?

She raises an eyebrow. He rattles it off.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Okay.  Now tell me what you’ve been doing for the last twelve hours.

---

**DETECTIVE #2 (to Madeline, calm but firm)**  
Full name?

**MADELINE**  
Madeline Yi.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Phone number?

She gives it.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
And where were you, and what were you doing for the last twelve hours?

Madeline stares at him.  She doesn’t merely lie. She lies like a sleeping brontosaur, all over the place.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Recognition” – Bill’s Side**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – WEST SIDE OF THE TAPE – EARLY MORNING**

Bill stands with **Detective #1**, arms crossed, brow wet with grime. She’s jotting notes without looking up.

Then, just casually — like it’s nothing.

**DETECTIVE #1 (light, conversational)**  
Haven’t I seen you somewhere before, Mr. Davenport?

Bill doesn’t flinch.  Not exactly.

But something behind his eyes **tightens.**

**BILL (flat)**  
Maybe.

**DETECTIVE #1 (grins slightly)**  
Yeah.  Maybe you were at that venue fire on 9th?  Or the thing at the pier with the vintage car club and the—what was it—meth lab?

Bill doesn’t answer. He doesn’t have to.

**DETECTIVE #1 (still writing)**  
You’ve got the face of a guy who walks into bad scenes with good intentions.  
And walks out… sometimes.

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #1 (without looking up)**  
You want to get ahead of this, Mr. Davenport, now would be the time.

Bill exhales. Slow. Measured.

**BILL (quietly)**  
I walked into hell to pull her out.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Yeah?  Then make sure your story doesn’t burn you on the way back up.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Pressure Point” – Bill’s Interrogation**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – WEST PERIMETER – DAWN**

The city hums in the background. Flashbulbs pop behind the tape. Another unmarked car pulls up. The monkey circus grows.

**Detective #1** flips her notebook shut with one hand, pulls out her phone with the other.

She glances at Bill, not unkind — just clinical.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Alright, Mr. Davenport.  With what I’ve got so far, I’m gonna go ahead and pull your record.  Just to see who I’m talking to.

She taps the screen.

**DETECTIVE #1 (casual)**  
You just sit here and chill for a second.

She smiles.  Not warm.

**DETECTIVE #1 (without breaking eye contact)**  
This won’t hurt.  *Unless it needs to.*

Bill doesn’t move. Doesn’t blink.

**BILL (quiet)**  
Just make sure you get the whole record.  The shit they don’t put in the system.

**DETECTIVE #1 (tapping the search)**  
That’s what I’m counting on.

She walks a few steps away. Her back turns.

But Bill knows the drill.

**They’re digging.**

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Two Million Hits” – Discovery**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – NYPD PERIMETER – DAWN**

**Detective #1** stands a few paces from Bill, thumbing through his record on her department app. Her brow furrows slightly.

**DETECTIVE #1 (muttering)**  
Fourteen arrests?

She taps the screen. Scrolls. Skims the entries.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Marijuana. Mushrooms. Oregon.  Goddamn hippie file.

She exhales, unimpressed. Most of it’s garbage. Old charges. Reduced or dropped. Probation. Diversion programs. Still — messy.

Out of habit, she types his name into **Google**.

*William Davenport.*

**1,960,000 results.**

She blinks.

**DETECTIVE #1 (softly)**  
…what the actual fuck?

She taps “Images.”

The first picture: **a stage. A stadium. A man with a synth, sweat-soaked, arms raised.** Spotlights.  **The same face.**  

She freezes. Scrolls.  Photo after photo.

*“The Soul of Commuted Speaks on Tour Burnout.”*  
*“William Davenport Joins War Relief Fundraiser.”*  
*“Bill Davenport’s Last Protest Show Draws 7500 in Portland.”*

**DETECTIVE #1 (dead quiet)**  
Oh…*Damn.*

She looks up. Slowly. Eyes dart back toward the squad car, where **Bill sits calmly**, arms crossed, just watching.  And now her brain starts connecting the pieces.

**This isn't just a grim sex crime in a tunnel.**  **It's a superstar.**  **Carrying another superstar.**  **Out of a scene that looks like a fuckin’ snuff film.**

**DETECTIVE #1 (to herself)**  
This case has gone to hell.

She glances at the cluster of reporters now **pressing against the police tape** with microphones and cameras.

**DETECTIVE #1 (barely above a whisper)**  
This case has *absolutely* gone to hell.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “You Have the Right” – The Line Is Crossed**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – PERIMETER ZONE – MINUTES LATER**

The drone still hums overhead.  The cameras are closing in. The yellow tape is stretching tighter.

**Detective #1** strides back toward the squad car, face hard now. No smile. No pretense.  She’s holding a notepad in one hand — and something heavier in her posture.

She stops in front of Bill.

**BILL (calm)**  
That was quick.

**DETECTIVE #1 (even)**  
Mr. William D. Davenport?

**BILL**  
Yeah?

**DETECTIVE #1 (formally, clearly)**  
I’m advising you that you are not under arrest at this time, but I am obligated to inform you of your rights as part of a custodial interview.

She pulls a laminated card from her jacket. **Starts reading.**

**DETECTIVE #1 (loud, clear)**  
You have the right to remain silent.  Anything you say can and will be held against you in a court of law.  You have the right to an attorney.  If you cannot afford one, one will be provided for you.

She lowers the card. Looks him in the eyes.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Do you understand these rights as I’ve read them to you?

**BILL (low, steady)**  
Yeah. I understand.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Good.

She closes the notebook.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Because you’ve just become very interesting, Mr. Davenport.  And I don’t like mysteries when they bleed.

---

### **“You Don’t Look Very Chinese” – Madeline’s Turn**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – OPPOSITE SIDE OF THE PERIMETER – SAME TIME**

**Detective #2** stands with Madeline. His tone is smooth. Civil. Like he’s **reading a menu** serving class warfare with au jus while watching her eyes.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Miss, can I see your driver’s license, please?

Madeline pulls it from her wallet with slightly trembling fingers.  She hands it over.  He holds it under the streetlamp.

**DETECTIVE #2 (reading it aloud)**  
Madeline… *Quinlan.*

He glances at her.  Then at the picture.  Then at her again.  Then the picture.
Then her.  And smiles.  But there’s **nothing warm about it**.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
You don’t look very Chinese, Miss Quinlan.

Madeline stares at him.  Her face goes still.

**DETECTIVE #2 (pleasant, too pleasant)**  
I think it’s time we made this formal.  He slips the license into his pocket, and from his coat draws a small, folded card — laminated.

**DETECTIVE #2 (reading evenly)**  
You have the right to remain silent.  Anything you say can and will be held against you in a court of law.  You have the right to an attorney.  If you cannot afford one, one will be provided for you.

He looks back up at her.

**DETECTIVE #2 (smiling faintly)**  
Because you *do* have rights in these circumstances.

Madeline says nothing.  Her face is calm.  But inside?  **Her fairy tale story is collapsing.**

---

# **“The Exit” – Avril Leaves the Scene**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – PERIMETER CHAOS – EARLY MORNING**

The flash of red and white lights cuts through the fog.

**The ambulance is loaded.**Two EMTs — stone-faced, methodical — lift the stretcher into the back of the rig. **Avril lies motionless**, oxygen mask in place, strapped in, her face a pale canvas of bruises and exhaustion.

No cameras are allowed within ten feet — but they still try.  One **lenses over the yellow tape**.  Another **climbs the hood of a squad car**.

The **back doors close.**

**AVRIL (V.O.) — distant, blurred, barely conscious**  
*Moving again.*  
*Cold.*  
*But moving.*  
*Are the rats gone?*  
*…Did I dream the girl with the flashlight?*

The engine revs.

The siren starts — not urgent, not screaming. **Just steady.** Winding into the distance.  And **Avril is gone**.  Not rescued.  Not saved.  Just… *removed from the scene.*

---

### **SCENE: “Transport” – En Route**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – EARLY MORNING**

The back doors of the **ambulance** shut with a solid, metallic *clunk.*

Inside, **Avril** is strapped to the gurney. IV in one arm. Oxygen mask over her face. Her eyelids flutter. She doesn’t speak.

The medic checks her pulse.

**EMT #1 (to driver)**  
Bellevue. Closest ER cleared for intake.

**DRIVER (over intercom)**  
Copy. ETA nine minutes.

The siren kicks on — a **steady, mournful wail** — and the ambulance pulls away from the curb.  Behind it, the chaos continues: cops, cameras, tape, lights, noise.  But **Avril is gone from it.**

Now it’s just her and the medics.  A pulse.  A city that almost killed her.  And a hospital that doesn’t know who’s coming yet.

---

### **SCENE: “Why the Kid?” – Departure**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – SUN’S UP NOW**

The **chaos hasn’t slowed** — it’s just gotten **colder**. More calculated. The tape is firmer, the officers quieter, the questions sharper.  A marked patrol car pulls up to the edge of the scene.

**Detective #2** stands beside Madeline, gently guiding her toward it.

**MADELINE**  
Am I under arrest?

**DETECTIVE #2 (not answering)**  
We just need to clear a few things up. Ride’ll be more comfortable at the precinct.

She looks back toward the crowd.  Toward **Bill**.

Across the scene, he sees them.

**BILL (half to himself)**  
Wait, what—?

The door opens. She’s ushered in.  No cuffs.  Just procedure.

But **Bill knows what that means.**

**BILL (to the closest officer, sharp)**  
Why the hell are they taking the kid?

**YOUNG OFFICER (shrugs)**  
Standard follow-up. She’s a primary witness.

**BILL**  
She’s a goddamn *hero*.

The patrol car door closes.  The engine hums.

**Madeline doesn’t look back.**  She’s trying to remember the lie.  And whether it will hold.  **Bill watches her disappear into the traffic.**  **And for the first time since they pulled Avril out of the dark, he feels truly alone.**

---

### **SCENE: “Go Faster” – Sarah in Transit**

**INT. YELLOW CAB – EARLY MORNING – LOWER MANHATTAN**

**Sarah** sits in the back of the cab like a bomb with a pulse. Her phone is out, screen blinding in the morning light. She’s got the **WABC stream pulled up**, the reporter’s voice too chipper for the hell they’re covering.

*“—as you can see behind me, an unidentified woman has just been taken from the scene in a marked NYPD vehicle, while another man—possibly musician William Davenport—remains on-site. We’re hearing the injured party may have already been transported—”*

The camera cuts to **Madeline** — hair a mess, eyes hollow — being loaded into the back of a squad car.

Sarah’s hand **clenches so tight the phone creaks.**

**SARAH (hissing)**  
No, no, no, no, no…

Beside her, **Jeff** watches his own screen. He flinches as the image of the ambulance pulling away fills the frame.

**JEFF (quietly)**  
That’s it. That’s her.

**SARAH (exploding)**  
That’s three goddamn balls in the air and I’m stuck in the back of a fuckin’ cab with you and this guy’s driving like it’s his retirement lap!

**CAB DRIVER (startled)**  
I’m doin’ the speed limit!

**SARAH (deadly calm)**  
Then break the fuckin’ law.  *That’s Avril Lavigne in an ambulance and my assistant in the back of a squad car and the entire label on the verge of a corporate coronary.*  So punch it. Now.

The cab swerves. Horns blare.

**JEFF (half-under his breath)**  
She’s gonna kill us before the press does.

**SARAH (without looking at him)**  
At least then I’d have something I can control.

---

# **“Nine Hundred an Hour” – The Call That Does Not Matter**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CREMEANS’ OFFICE – EARLY MORNING**

The room glows cold from his monitor bank. **Cremeans** paces, phone pressed tight to his ear.

Finally — a *click*.

**LAWYER (V.O.) (smooth, detached)**  
Chase, Matheson, and Doyle. Elijah speaking.

**CREMEANS**  
I need a criminal defense attorney.  Manhattan-based. White-shoe.  You come highly recommended.

**LAWYER (V.O.)**  
That’s always good to hear. What’s the situation?

**CREMEANS**  
We’ve got a high-profile sexual assault investigation, full media burn.  The victim is *Avril Lavigne*.  Two civilians pulled her out of the scene — they’re being treated like suspects.  Names are William Davenport and Madeline **Quinlan**.

Beat.

**CREMEANS (firm, fast)**  
I need someone in that precinct **now**.

**LAWYER (V.O.)**  
Our rate is nine hundred an hour.

**CREMEANS**  
Double it if you’re there in thirty minutes.

Silence. The lawyer recalibrates.

**LAWYER (V.O.)**  
Text me the precinct. I’m already dressed.

**CREMEANS**  
I just did.

He hangs up.  Stares at the phone. Doesn’t breathe.

**CREMEANS (to no one)**  
Buy the silence.  Then buy the truth.

---

### **SCENE: “Nothing Happens” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

The massive flat-screen TV dominates the room, tuned to a 24/7 news stream. No sound. Just the image:

*Crime scene tape.*  *A dozen cops standing around.*  *A squad car pulling away.*  *Reporters waiting like vultures with microphones.*

**Jeremy** sits at the edge of the long table, slouched forward, both elbows planted, eyes deadlocked on the screen.  **Cremeans** stands behind him, arms crossed, a hollow stillness in his chest that feels like grief… or vertigo.

They watch.  *And nothing happens.*  They keep watching.  *Still nothing happens.*  They wait.  *Still nothing—*

**JEREMY (soft, bitter)**  
This is gonna get so old so fast.

Cremeans doesn’t answer. Just nods once. Tight. Mechanical.

**JEREMY**  
The pace of this…It’s like the world’s sprinting and our souls are still tying their shoes.

**CREMEANS (low)**  
And the feed never blinks.

*The camera pans over the squad car that took Madeline. Again.*  *The overhead drone shot circles. Again.*  *The medic wipes their brow. Again.*

Every second feels like five.

**JEREMY (quiet)**  
They’re making this a funeral before we even get to the hospital.

**CREMEANS**  
They’re building the narrative.  And they don’t even need facts anymore. Just frames.

*Back to the crime scene tape. Same slow zoom. Nothing new. Just pressure.*

**JEREMY (sits back, voice hollow)**  
We’re not managing this.

**CREMEANS**  
We’re watching it manage us.

---

### **SCENE: “It’s Everywhere” – Media Meltdown**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – MINUTES LATER**

The TV keeps looping footage. Jeremy hasn’t moved.  **Cremeans** shifts to his laptop, eyes scanning screens like a man trying to dam a flood with duct tape.

He opens **Instagram**.

*Band account: 1.3 million followers.*  
*Notifications climbing by the thousands per second.*  
*Every post swarmed with comments: “is she alive???” “what happened???” “this is fake, right?”*

He flips to **X (Twitter)**.

**CREMEANS (muttering)**  
Trending in 34 countries…

He clicks the analytics tab. Languages: English. Spanish. Portuguese. Japanese. French. Farsi. Ukrainian.

*\#Avril*  
*\#UndergroundScene*  
*\#SubwayScandal*  
*\#WhatHappenedToAvril*

He pulls open a global media aggregation dashboard.

**CREMEANS (voice flat now)**  
MSNBC. NBC.com. ABC News.  The *New York Times*.  The *Post*.  *Barstool.*  
*E! Fucking Online.* He clicks through.

Same image.  Different headlines.

*“Subway Tragedy Tied to Rock Icon”*  
*“Avril Lavigne Found in Underground Hellscape”*  
*“Superstar or Victim? Industry Shaken by Early Morning Discovery”*

He hesitates.  Then opens **TorontoStar.ca**.

**Page one.**  Her face.  Half-lit. Oxygen mask.  

Caption: *"Lavigne: Canada’s Fallen Daughter?"*

Cremeans leans back. One hand over his mouth.

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
Okay.  Okay, yeah.

He closes the laptop.

**CREMEANS (to no one)**  
We’ve already lost the narrative.

---

### **SCENE: “Are You Okay, Buddy?” – The Breaking Point**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

Jeremy hasn’t moved from his chair, still watching the endless stream of cable news and online headlines. Cremeans stands at the window, hands on the sill, **back turned** to the screen like it’s physically burning him.

**CREMEANS (quiet, bitter)**  
Our spin doctor’s in the back of a squad car.  *She’s so fucking busted.*

**JEREMY (dry, not even looking up)**  
That’s the second time you’ve used profanity in the past ten minutes.  
You okay, buddy?

Cremeans doesn’t answer.

Jeremy reaches into the mini fridge under the table and pulls out a can of **Mountain Dew** — the emergency fuel, the gamer serum, the sacred tonic of long nights and impossible crises.

**JEREMY (offering it)**  
You want one?  You’re twitchin’ like a Blade Runner extra.

Cremeans turns, finally. His face is tight, his eyes rimmed red — *not from sleep deprivation. From holding everything in for too long.*

**CREMEANS (flat)**  
This is about as bad as it was when my dad died.

Jeremy freezes.  That gets through.

**CREMEANS (lower)**  
I haven’t slept in forty hours.  Avril started spiraling last week, and it’s been one red alert after another.  Madeline was the only one who could talk her down.  Now she’s in holding, Bill’s probably next, and Avril’s in the ER with rat bites and semen on her leg.

He doesn’t cry.  But he might, if one more domino falls.

**CREMEANS (hollow)**  
I think I just…hit the edge.

Jeremy puts the Mountain Dew on the table.  Doesn’t say anything for a second.

Then, quietly:

**JEREMY (soft, real)**  
We’ll pull her back.  All of them.  Even if we gotta break the fuckin’ world to do it.

---

### **SCENE: “That’s Our Band Member” – Stonewall**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – POLICE LINE – MORNING SUN HARD AND UGLY**

**Sarah** and **Jeff** push through the crowd of cameras and reporters, sleeves rolled up, eyes locked on the yellow tape and the **thick blue wall of uniforms** just behind it.

They reach the front.

**SARAH (to the first uniformed cop she sees)**  
We need to speak to William Davenport. Now.

The cop doesn’t even blink.

**COP (flat)**  
You need to stay right where you are, ma’am.

**SARAH (gritting her teeth)**  
That’s our band member.

**COP (louder)**  
Don’t care.

**SARAH** takes a single step forward.

**COP (snaps)**  
One more step and I will *break your fuckin’ jaw.*

The tape flutters between them.

Jeff flinches. Sarah **does not move.**

**JEFF (softly, to Sarah)**  
He’s serious.

**SARAH (low, lethal)**  
So am I.

She stares the cop down for three long seconds.  But she knows.  **This is the part where she plays chess, not chicken.**  She backs off half a step. Eyes still locked.

**SARAH (to Jeff, cold and controlled)**  
Get the attorney on the line.  This just became a hostage negotiation.

---

### **SCENE: “Time to Pivot” – Pullback at the Line**

**EXT. CANAL & CENTRE – POLICE PERIMETER – MOMENTS LATER**

Sarah stares at the officer for one last second, her jaw tight enough to crack enamel.  Then her phone buzzes.  She almost ignores it.

But the tone is different. **One she only uses for Cremeans.**  The “if-this-goes-off-shit-is-on-fire” tone.

She flicks it open.

**CREMEANS (TEXT):**  
*I’ve got something. Meet me at HQ. We need to regroup. This isn't a salvage op — it's a war.*

She swears softly under her breath.

**SARAH**  
Fuck.

**JEFF (tense)**  
What is it?

**SARAH**  
Cremeans is building something. A plan.  We’re not getting anything done here.

She turns, already moving back toward the cab.

**JEFF (following)**  
And Bill?

**SARAH (dark)**  
They’re not budging.

**JEFF (mutters)**  
That’s self-evident.

**SARAH (clipped)**  
He’s in the system now.  We don’t get him out with shouting.  We get him out with *strategy.*

She throws open the cab door.

**SARAH (to Jeff)**  
Get in.  We’re not losing this band today.

They slam the doors. The cab peels off.

**Behind them**, the chaos continues.  **Bill** still inside.  **Madeline** already gone.  **Avril**… somewhere between life and legend.

---

# **“Intake” – Bellevue ER**

**INT. BELLEVUE HOSPITAL – EMERGENCY ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

**The double doors burst open.** The **ambulance crew** wheels Avril in — still unconscious, still masked, a sheet over her body, her wrists limp against the rails.

Inside, **a huddle of professionals is already waiting.**  Three **ER nurses**, two **doctors**, and a **crisis intervention counselor**. All of them tired. All of them locked in.  This is not a photo op.

This is **the machinery of trauma care.**

**DR. KAPLAN (quiet, firm)**  
Okay, we’ve got a female patient, approximate age mid-thirties, unconscious on arrival. Signs of physical trauma, probable sexual assault. Let’s stay sharp.

**NURSE ROPER**  
Vitals?

**EMT (pushing gurney)**  
BP’s low. She’s hypothermic. GCS is 9. Not talking. Responds to pain but not verbal cues.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
We’re going to do this by the book. SART protocol.  No stripping the patient. No cutting clothing unless it interferes with life-saving treatment.  Photograph everything. Chain of custody from the jump.

**COUNSELOR (softly)**  
No questions to the patient until she’s stable.  We speak when she speaks. Not before.

**NURSE (nodding)**  
Rape kit?

**DR. KAPLAN**  
Ready. But we wait.  We need consent.  If she can’t give it, we stabilize first.

They guide the gurney down the corridor. One nurse walks beside Avril, watching her face.

**NURSE ROPER (to herself, almost a prayer)**  
C’mon, honey. Stay with us.

The fluorescent lights overhead flicker.  The doors swing open again.  And Avril disappears into the white.

---

### **SCENE: “Evidence and Triage” – Bellevue ER, Intake Room**

**INT. BELLEVUE – FORENSIC EXAM ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

Fluorescent lights buzz faintly above the sterile white space. **Avril lies motionless** on a transfer table. **Two nurses** and **Dr. Kaplan** begin the examination. A **forensic technician** observes from the corner, clipboard in hand.

**NURSE ROPER (gently checking pupils)**  
Pupils nonresponsive.  Fixed. Mid-dilation.

**DR. KAPLAN (notes aloud)**  
Probable narcotic exposure.  Request full tox screen. IV panel, opiates, benzos, amphetamines.

Nurse lifts Avril’s arm. Examines the crook of her elbow.

**NURSE ROPER**  
Track marks.  Fresh puncture site, left arm.  Multiple scars along the median cubital vein. Probable intravenous use.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
Start Narcan, slow drip. Just to rule out.  Stabilize vitals before anything invasive.

**NURSE #2 (pulling small items from blazer pocket)**  
Amphetamine tabs in foil. Protective syringe cover — no needle.

**DR. KAPLAN (to the tech)**  
Label for police. Bag and seal.

**TECH (tagging evidence)**  
Chain of custody initiated: 6:41 AM.

**NURSE ROPER (grimacing as she lifts blouse hem)**  
Her blouse is soaked through. Strong odor — likely semen, multiple deposits.  
Mixed with blood and vaginal discharge. Some matted in fabric fibers.

**DR. KAPLAN (tight, professional)**  
Blouse is now both biological hazard and criminal evidence.  Handle with full gloves. Cut only where needed to preserve fluid patterns.

The nurses exchange a look — just for a moment. Just human.  Then the scissors come out.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
Let’s be gentle.  Even now, it matters.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Check Her Nails” – Evidence Search**

**INT. BELLEVUE – FORENSIC EXAM ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

**Dr. Kaplan** steps back from the table, glancing at Avril’s unconscious form, her breathing shallow, face ghost-pale under harsh light.

He speaks low. Calm. But every word lands.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
Ramos, check her nails.

The room stills for half a second.

**NURSE ROPER** knows **exactly** what that means.  She doesn't nod. Doesn't speak. She just **moves.**  She lifts Avril’s hand carefully, reverently, as though touching a wounded child.  **Her gloves creak.**  She examines the fingertips. The undersides.  One by one.

**ROPER (softly, to the tech)**
