Left hand — clear buildup under index and middle fingernails.  Dry particulate. Some pink, some dark. Could be blood. Could be textile.  
Tag and scrape.

**TECHNICIAN** steps in, snapping open a sterile evidence kit, swabs and scrapers at the ready.

**ROPER (continuing, right hand)**  
Right hand… same. More accumulation. She fought someone.

**DR. KAPLAN (quietly)**  
Let’s make sure it sticks.

**Roper gently lowers the hand back to the table.** It stays curled — like it’s still trying to hold onto something.

---

# **“The Interrogation” – Precinct Room, NYPD**

**INT. INTERROGATION ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

**Madeline** sits alone at a metal table. The walls are dull gray, chipped. The two-way mirror hums with invisible attention. The lighting is too bright and somehow still gloomy.

She crosses her legs slowly. Her **red heels catch the light.** Her blouse is wrinkled from the hours in the tunnel, but still stylish. Her mascara is cracked. Her composure? Barely holding.  She knows she’s being watched.  And then — the door creaks open.

**Two detectives enter.**

**Detective #2** — the younger one — **closes the door gently behind him**, carrying a manila folder like it’s a prop he doesn’t need yet.

**DETECTIVE #2 (smooth, smiling)**  
Wow. You clean up good.

Madeline says nothing.

**DETECTIVE #2 (casual)**  
I mean, seriously — the dress, the cut on that blouse, the heels?  You’ve got style, Miss… Quinlan, right?

**MADELINE (cool, guarded)**  
That's right.

**DETECTIVE #2 (tilts his head)**  
Didn’t think they taught fashion in urban archaeology forums.

A beat. He smiles wider.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
But hey — great taste. Red heels with that kind of stress? That’s commitment.

**Madeline** stares at him.

She knows this game.  She *played* it — on red carpets, on TikTok, in backroom meetings with stylists and execs.

**MADELINE (flat)**  
You going to ask me about my shoes, or the unconscious woman I carried out of a subway?

The detective’s smile doesn’t falter.  But his eyes narrow just a little.

**DETECTIVE #2 (pleasant)**  
We’ll get there.  Let’s just talk first.  You and me. Casual.

He pulls out the chair.  Sits.  Flips open the folder.  **Madeline breathes in slowly.**  And waits.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Save Avril” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**DETECTIVE #2** leans back in his chair, flipping through the file like it’s a dinner menu. He doesn’t look at Madeline when he starts speaking.

**DETECTIVE #2 (soft, almost friendly)**  
Ms. Quinlan… we’ve been watching this unfold just like everyone else. TV. Twitter. Newsfeeds. Reddit. TikTok. Hell, even *my ex-wife* posted about it.

He glances up.

**DETECTIVE #2 (smiling)**  
Hashtag Save Avril, right?

Madeline doesn’t move.  He leans forward now, elbows on the table, fingers laced.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
It’s everywhere.  And it’s awful. What happened to Ms. Lavigne? Tragic. Shocking. Heartbreaking.

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #2 (gently)**  
As I understand it… *you* bought some of those hashtags, didn’t you?

A slow silence settles over the room.

**MADELINE (tight, careful)**  
We were tracking engagement.  Social response. Sentiment analysis. That’s part of my job.

**DETECTIVE #2 (nodding, like it makes sense)**  
Sure. Totally.  You’re the one who manages the image. You shape the narrative. You tell people what to think.

He slides the folder forward.  Pulls out a **printout of an ad buy receipt.** Madeline’s name. Timestamped. *#SaveAvril.*

**DETECTIVE #2**  
You didn’t post it. You paid for it.  Right before she was found.

**MADELINE**  
I didn’t know she’d be—

**DETECTIVE #2 (cutting in, soft but sharp)**  
That’s the thing.  How *did* you know, Ms. Quinlan?

He lets the words hang.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Because it kinda looks like you were ready for the fall…*Before* anyone else knew she’d been pushed.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Go On” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

The fluorescent lights hum. The mirrored glass reflects just enough of her own outline to feel like someone’s sitting behind it.

**Detective #2** clasps his hands neatly on the table, like a priest or a school principal, polite to the edge of cruelty.

**DETECTIVE #2 (calm, composed)**  
So here’s what I’d like, Ms. Quinlan.

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
I’d like you to walk me through the last… oh, let’s call it **twelve hours**.  Where you were. What you were doing. Who you were with.

He gestures loosely, almost indulgently.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Start wherever you’d like — maybe with the Instagram traffic spike, maybe with the GPS ping, maybe when you and Mr. Davenport decided to take your little field trip.

He leans in now, just a bit.

**DETECTIVE #2 (voice tightening)**  
And please… I am *begging you*, with all the respect I can barely muster —  
Tell me what exactly you were doing in **one of the more exclusive, hidden, underground sex dungeons** in New York City.

Beat. The silence is razor-thin.

**DETECTIVE #2 (mock-polite)**  
Go on.

He smiles.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
We’re taking notes.

**Madeline** doesn’t blink.  But her hand on the table tightens ever so slightly.
Because she knew this was coming.  She just didn’t know it would feel like **this.**

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Card Not Played” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**Madeline** straightens her back, her voice finally cutting through the weight of the room.

**MADELINE (clear, calm)**  
I want my attorney.  And I want to know what I’m being charged with.  Because I didn’t do anything wrong.

**Detective #2** exhales like he’s been waiting for this cue.  He sits back, grinning like a man holding aces.

**DETECTIVE #2 (pleasant)**  
Of course. Like any American citizen, you’ve got constitutional rights.  We’ll make sure you get every single one of them — **as fast as humanly possible.**

He taps the file folder on the table.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
The charge?  Well, let’s start easy.

He opens the folder, pulls out the **driver’s license**.

**DETECTIVE #2 (mocking slight confusion)**  
You gave your name as **Madeline Yi** to officers at the scene.

He holds up the license.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
But your legal name is **Madeline Quinlan.**  We’ve got that documented and timestamped.

He closes the folder.

**DETECTIVE #2 (voice sharpening)**  
That’s giving a false identity to a police officer.  That’s a chargeable offense.  Do you know how much **time** people do for lying to cops?

He leans forward, just slightly.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
And that’s without even mentioning being a possible **accessory to rape.**

He smiles cold.

**DETECTIVE #2 (flat)**  
Nope.  *That card hasn’t been played yet.*

A pause.

**DETECTIVE #2 (casual)**  
Now…if you’d like to **revise and extend your bullshit remarks**, you’re welcome to do so.

He taps the table, once.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Otherwise, I’ll get your lawyer on the line right now.

**Madeline’s jaw is set.**  She doesn’t answer.  Not yet.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Truth as a Weapon” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

The room is quiet.  Madeline’s lips part slightly.

**MADELINE (slowly, aloud to herself as much as them)**  
I have the greatest weapon of all…

Her voice is trembling but rising.

**MADELINE**  
The truth.

The younger detective — **Detective #2** — watches her carefully.  Not interrupting. Not rushing. Just…**pressing softly**.  He tilts his head. Glances sideways at the **older detective** behind him, then back to her.

**DETECTIVE #2 (calm, open-palmed)**  
Do you swear to tell the truth… the whole truth… and nothing but the truth?

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
Because I’m all ears.

He leans forward, very slightly.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
But — and this is important, Madeline — *you don’t have to say another thing.*

**DETECTIVE #2 (gentle, serious now)**  
You *have* rights.  And we will honor them.  To the letter.

His voice is low. Intimate. Like a confession booth.

**DETECTIVE #2**  
But if you want to talk, if you really believe that what you’ve got is the truth —  
then go ahead.

A pause.

**The room holds its breath.**  Madeline’s eyes are locked on the mirrored glass.  She knows someone is behind it. Watching.  **Judging.**

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Book Her” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**Madeline** doesn’t move.  She stares straight ahead, jaw clenched, breath shallow.  She **says nothing.**  **Detective #2** watches her a second longer.

Then — *click.*  He presses a button under the table.  The door opens.  A **female officer** enters. Stone-faced. Already pulling on gloves.

**DETECTIVE #2 (without a flicker of emotion)**  
Book her.

**FEMALE OFFICER (calm)**  
Understood.

**DETECTIVE #2 (to the officer, matter-of-fact)**  
False identification to a police officer.  Potential sexual assault accomplice.  Brought out of a suspected drug den with controlled substances on her person.  Oh — and…

He stands slowly. Closes the folder.

**DETECTIVE #2 (dry, sharp)**  
Given the nature of the facility she was recovered from… Let’s go ahead and prep for a **body cavity search**, too.

**Madeline’s asshole puckers. Her face flushes.** Still, she doesn’t speak.

**DETECTIVE #2 (smiling, just enough to be cruel)**  
You’re excused, Ms. Quinlan.

The **female officer** steps toward her.

The door closes behind them.  **Madeline is no longer a witness.**  **She is now property of the system.**

---

# **“Off the Grid” – Island Records, 14th Floor Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – MAIN CONFERENCE ROOM – 14TH FLOOR – MORNING**

The **elevator dings**.

**Sarah and Jeff step out**, both looking like they’ve been *through* something. Their clothes are rumpled, eyes burning, expressions sharp.

Inside the glass-walled conference room, **Jeremy** is already pacing.  
**Cremeans** is seated at the table, laptop open, multiple feeds running — news sites, live X trends, Instagram analytics, legal docs.

The moment Sarah walks in—

**JEREMY (pointing at Jeff)**  
Where the *fuck* were you?

Jeff stops dead.

**JEREMY (snapping)**  
You disappeared for two hours!  Completely off the grid. Nothing. Not a call. Not a text. You went *dark* in the middle of a goddamn manhunt!

**JEFF (calm, pissed)**  
We were following a lead.

**JEREMY**  
Bullshit! You got ghosted. While your friend was being hauled into a squad car and Madeline was getting interrogated like she runs a cult in Alphabet City.

**SARAH (snapping)**  
Enough!

She drops her bag hard on the table.

**SARAH**  
We were on the street, Jeremy. You think we were joyriding through Midtown for bagels?

**JEREMY (still furious, but dropping volume)**  
You weren’t *communicating.*

**CREMEANS (without looking up)**  
No one was. That’s the problem. We had four narratives spinning at once and no central voice.

**JEFF (gritting his teeth)**  
We were *trying to find Avril.* You remember her? Covered in blood? In the ER right now?

**JEREMY**  
While Madeline gets processed like cartel? While Bill's getting read his rights on live TV?

**SARAH (quiet, cold)**  
And what did *you* do while we were in that hell?

**CREMEANS (raising his hand, calm)**  
Guys.

They all stop.  Cremeans slowly turns his laptop toward them.  On screen: a drafted *legal strategy brief*.

**CREMEANS**  
We have a plan.

Beat.

**CREMEANS**  
But it’s gonna cost us everything if we don’t move **now**.

---

# **“No Cover-Ups This Time” – Bellevue ER, Assault Kit Room**

**INT. BELLEVUE – SEXUAL ASSAULT RESPONSE ROOM – LATE MORNING**

The fluorescent lights above are harsh and unblinking. The room smells of antiseptic and **grief**.

**Avril** lies on the table, barely conscious, hooked to an IV drip, eyes fluttering but unfocused. Her blouse and skirt are being **carefully removed** by **Nurse Roper**, piece by piece, **tagged and sealed**, each step logged in chain-of-custody forms by a **forensic tech** standing nearby.

**Dr. Kaplan** is gloved, masked, and solemn. He does not flinch. He does not rush.

**NURSE ROPER (quietly, clinical)**  
Multiple tears, vaginal wall. Fresh.  But… also some scarring.  Previous trauma. Days old, maybe less.

**DR. KAPLAN (nods, voice low)**  
We document everything.  Full exam. Full kit. Swabs, samples, under fingernails. Hair. Toxicology. Photos with consent.

**Roper hesitates.** The woman on the table is **barely there**. And she's famous. **Too famous.**

**ROPER (soft)**  
Do you think she knows who she is right now?

**DR. KAPLAN (without missing a beat)**  
That doesn’t matter.  We know who she is.  We’re obligated — to her. And to **the truth**.

He pauses. Then adds, firm:

**DR. KAPLAN**  
This band already dodged some shady shit twelve years ago.

He glances at the tech. Then at Ramos.

**DR. KAPLAN (steel in his voice)**  
That is **not** what happens today.

The tech nods. Starts photographing every piece of evidence. Click. Click. Click.  The law will have its trail.  Avril exhales softly. Not aware. Not awake. But **alive**.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Incapacitated” – Bellevue ER, SART Room**

The tension in the room sharpens.  **Nurse Roper** finishes logging the evidence bags, but her voice is quiet, strained.

**ROPER (softly, shaken)**  
That woman can’t consent to anything, Doctor.

**Dr. Kaplan** doesn’t look up immediately. He’s placing the last blood vial into its sealed container. Then, he turns — calm, composed, but with **a fire buried deep beneath the surface.**

**DR. KAPLAN (quietly, firmly)**  
You're right.

Beat.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
She can’t speak for herself.  She can’t refuse.  She can’t approve.  Which means *everything we do* has to be defendable in court, in ethics, and in medicine.

He steps closer to the table, glances down at Avril — **motionless, exposed, unconscious.** The silence in the room wraps around her like a second sheet.

**DR. KAPLAN (to the whole room)**  
So we do what’s necessary.  No more. No less.  We document. We stabilize. We protect.  And we prepare—for *every possibility.*

He looks directly at Roper.

**DR. KAPLAN**  
This isn’t just medicine.  It’s **evidence.**  And she deserves better than what brought her here.

---

# **“The Second Round” – NYPD Precinct, Interrogation Room**

**INT. NYPD – INTERROGATION ROOM – LATE MORNING**

The room is bare, gray, and humming with cheap fluorescent light. **Bill Davenport** sits alone at the table, still in the same clothes from the tunnel — dried sweat, city grime, and something worse clinging to him.  The door creaks open.  **Detective #1** steps in, calm and smooth, a cup of coffee in her hand.  She shuts the door behind her and doesn’t sit right away.

**DETECTIVE #1 (friendly tone)**  
How ya doin', Mr. Davenport?

**Bill** doesn’t answer right away. He just watches her — eyes sharp, not defiant, but tired of the game.

**BILL (flat)**  
Been better.

**DETECTIVE #1 (nods, as if sympathetic)**  
Yeah. I’d imagine.

She finally sits across from him, sets the coffee down in front of herself — *not offering him one.*

**DETECTIVE #1**  
You’ve had a hell of a morning.  We all have.  Whole city’s talking. You, Madeline Quinlan, and a girl in the ER that used to be a headliner at the VMAs.

She leans in just slightly.

**DETECTIVE #1 (measured)**  
And we’d like to hear your version of it.  Unless you’d prefer to keep quiet.

A long pause.

**DETECTIVE #1 (still polite)**  
Your call, Mr. Davenport.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Truth According to Bill” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**BILL (leaning forward, voice low and level)**  
Alright. You want the whole thing? Here it is.

He folds his hands on the table. Looks the detective square in the eye.

**BILL**  
We’ve been tracking Avril for the past six days.  Not through some PR campaign, not through handlers. Through **desperation**. Because she’s been on a bender. An *epic* one.

**DETECTIVE #1 (quietly taking notes)**  
Define “bender.”

**BILL**  
Alcohol. Weed. Pills. Coke. God knows what else.  She’s been **having sex all over the city** — strangers, randos, anyone who caught her eye.  She’s been **posting it.** On Instagram. On her alt.  Photos that would *kill a brand in ten seconds flat*.  Photos that made *me* sick, and I’m not exactly innocent.

He pauses.

**BILL (a little darker)**  
Drinking from a bottle of tequila in a bathtub full of beer cans.  Holding a joint the size of my forearm.  Smeared lipstick, no pants, laughing like it’s Mardi Gras and the world doesn’t end.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
And this was… public?

**BILL**  
Public enough.  You ever try getting a spiraling celebrity to give up her phone?  We tried. **Cremeans tried.** Sarah tried. Hell, she told Cremeans to go to hell. *Direct quote.*

**DETECTIVE #1**  
And last night?

Bill exhales. Rubs his eyes.

**BILL**  
She disappeared from a club downtown. Again. We started digging.  Madeline found an old urban archaeology map of a sealed subway tunnel.  She pinged it against some tagged photo metadata.  We took a shot.  We found her in a **subway dungeon**.  Lying in filth.  Covered in—  

(seething)  
—**stuff that doesn’t belong on any human being.**  She wasn’t moving.  The rats were closing in.  We pulled her out. Me and Madeline. No one else.

**BILL (quiet, clear)**  
And now you’re sitting here asking me if I raped her.  Because I carried her.

He stares the detective down.  Not angry.  Just **done**.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Let’s Talk About You” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

The detective flips back a few pages in her folder. She doesn’t raise her voice. She doesn’t accuse. She just **opens the next wound**.

**DETECTIVE #1 (even, pointed)**  
Let’s talk about *your* drug use, Mr. Davenport.

Bill doesn’t flinch.

**DETECTIVE #1 (reading)**  
Fourteen arrests for marijuana possession. One for psilocybin mushrooms.  Thirteen of those cases were either dropped or reduced. Oregon, mostly. That’s your territory?

**BILL (nodding)**  
Yeah. Portland scene. Long time ago.

**DETECTIVE #1 (not letting up)**  
Last recorded bust was six years ago.  But we both know that doesn’t mean clean.  So let me ask directly:

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Are you using?

**BILL (blunt)**  
No.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
When’s the last time you smoked?

**BILL (cool, steady)**  
A month ago. At home. Legally.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
And last night?

**BILL (without hesitation)**  
Stone sober.

She watches him. Long pause. Letting silence do the probing.

**DETECTIVE #1 (softer, but pointed)**  
You’re a recovering scene kid with a long-standing familiarity with narcotics.  You were found pulling an unconscious woman out of a suspected drug den with paraphernalia in her pockets.  That’s a **very specific look**, Mr. Davenport.

**BILL (low, measured)**  
I wasn’t high.  I wasn’t using.  I was saving her life.

Another long pause.  She doesn’t write that part down.  Not yet.

**DETECTIVE #1 (quiet)**  
We’ll run a tox on you anyway.

**BILL (dry)**  
Be my guest.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Needle Goes In” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

The air in the room is heavier now — no more false warmth. The temperature has dropped, but the questions burn hotter.

**DETECTIVE #1 (cool, clinical)**  
Do you ever frequent gay bathhouses, Mr. Davenport?

Bill blinks. Just once.

**BILL (even)**  
No.

**DETECTIVE #1 (still flipping pages)**  
Ever snap poppers?  You familiar with the underground club scene? Backroom spots in Alphabet City?

**BILL (tight)**  
Not in the last decade.

**DETECTIVE #1 (pressing now)**  
You’re the only one in the band who’s not married — or wasn’t married — right?

**BILL (shrugs slightly)**  
I didn’t sign up to be a husband.

**DETECTIVE #1 (leaning in)**  
Which means you’ve had more… *freedom* to play the field, so to speak.  No strings. No alibi.

**BILL (icy)**  
Is that what this is now?

**DETECTIVE #1 (stone cold)**  
It means you don’t have a regular, documented sexual outlet.  So maybe you're improvising.

Beat.

She closes the folder.

**DETECTIVE #1 (direct)**  
Tell me, Mr. Davenport:  When was the last time you slept with **Avril Lavigne?**

The silence that follows is *razor-thin*.  Bill doesn’t break eye contact.

**BILL (low, calm)**  
Never.

**DETECTIVE #1 (watching)**  
Never?

**BILL (dead serious)**  
Not once.  Not drunk.  Not sober.  Not on tour.  Not in a hotel.  Not when she was a star.  Not when she was falling apart.

She watches. Waits. No movement. No tells.

**DETECTIVE #1 (soft, just enough venom)**  
We’ll see what she says when she wakes up.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Two Choices” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**Detective #1** opens a slim manila envelope and slides a sealed **DNA collection swab kit** across the table, slow and deliberate. She doesn’t raise her voice. Doesn’t blink.

**DETECTIVE #1 (measured)**  
With your permission, of course, we’d like to take a DNA sample.

She sits back in her chair.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Now, you do have rights under our Constitution. I’m here to honor those.

She folds her hands.

**DETECTIVE #1 (quiet authority)**  
So here are your options, Mr. Davenport.  Option one: you **consent**, and we swab right now.  You get it done. You get your dignity. You might even get your day moving again.

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #1 (voice cooling)**  
Option two: I go get a **warrant**. That takes about **four hours**, give or take.  You sit here.  In this chair.  No phone. No bathroom. No exit.

She taps the swab gently.

**DETECTIVE #1 (final)**  
Then we take the DNA sample anyway.  *Then* you can go to the bathroom.

She smiles.  Not warm. Not cruel.  Just **inevitable**.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
Your move.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Let’s Get It Over With” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**Bill** exhales through his nose, eyes tired, lips twitching in a crooked half-smile that has no humor in it.

**BILL**  
Look, I gotta pee.

He leans forward, elbows on the table, and nudges the DNA kit with two fingers.

**BILL (dry)**  
So let’s get this test done, yeah?  I’ve got *nothing to hide.*

He looks her dead in the eye now, voice rising—not angry, just *done.*

**BILL**  
I haven’t gotten laid in ten days.  I didn’t rape anybody.  I *carried* her.  Up three fucking flights of stairs. In the dark.  With **rats**, mind you.

He gestures vaguely upward, toward the city they climbed out of.

**BILL**  
And the only goddamn light we had was a **25-year-old assistant** with an iPhone and more guts than most people I’ve ever played a stadium for.

He leans back, arms wide like: *go ahead. Do it.*

**BILL (flat)**  
Swab me.  Then let me take a leak.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Not Quite Yet” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

**Detective #1** gives Bill a tight, unreadable smile and pulls the DNA kit closer. She unseals it with clinical efficiency, lays out the swab, the vial, the gloves.

**DETECTIVE #1 (calm, cool)**  
Well, Mr. Davenport, we’ll get this test done.

She stands, gestures to the hallway door.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
And because you’re not quite yet a person of interest…

She smiles wider, just slightly — the kind that means *"you’re close."*

**DETECTIVE #1 (mock-genteel)**  
We’re not even going to watch.  How’s that for trust?

She opens the door. A **uniformed officer** stands just outside.

**DETECTIVE #1 (to the officer)**  
Escort him to the restroom.  Swab, seal, log. No eyes, no hands, just the sample.

Then, turning back to Bill—

**DETECTIVE #1 (voice dipping)**  
But, uh… let’s not get any ideas.

**DETECTIVE #1 (cool and firm)**  
We’re not going to let you go **too terribly far.**

She steps back, arms crossed.

**DETECTIVE #1 (final)**  
Let’s all keep playing nice.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Don’t Call Her Maddy” – Interrogation Room, NYPD**

Bill is halfway through standing up when he turns, voice tight.

**BILL (sharp)**  
What about the kid?

**Detective #1** glances up from her notes, casual.

**DETECTIVE #1 (mild)**  
Maddy?

**BILL (snaps)**  
That would be **Madeline**.

A pause. His tone is ice.

**BILL**  
No one calls her *Maddy* and gets away with it.

The detective raises an eyebrow.  Then sets her pen down slowly.

**DETECTIVE #1 (flat, matter-of-fact)**  
She gave a fake ID to a cop.  In a cop car.  Right in front of a precinct.  That’s **felony stupid**, Mr. Davenport.

She leans in just a touch.

**DETECTIVE #1**  
She’s looking at **hard time.**  You don’t lie to NYPD in the middle of a live scene. Especially not when you’re crawling out of a rat pit with a potential rape victim and amphetamines in your pocket.

She lets it hang. Then adds, too casually:

**DETECTIVE #1 (mock sweet)**  
She’s going straight to jail.  Do not pass Go.  Do not collect two hundred dollars.

Bill’s jaw tightens.  But she’s not done.

**DETECTIVE #1 (leaning in now, real quiet)**  
And Mr. Davenport…If she decides to revise her **bullshit** story?

Beat.

**DETECTIVE #1 (cold)**  
You’re not going to like it very much.

---

# **“Strip Search” – NYPD Precinct, Holding Area**

**INT. NYPD – PRIVATE SEARCH ROOM – LATE MORNING**

The **fluorescent light** overhead doesn’t flicker. It hums. Constant. Flat. Cold.   There’s **no clock** in this room. No windows. No airflow. Just tile and shadows.

**Madeline stands at the center**, already stripped of her shoes, jewelry, and dignity.  Her wrists twitch involuntarily. Her jaw’s locked tight enough to cramp.   She’s **stone still**, except for the **tiny tremor in her breath**—like her lungs are trying not to make noise.

**Two female officers** are present:

* **Officer #1**, older, large hands, silent.
* **Officer #2**, clinical, glove-snapping, reciting from memory.

No names.  No eye contact.   No acknowledgment that **she’s a person**.

**OFFICER #2 (flat, procedural)**  
You are subject to a full-body search as part of your high-risk intake designation.  This includes cavity inspection. Internal.  Face the wall. Remove all clothing. Hands on the rail.

Madeline hesitates. Just a second.  Then she obeys.  Her fingers **fumble** with the buttons. Her shirt peels off like **wet paper**.   Her bra strap catches on her elbow, and she **wrenches it off** without finesse.  Her skirt slides down. Her underwear follows. It gets **stuck on her heel.**

She stares at the grout between the tiles as she kicks it away.  There is **no sound** except latex gloves being stretched over hands.

**OFFICER #1 (calm, practiced)**  
Bend forward at the waist. Separate the cheeks. Deep breath.

Madeline obeys.  Her palms press against **cold tile**.  Her arms tremble slightly. Her knees lock.  Her breath catches halfway down. She tries again.  **Breath. In. Out.**

The glove **enters.**

No warning. No counting. No cruelty.  Just **penetration. Deep. Unnatural. Uninvited.**  Her body *accepts* it with a shame that makes her toes curl on the tile.

**(V.O. – Madeline)**  
*It’s not pain. Not really.*  *It’s being touched where no one should touch unless they ask first. Unless they love you. Unless you say yes.* *No one asked.*  *No one said anything.*

She stares at a **chip in the paint** on the wall.  Wonders how long it’s been there.  How many other women have stared at it, too. How many tried to go somewhere else in their heads.  **The glove withdraws.**  There’s a slick sound. A wipe. The snap of latex coming off.  

No one speaks.

**OFFICER #2 (quiet)**  
You may dress.

Madeline doesn’t move.  Not right away.  She feels like if she moves too fast, her organs will spill out of her.  Like she might make a sound she can’t take back.

She pulls her clothes on **slowly**:

* Bra twisted, backwards, rehooked with shaking fingers.
* Shirt buttoned wrong, rebuttoned.
* Underwear forgotten, then grabbed.
* Skirt wrinkled, clinging to damp skin.

She doesn’t look at them. They don’t look at her.

**When she finally stands**, she’s not the same girl who walked in. Her spine is **straighter**, somehow.  But her shoulders are **collapsed inward**—like someone tied strings around her soul and pulled tight.

She walks out of the room.  No one opens the door for her.  No one tells her she did fine.

---

### **INT. NYPD HOLDING AREA – MOMENTS LATER**

She sits on the bench.  Alone.  The room is crowded, but **she’s alone.**  She doesn’t speak. She doesn’t cry.  Just stares straight ahead, **trying not to be in her own skin.**

**(V.O. – Madeline)**  
*I will never forget the sound of that glove.*  *I will never forget how no one looked at me.*  *I will never forget what I felt like when I bent over.*  *I don’t care what they charge me with.*  *I just want that room to burn.*

---

### **SCENE: “The Clink” – NYPD Holding Cell**

**INT. NYPD HOLDING – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The **iron gate slams shut** behind her with the *clack* of a world ending.  **Madeline** stands just inside the holding cell. The walls are stained. The light flickers. The **stench** is unholy — sweat, bleach, and something older.

There are **five other women** already in the cell. **None of them like her.**  They glance up. Not curious. Not welcoming.  Just… sizing.

One is sleeping with her back to the wall.  Another is **pacing**, muttering to herself in Spanish.  Two are seated, whispering, eyes sharp.  And one — older, scarred, heavyset — just stares at Madeline like she’s a piece of *new meat dropped into the tank.*

**Madeline doesn’t belong here.**

She knows it.  *They* know it.

She’s **an Ivy Leaguer**.  Child of privilege.  Academic elite.  A well-groomed asset from a polished world.  She’s read *The New Yorker*. She’s *been in it.*
And now she’s in **city holding.**

She moves slowly to a bench against the far wall, sits with her back straight, legs crossed, **clutching her knees with her hands to avoid shaking.**

The older woman smirks.

**OLDER WOMAN (to her, mocking)**  
Nice shoes.

**Madeline doesn’t respond.**  She doesn’t know the rules here.  Not yet.  But she’s going to learn them **the hard way.**

---

# **“Fallout Inbox” – Island Records, 14th Floor**

**INT. CREMEANS’ OFFICE – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The glow from three monitors washes over **Cremeans’ face**, ghost-pale and tight with tension. Behind him, **Sarah and Jeremy** argue quietly in the hallway, the door cracked but not open.

**Cremeans’ laptop pings.**

New email.  
**From:** elijah.matheson@cmdlegal.com
**Subject: Madeline Quinlan & Bill Davenport – Update**

He clicks.

*“At precinct. They’ve booked Quinlan on felony charges. Working on details.”*  
*“I’m going to try to get Davenport out now. It shouldn’t be difficult. He’s not even officially a person of interest — yet.”*

Cremeans stares at it.  **No salutation. No spin. Just facts.**  He slowly removes his glasses. Rubs the bridge of his nose with two fingers.

**CREMEANS (to himself, softly)**  
Felony.  Jesus, Madeline…

He swallows hard. Clicks open a secure comms window. Drafts a message to Sarah. Stops. Doesn’t send it yet.  He knows what it means.  **They’ve lost her.**

And if they don’t move **fast**, they might lose **Bill** too.

---

### **SCENE: “Write Him Back” – Island Records, 14th Floor Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – MAIN CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The room is thick with tension. **Cremeans** is standing, staring at his laptop like it just cursed him. The email from the lawyer still open.

**Sarah bursts in** like a thunderclap, **Jeff and Jeremy** just behind her.

**SARAH (exploding)**  
*How the fuck did that happen?\!*

Everyone turns.

**SARAH (furious, pacing now)**  
This is a **fucking sex crime case**, and our little **Madeline**—the only one with the guts to crawl into that goddamn tunnel—is the one getting **booked**?!

She stops in front of Cremeans, her eyes blazing.

**SARAH (venomous)**  
*Write him back.*

Cremeans blinks.

**CREMEANS**  
Sarah, I—

**SARAH (cuts him off)**  
*Write him the fuck back\!*

And then, she **jumps up onto the conference table**, right in front of his screen, heels clacking on the wood.  She **points her finger down at him**, eyes wild, voice shaking with fury and disbelief.

**SARAH (roaring)**  
You tell that nine-hundred-dollar-an-hour corpse with a Harvard degree that he needs to FIX THIS.  That girl is not a criminal.  She’s a goddamn hero.

**JEFF (softly, off to the side)**  
Jesus…

**JEREMY (not even arguing this time)**  
She’s not wrong.

**SARAH (finger still wagging, teeth clenched)**  
Write.  Him.  *Back.*

Cremeans nods once, sits, and begins typing.

**SARAH (softer, but no less lethal)**  
And if he can’t get her out in the next two hours?  We find someone who can.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Airtight” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 14TH FLOOR – MINUTES LATER**

**Cremeans’ laptop pings.** A new message appears from the defense attorney.

**From:** elijah.matheson@cmdlegal.com  
**Subject:** Quinlan – Update

They’ve bagged her.  Gave a false name to a sworn officer during a live scene involving a potential sexual assault victim.  She was in the vehicle.  
She initiated the lie.  They logged it.  Recorded it.  Booked her.  That’s an airtight case.  She’s looking at real time.

Cremeans reads it once.  Then again.  He doesn’t say anything. Just turns the screen toward **Sarah**.  She reads it. Her eyes **don’t blink**.

**SARAH (quietly, deadly)**  
Real time?

**CREMEANS (voice dry, numb)**  
“Airtight case.”

**JEFF (in disbelief)**  
She’s not a criminal. She’s just—she was scared. She panicked.

**JEREMY (flat)**  
Yeah, well…*The system doesn’t care about panic.*

**SARAH (quietly)**  
She gave the wrong name in front of a cop with a body cam.  They don’t need a motive.  They just need the timestamp.

She steps back from the table. The fire in her isn’t gone, it’s just **coalescing**.

**SARAH (cold)**  
Okay.  If the law won’t save her?

We **will.**

---

### **SCENE: “Give Me the Name” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**Sarah** stands at the head of the table, fury vibrating through her voice, but her aim is surgical. She’s not lashing out blindly — she’s locked in on **Jeff**.

**SARAH (pointing hard)**  
*You. Jeff.*

He looks up, startled.

**SARAH (voice sharp, fast)**  
I don’t want the story. I don’t need the backpedal.  I want **the name.**

Jeff blinks.

**SARAH (stepping toward him)**  
You had a lawyer.  A real one.  The one who got you out of that **disaster in Massachusetts** when Kathy died in your apartment and your nose was a pharmacy.

Beat.

**SARAH (burning, relentless)**  
That lawyer — *that* son of a bitch — pulled you out of a goddamn fire.  
And if he could do that?  He can pull **Madeline** out of this jailhouse.

**JEFF (hesitating)**  
Sarah—

**SARAH (snaps)**  
*Give me the name.*

**JEREMY (quietly, off to the side)**  
She’s right, man.

**SARAH (final, cold as steel)**  
We’re not letting her rot while we stand around wringing our hands like executives at a funeral.

**SARAH (one last time, slow and deadly)**  
Give me.  The fucking.  Name.

---

### **SCENE: “Call Your Guy” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**Sarah** stands in the middle of the room, seething — **not accusing, commanding**. Her eyes are locked on **Jeff**, and everyone else in the room knows to stay out of her way.

**SARAH (sharp)**  
*Jeff.*

He turns, already defensive, but she doesn’t let him speak.

**SARAH (biting, focused)**  
I want a name.  Not a story. Not a memory.  The **lawyer**.

**JEFF (frowns)**  
I don't think—

**SARAH (fires over him)**  
The one who cleaned it up when Kathy died at **St. Eligius.**

Jeff freezes.

**SARAH (lower, but no less furious)**  
She was in rehab. You dropped her off with a van full of other broken kids, and four hours later, *her brain exploded.*

**She stares him down.**

**SARAH (cold)**  
It wasn’t your fault.  But it damn near *became* your fault until your guy — whoever he was — stepped in and handled it. Silenced the whispers. Sealed the files.

**She steps closer.** Her voice is steel now.

**SARAH**  
*That’s* who I want.  That same lawyer.  Because **if he could protect you** in a mess that close to a corpse, he can damn well get **Madeline** out of a holding cell on a bad ID and a bullshit accusation.

**JEFF (quiet, uncertain)**  
Sarah, that was years ago. I don't even know if—

**SARAH (snaps, full heat)**  
*Don’t even start.*

She points directly at him now, finger steady.

**SARAH**  
Call him.  Text him.  Scream his name into the wind.  I don’t care how you find him — *but you do.*

**SARAH (final)**  
You owe her that much.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Card” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**Jeff** stands at the side of the table, reaching into his wallet like it’s a vault. He pulls out a **battered, sun-faded business card**, worn at the edges but **still intact**.

He turns it over once. Looks at the number.

**JEFF (quietly)**  
I’ve had this for twelve years.  I don’t even know if he still practices. He might’ve retired.  And I don’t know if he’s even **licensed** to practice in New York. I mean—*Massachusetts and New York aren’t—*

**SARAH (low and lethal)**  
*Make the fucking call, sir.*

**Jeff freezes.**

He looks up.  **Sarah** is standing across from him like a force of nature, like **a warhead dressed in a record label's black blouse**.  Her eyes could cut glass. Her voice doesn’t rise — it doesn’t need to.

**SARAH (calm and deadly)**  
We are not going to lose her because you got **shy about interstate law**.

**JEFF (swallows)**  
Okay.

He takes a breath.  Taps the number into his phone.  Puts it on speaker.  The line rings once.

Twice.

And then—

**VOICE (V.O., crisp, cold)**  
This is Bennett King. Who’s this?

**Sarah smiles.**  Not kindly.

---

### **SCENE: “Six Hours Out” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY AFTERNOON**

**JEFF (clearing his throat)**  
Bennett. It’s Jeff. Jeff Evans.

A pause.

**BENNETT (V.O.) (slow smile in his voice)**  
Well, well. **Jeff Evans.**  Didn’t think I’d hear that name again unless I was deposing you.

**JEFF (half-hearted smile)**  
Not this time.  
I need help.

**BENNETT (V.O.) (already intrigued)**  
Is it you?

**JEFF (shaking his head)**  
No. It’s a colleague.  Name’s Madeline Quinlan. She’s in custody at NYPD, Canal and Centre.  Felony false ID. They’re posturing like she’s tied to a sex crime case.  It’s bad.

**BENNETT (V.O.) (slight pause)**  
Huh.

Beat.

**BENNETT (V.O.)**  
I'm in Boston.

**JEFF** closes his eyes for half a beat.

**JEFF**  
Understood.

**BENNETT (V.O.) (coolly efficient)**  
I’ll be there in six hours. Maybe five if the troopers are looking the other way.  
In the meantime, text me everything: name, arrest sheet, precinct details, anything that smells like leverage.

**JEFF**  
You still licensed in New York?

**BENNETT (V.O.) (snorts)**  
You think I’d give up my Manhattan card?  *Please.*

**JEFF (relieved)**  
Thank you.

**BENNETT (V.O.) (smiling)**  
Jeff… you already bought me a beach house in Rhode Island.  Let’s see what Kiawah Island costs you.

*Click.*

**Jeff lowers the phone slowly.** Everyone’s watching.

**SARAH (without a trace of irony)**  
He’ll do.

---

**SCENE: “I’ll Quit on the Spot” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY AFTERNOON**

**Sarah** grabs her phone, her blazer, and the room’s attention in one sweep. She’s not yelling anymore — she’s **crystal-clear, deadly-calm**, and louder than any scream because of it.

**SARAH (to the room)**  
I’m going upstairs.

**JEFF (cautious)**  
To…?

**SARAH (without missing a beat)**  
*To talk to the CEO.*

That stops everyone.

**CREMEANS (blinking)**  
Wait. Right now?

**SARAH (clipped)**  
Yes, *right now*. Because this mess? This crisis?  It’s going to put a **severe kink in this quarter’s P&L statement**.

She grabs the door handle, turns back.

**SARAH (flat, honest)**  
And you know what?

**SARAH**  
*I don’t give a flying fuck.*

She locks eyes with each of them in turn.

**SARAH (cold)**  
If I don’t get what I want? If I don’t get **support** for Madeline?  If I don’t get **buy-in** to run the recovery the way I know it needs to be done?

Beat.

**SARAH (final)**  
*I will quit. On. The. Spot.*

The room is frozen.  She opens the door.

**SARAH (to herself, on the way out)**  
Let’s see how they like unfucking a brand without the one person holding the walls up.

*Door closes.*

---

### **SCENE: “Holey Roller” – Island Records, Elevator Bank**

**INT. ELEVATOR – 14TH FLOOR – MOMENTS LATER**

The elevator doors start to close—**Sarah inside**, jaw locked, eyes blazing.

At the last second, **Cremeans slips in**, breathless, laptop clutched to his chest.

**CREMEANS (tentative)**  
Sarah, listen—You’re right. You’re absolutely right, I just think—

**SARAH (explodes)**  
*No. No, no, no, no, no.*  You don’t get to walk in here with your spreadsheets and your Twitter feeds and your *calm voice bullshit* and try to play paramedic after the crash!

**CREMEANS (hands up, trying)**  
I’m not saying back down. I’m saying **strategize**—

**SARAH (turns, finger in his chest)**  
*Strategize?!*

The elevator descends.

**SARAH (raging)**  
We have the label's **kid** in a holding cell, a **global scandal** rolling down on us, and you wanna talk about **engagement metrics**?

**CREMEANS (calmly)**  
I’m on your side, Sarah.

**SARAH (snaps)**  
You’re a **holey-roller, cover-your-ass son-of-a-bitch** who thinks crisis management is a fucking *whiteboard exercise*.  You can take your charts and **take a poo flinging fuck off**.

Cremeans flinches. But doesn’t respond.  The elevator dings — **9th floor.**

**SARAH (full fire now, voice sharp as shattered glass)**  
You don’t get to calm me down.  I’m not a **glitch** in your code.  I’m the goddamn **firewall** keeping this company from self-immolating.

**Ding. 5th floor.**

She steps up to his face, voice low, lethal.

**SARAH (cold as death)**  
Now either shut up and back me, or get out of the way and let me burn this place down **professionally.**

The elevator hits the **executive floor**.  She storms out.  Cremeans stays behind, shaken but silent.

---

### **SCENE: “Midwestern Nice Doesn’t Cut It” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

The elevator *dings* in the distance.  **Cremeans** walks back in, slower than before, his shoulders tight, his expression flat. **Jeff** and **Jeremy** look up from their phones, the silence heavy with fallout.

**JEFF (carefully)**  
How’d it go?

**CREMEANS (quiet, measured)**  
She called me a "**holey roller son-of-a-bitch**" and told me to and "**take a poo flinging fuck off**."

A long pause.

**JEREMY (blinking)**  
…Yikes.

**Cremeans** doesn’t sit. He just stands there for a moment, letting the silence breathe.

**CREMEANS (low, thoughtful)**  
We’ve got to remember something.

They wait.

**CREMEANS**  
*We are allies. And enemies.*

**JEFF (frowns)**  
What does that mean?

**CREMEANS**  
It means Sarah works for Island.  I work for Commuted.  You're the talent.  I'm the LLC.  And she just made that very clear in that elevator.

He finally sits, dropping his laptop on the table with a tired thud.

**CREMEANS (more to himself)**  
I tried the whole Midwestern nice thing. Calm her down. Talk it through.  Didn’t work.

**JEREMY**  
She’s on fire.

**CREMEANS (flat)**  
Yeah. And we’re standing real close to the flames.

---

# **“Sprung” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

The phones are dead silent — until **Cremeans’ cell rings**, buzzing against the table like it’s possessed.

He checks the screen.

**CREMEANS**  
It’s Bill.

He picks up.

**CREMEANS (quickly)**  
Bill? Talk to me.

**INTERCUT – EXT. NYC STREET – BILL ON THE PHONE**

**BILL (winded, confused)**  
Yeah. It’s me.  I’m out. I’m—*they let me go.*

**CREMEANS (blinking)**  
Wait—what?

**BILL (rushed)**  
They just… gave me back my phone. Said I wasn’t a person of interest. My lawyer said the same thing.  I don’t even know what that *means*, but—

**JEFF (overhearing, cutting in)**  
Bill, where’s **Madeline**?

**BILL (quiet)**  
She’s not with me.

**The room freezes.**

**JEREMY (low)**  
Shit.

**CREMEANS (carefully)**  
Bill. Are you near a charger?

**BILL**  
Phone’s dying. One percent maybe. I’m outside the precinct. Just—  
Can someone tell me *what the hell is going on*?

**CREMEANS (quiet)**  
We’re trying to. Sit tight.

**BILL (strained)**  
They didn’t even say why they let me out. Just said, *"you’re not who we’re focused on."*  I thought maybe that meant she was out too, but—

**SARAH (from behind them, having just reentered)**  
*She’s not.*

Everyone turns.

**SARAH (ice cold)**  
And we’re running out of time.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “For Now” – Island Records, Conference Room**

The team is still digesting Bill’s call when the conference room door opens.

**Sarah** walks in — her expression unreadable, her hair just slightly out of place, blazer unbuttoned like she peeled it off on the elevator ride and threw it back on out of spite.

No one speaks.

She drops her phone on the table. Looks around at **Cremeans**, **Jeff**, **Jeremy**.

Then:

**SARAH (flat)**  
You may presume that I kept my job.

Beat.

**SARAH (still cool)**  
*For now.*

No celebration. No smile. Just the weight of a woman who’s been toe-to-toe with corporate power and came out breathing — and pissed.

**JEFF (quietly)**  
How bad?

**SARAH (grim)**  
Bad enough I have to babysit every move we make until this thing is cold.  
But we’ve got a window.

**CREMEANS**  
And Madeline?

**SARAH (looks at him like a loaded gun)**  
Still inside.

**JEREMY**  
So what now?

**SARAH (grabbing her phone again)**  
Now we build pressure.  Now we leak.  Now we burn the optics from the outside in.

---

### **SCENE: “Orders from the Top” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

**Sarah** stands at the head of the table, sleeves pushed up, phone in one hand, pointing with the other.

**SARAH (to Jeff)**  
Jeff, you’re on the **BBC**.

**JEFF (blinking)**  
Seriously?

**SARAH**  
Yes. You’re good with the Brits. They like the slower pacing — gives you time to think. Stick to tone control, no facts they can twist. Stick to language like “support,” “deep concern,” and “private health crisis.” That should be your mantra. Say it with vowels.

She turns.

**SARAH (to Jeremy)**  
Jeremy, you’re on **local stations** — ABC, NBC, Fox.  You’re gonna be tied up for the rest of the day. Sorry about that. Thank you very much. Be on your way.

**JEREMY (half-grinning)**  
Yes, ma’am.

**SARAH**  
Go downstairs. Use the media room on the first floor.  
There’s probably a *horde* of cameras outside. We’ll screen them — bring in the **locals**.

She pauses.

**SARAH (thinking aloud)**  
Who the fuck else is local these days? New York One? Is that still a thing?

No one answers.

**SARAH (waving it off)**  
Doesn’t matter. If they’ve got a mic and a logo, let them in one at a time.

She pivots.

**SARAH (to the group)**  
When **Bill** gets here, he goes **on ice.**  We are not — I repeat, *not* — having him say a goddamn word to *anyone.*

Beat.

She turns to **Cremeans**.

**SARAH**  
And you, Cremeans?  You’re gonna write some **scripts.**

**CREMEANS**  
For who?

**SARAH**  
For *everyone*.  We need clean messaging.  We’re gonna use some of our alt accounts — the influencers, the soft echo chambers. Start **blasting narratives across platforms**.

Cremeans nods, already typing.

**SARAH (clear, sharp)**  
The narrative is:

**She pauses.**

**SARAH (cold, calm, controlled)**  
*Avril Lavigne suffered a psychological and medical crisis.*  
*She is currently in recovery.*  
*She was found by two members of her close professional circle.*  
*One is being unfairly held.*  
*The other has been released.*  
*We ask for privacy.*  
*We thank the NYPD for their cooperation.*  
*And we are monitoring the situation closely.*

Beat.

**SARAH (to Cremeans, fire in her voice now)**  
Now make it look like *ten thousand people just happened to say that all at once.*

---

# **“The Cell” – NYPD Holding, Late Afternoon**

**INT. HOLDING CELL – NYPD PRECINCT – LATE AFTERNOON**

**Madeline** sits on the cold bench, arms wrapped tightly around her knees. Her blazer is gone. Her shoes are scuffed. Her eyes — glassy, red — stare at the wall across from her like it might split open and let her escape.

Around her: **concrete, iron, and strangers**.

The cell smells like old disinfectant and sweat. No windows. No clocks. **Time doesn’t pass here — it just drips.**

One of the other women — a street-tough thirty-something with smeared eyeliner and a cigarette voice — watches her like a cat watches a bird.

**WOMAN (quietly)**  
You ain’t from here, huh?

**Madeline** doesn’t respond.

**WOMAN (smiling)**  
Yeah. I can tell.

She turns back to her corner.

**Madeline closes her eyes.**

She is:

**Incredibly afraid.**  **Incredibly alone.**  And in **incredible trouble.** She tries not to cry — because crying in here feels like bleeding in the ocean. She clenches her jaw, tries to think. Tries to remember the names of people who might be helping. She pictures Sarah. Cremeans. The band. Bill. *Anyone.*

**But no one has come.**

Not yet.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Marked” – NYPD Holding Cell**

**INT. HOLDING CELL – NYPD PRECINCT – LATE AFTERNOON**

The cell buzzes with fluorescent fatigue and the low murmur of boredom, resentment, and street-scarred instinct.  **Madeline** sits near the corner, trying to make herself invisible — knees up, jaw clenched, eyes fixed on a crack in the wall.

But invisibility doesn’t work here.

Not when you **look like privilege**.  Not when you **smell like fear**. A voice cuts across the cell — sharp, nasal, loaded with challenge.

**WOMAN (mid-40s, bleached hair, Queens accent)**  
*Hey, bitch.*

Madeline doesn’t look up.

**WOMAN (louder)**  
*Hey. I’m talkin’ to you.*

Madeline slowly turns her head.

**WOMAN (eyes narrowed)**  
Why the fuck are you here?

A second woman — younger, hoodie pulled tight — snorts under her breath.

**HOODIE GIRL (mocking)**  
She looks like she got lost on the way to brunch.

**BLEACH HAIR WOMAN (to Madeline)**  
So what is it, huh?  You kill someone?  Rob a store?  *Sex crime?*

That last one lands like a brick.

**Madeline flinches.**

The older woman grins. Jackpot.

**WOMAN (leaning in, smug)**  
Thought so.

**MADELINE (voice tight, quiet)**  
I didn’t do anything.

**WOMAN**  
Yeah, none of us did, sweetheart.

Laughter. Low. Ugly.

**Madeline looks down at her hands.** She’s still shaking.  Because in here?  
**Truth doesn’t matter.**  Only how long you can hold your ground.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “You Better Fess Up” – NYPD Holding Cell**

**INT. HOLDING CELL – NYPD PRECINCT – LATE AFTERNOON**

The women have shifted. There’s no more performance — **now it’s just pressure**. Real. Heavy. Close.  **Madeline** stares straight ahead, trying not to breathe too loud.  But **Bleach Hair Woman** steps closer. Real close.  Leans down until her voice is **right by Madeline’s ear** — just loud enough for the others to hear, but soft enough to feel like **a secret made of knives.**

**WOMAN (quiet, sing-song)**  
Honey… you better fess up.

Madeline doesn’t move.

**WOMAN (smiling now)**  
'Cause when the plastic surgeon gets done with you…?

She tilts her head, still smiling.

**WOMAN**  
*Your mama still ain't gonna recognize your face.*

The room gets colder.  Another girl in the corner laughs — low, humorless.

**Madeline’s breathing picks up.** Her hands curl into fists on her knees, **white-knuckled**, but she says nothing.

**WOMAN (mock sympathy)**  
Oh… you thought this was temporary.  You thought someone was comin’ for you.

Beat.

**WOMAN (harsher now)**  
*They’re not.*

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Last Straw” – NYPD Holding Cell**

**INT. HOLDING CELL – NYPD PRECINCT – LATE AFTERNOON**

**Madeline** doesn’t respond. She **can’t**. Her chest tightens, her vision blurs, and that long, impossible line she’s been walking **finally gives out** beneath her.

She had:

— crawled through tunnels  
— tracked a friend to the edge of hell  
— **saved a life**  
— been strip-searched  
— cavity-checked  
— booked  
— labeled an **accomplice to rape**  
— **threatened** with violence in a fluorescent-lit cage

And now, a woman twice her size just told her her face was next.  That was it.
**Madeline folds.**

**She bursts into tears** — not polite sniffles, not the kind you can hide with a shoulder — **this is body-shaking, silent, feral weeping.**  She presses both hands to her mouth, trying to stop the noise, trying to **stay invisible**, but it’s too late.

The room notices.  

Bleach Hair Woman steps back, smiling.

**WOMAN (mocking)**  
Aww. There she goes. Told you she’d crack.

But Madeline doesn’t hear it anymore.  She’s gone inward.  **She was the one who saved the day.**  And now she’s **alone. Cold. Dirty. Terrified.**  Her body hurts. Her pride is gone.  And the people upstairs?  **She has no idea if they even care.**

---

### **SCENE: “The Arrival” – NYPD Precinct, Secure Room**

**INT. HOLDING CELL – MOMENTS EARLIER**

A **guard opens the door** without warning.

**GUARD**  
Quinlan. On your feet.

**Madeline** startles, still mid-sob, eyes puffy and red, breath caught in her chest.

**GUARD (sharper)**  
Let’s go.  You’ve got… representation.

---

### **INT. NYPD – SECURE INTERVIEW ROOM – MINUTES LATER**

Fluorescent light again. But **cleaner**, somehow. Less rust. More silence.

**Madeline** is led in by two officers. Her hands are shaking. Her eyes down.

Then—She sees him.

**Bennett King.**  
Tall. Immaculate. **Charcoal suit, silk tie, black eyes like the ocean in winter.**  Sitting with a **folder the thickness of a novel** and a stare that **could outlast a courtroom clock**.

He doesn’t stand.  He just gestures to the seat across from him like it’s **hers by right.**

**BENNETT (cool, measured)**  
Ms. Quinlan.  You’ve had a morning.

Madeline sinks into the chair like her bones gave out.

**BENNETT (opening folder)**  
You’re not charged.  Not formally. Not yet.  They’re leaning hard on implication and optics. That ends now.

Beat.

**BENNETT (calm, professional)**  
You’re going to answer some questions.  I’m going to give you exact language.  You’ll say only what I tell you to say.  And we’ll walk out of this like it never happened.

Madeline says nothing.  Just stares at him — raw, ruined, and **barely holding on**.

**BENNETT (softens just enough)**  
You’re not alone anymore, Madeline.

And for the first time in hours—**She believes it.**

---

# **“Come to Jesus” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – LATE AFTERNOON**

**Madeline** sits stiffly across from **Bennett King**, eyes still swollen, posture small.  He flips open a folder, slides a still frame across the table: a grainy body cam image of **her in the backseat of a cruiser**, mouth mid-sentence.

**BENNETT (flat, calm)**  
What were you thinking when you gave a false name to a cop?

Madeline opens her mouth, but he **holds up a finger.**

**BENNETT (sharper now)**  
*No. Don’t talk yet. Listen.*

He leans forward, voice tightening:

**BENNETT**  
Did you think you were back at **Columbia**?  Still a **freshman**, trying on rebellion like it’s a second major?  This isn’t campus security. This is **real life.**

He taps the image on the table.

**BENNETT (cold)**  
I’ve watched the video.  *I watched you lie.*  Bold-faced. Clean delivery.  You even made eye contact with the officer when you said it.

**He lets it hang.**

**BENNETT (measured)**  
This is an **open and shut** case, Madeline.

Beat.

**BENNETT**  
Now — here’s what we’re going to do.  You’re going to tell me **why**.  No spin. No fluff. No white-girl PR sob story.

**BENNETT (flat, unblinking)**  
This is **Come to Jesus.**

He pauses — just long enough.

**BENNETT (dead serious)**  
And I don’t care if you’re Jewish, Catholic, agnostic, Zoroastrian, or pray to a crystal.  Right now?  *You are in the church of consequences.*  And I am your only priest.

**MADELINE**  (small, trembling)  
I was trying to protect her.

**BENNETT (quiet, finally allowing space)**  
Then let’s start with that.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “$1,800 an Hour” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – EVENING**

**Madeline** sits frozen. Her hands are locked together so tightly her knuckles are white. Across from her, **Bennett King** closes the folder, folds his hands, and stares at her like he’s already on the stand, mid-cross.

**BENNETT (low, even)**  
Put it all on the line, Ms. Quinlan.

She doesn’t answer.

**BENNETT (calmer, colder)**  
Because let me explain something very clearly to you right now.

He leans in.

**BENNETT**  
They’re paying me **eighteen hundred dollars an hour.**

He watches her reaction — nothing.

**BENNETT**  
And this? This **right here**?  This is going to take me **weeks**.

Beat.

**BENNETT (slow, deliberate)**  
Weeks of filings.  Weeks of discovery battles.  Weeks of press control.  Weeks of parsing every word you’ve ever said in a digital space.  And all of that? Is either for **something true**…Or for **a lie I find out too late to spin**.

**MADELINE (quiet)**  
I wasn’t trying to deceive. I panicked.

**BENNETT (immediate)**  
Good. Then let’s get that panic **on the record**.  Let’s get the story **clean**, **structured**, and **legally survivable**.

He opens a fresh page on his yellow legal pad.

**BENNETT**  
Start from the moment you got the ping.  Don’t skip a second.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Note by Note” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE INTERVIEW ROOM – NIGHTFALL**

**Madeline** finishes her sentence, voice barely audible, her eyes locked on the legal pad in front of Bennett.

**BENNETT (nods once)**  
That’s a good first start.

He sets his pen down. Leans back in his chair.  Then his voice changes — not louder, but **harder. Sharper.**

**BENNETT (cold)**  
But now you’re going to tell me **what the hell you were doing**.  *All* of it.  From the first moment.  From the beginning.

**BENNETT (voice rising slightly)**  
We play it forward — note by note, beat by beat — until we land in that fucking subway tunnel, with a near-dead woman and your fingerprints on everything.

**Madeline** breathes in sharply, tries to stay composed.

**BENNETT (presses)**  
No skipping. No summaries. I don’t want your highlight reel.  I want your **confession before the world gets one leaked through the tabloids**.

Then — a pause.  He leans forward, locks eyes.

**BENNETT (low, dangerous)**  
And by God, Madeline…*are you protecting Mr. Davenport?*

She stiffens.

**BENNETT (cuts through her)**  
Because if you are — If you’re protecting him…  And he’s guilty?

His hand slaps the legal pad shut.

**BENNETT (deadly calm)**  
You are going **straight to hell**.

Beat.

**BENNETT (flat)**  
And even *I* can’t save you from that.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “You Might Just Live” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – LATE NIGHT**

**Madeline** talks for over ten minutes straight.  Her voice cracks, but she keeps going.  She traces the social media tracebacks.  The metadata cross-check.  The abandoned station blueprints.  The route.  The flashlight.  The stairs.  The rats.  *Avril.*  Bill.  Everything.

She gets some things out of order. Corrects herself. Breathes through panic. But she gives him **everything she has**.

And when she finishes — finally — **she looks like she’s aged a year**.

Silence.

**Bennett** sits back. Doesn’t write. Doesn’t speak.  He just **watches her**.  And then, at last:

**BENNETT (quietly, nodding)**  
Good.

Beat.

**BENNETT (again, with a hint of approval)**  
Good.

He closes the legal pad.

**BENNETT (smoother now, colder still)**  
You might just live to see tomorrow.

**Madeline** swallows. Doesn’t cry. But her shoulders sag — the smallest drop of weight off her chest.

**BENNETT (grabbing his phone)**  
Now sit tight. Don’t talk to anyone. Don’t *look* at anyone.  I’m going to go rearrange the city on your behalf.

---

### **SCENE: “What Doesn’t Add Up” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

**Madeline** sits in the hard chair, spent but steady. **Bennett King** stands, collecting his materials, ready to move.  But he doesn’t leave.  He turns slowly. Eyes cold, tone casual.

**BENNETT**  
I got one question for you, Madeline.

She looks up, wary.

**BENNETT (casual, flipping a page)**  
Actually… make that a few.

He walks back to the table, calm and deliberate.

**BENNETT (even)**  
Where did you go to school?

**MADELINE (blinks)**  
Columbia.

**BENNETT (nods)**  
Columbia. Right.

He glances down at the page.

**BENNETT**  
English and Marketing. Double major. Graduated 2015.  That right?

**MADELINE (careful)**  
Yes.

**BENNETT (calm)**  
No minors?  No unfinished semesters?

**MADELINE**  
No. Straight through. I did some summer courses to finish on time.

**BENNETT (tapping his finger)**  
Interesting.

He stares at her a moment. Then:

**BENNETT (flat)**  
You ever get written up?

**MADELINE**  
No.

**BENNETT**  
Probation?

**MADELINE**  
No.

**BENNETT**  
Any internships while you were in school?

**MADELINE**  
Yes. Two.

**BENNETT**  
Where?

**MADELINE**  
Miramax… and a summer placement at Condé Nast.

**BENNETT (smiles, but it doesn’t reach his eyes)**  
Condé Nast. Impressive.

He leans forward, resting his elbows on the table.

**BENNETT (soft, surgical)**  
Now… *why* did you lie to the cop?

Madeline hesitates.

**BENNETT (pounces)**  
See — *that* hesitation? That’s what I’m talking about.

He doesn’t yell. He doesn’t even blink.

**BENNETT**  
You’re **covering** something, Ms. Quinlan.

**MADELINE (quiet, defensive)**  
I told you everything I—

**BENNETT (cuts her off, calm as death)**  
No. You told me *a version.*  A detailed one.  But not the whole one.

He leans in.

**BENNETT (dead serious)**  
I don’t know what part of this story you’re trying to protect.  But if you’re lying to me now?  If you’re holding **even one thing back** — one message, one moment, one mistake?

**BENNETT (cold)**  
I will find out.

He lets that hang.

**BENNETT (quiet, final)**  
You have exactly one more chance to give me **the truth**.  All of it.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “How Much Do You Make?” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

**Bennett** flips to a tabbed page in his file. Glances at it, then at Madeline.

**BENNETT (casual, too casual)**  
How much do you make, Ms. Quinlan?

**MADELINE (thrown slightly)**  
Excuse me?

**BENNETT (reading)**  
I have it on good account that you pull in around **$165,000 a year**.

He looks up.

**BENNETT (tilts his head)**  
Is that accurate?

**MADELINE (hesitates)**  
That’s… close.

**BENNETT**  
Plus or minus?

**MADELINE**  
Plus. A little. Bonuses. Stock options. It's variable.

**BENNETT (nods, dry)**  
Variable. Sure. Add in a couple of **strawberry milkshakes** you like so much at that spot in Nolita — that gets us what, 168? 169?

**Madeline stares.**

**BENNETT (still smiling)**  
Yeah. I notice things. That’s kind of my job.

He leans in slightly, tone sharpening.

**BENNETT**  
You make more than a lot of the cops in this building.  You make more than some of the **DAs** who might take this case.

Beat.

**BENNETT (lower now)**  
So what I need to know is — why would a woman making $165K a year, with a Columbia degree, a record label job, and a social graph deeper than half the industry…

**BENNETT (hard)**  
Lie to a cop?

He lets it hang again.

**BENNETT (cold, clear)**  
Because the people who prosecute women like you?  *Love* that question.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Privilege Check” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

**Bennett King** closes the folder. Doesn’t need it now.  He straightens in his chair and points at himself — two fingers tapped to his chest.

**BENNETT (measured, deadly calm)**  
I am a **Black man** in America.  Dark as midnight.  Raised by a Black parents from the Island, scholarship kid, made it through Yale Law by working twice as hard for half as much respect.

Beat.

**BENNETT (tilting his head)**  
I don’t get breaks.  Not from cops.  Not from courts.  Not from *anyone.*

He turns that finger now — straight at **Madeline**.

**BENNETT (cold, quiet)**  
*You*?

He gestures up and down.

**BENNETT**  
Ivory pale.  Tiny.  What, not even a hundred pounds dripping wet?  Five foot nothing, Columbia-educated, full wardrobe from SoHo and a skincare budget bigger than my retainer.

**BENNETT (harder now)**  
Am I on target?

She says nothing.

**BENNETT (pressing)**  
Or maybe I’m **over** the target?

**He leans forward — just enough.**

**BENNETT (cutting)**  
Tell me, Ms. Quinlan:  Would you say you’ve led an incredible life of **leisure** and **pleasure**?

Beat.

**BENNETT (cold as concrete)**  
*Leisure… and pleasure… and privilege?*

Madeline finally speaks, voice low, cracked.

**MADELINE (quietly)**  
Yes.

**BENNETT (nods)**  
Good.

He sits back, eyes locked on hers.

**BENNETT**  
Then you understand *exactly* why you don’t get to lie.  *Not now.*  Not ever again.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Beautiful People” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

**Bennett** leans back, arms crossed now, watching her like a raptor with a law degree.

**BENNETT (coolly)**  
So… would you say, Ms. Quinlan…

He tilts his head slightly.

**BENNETT**  
That you’re one of the **beautiful people**?

**Madeline** blinks, confused. Her voice barely holds steady.

**MADELINE**  
The beautiful people? I… I don’t understand.

**BENNETT (sing-song, mocking)**  
*The beautiful people. The beautiful people.*  
*The beautiful people. The beautiful people.*

**Madeline** stares. He doesn’t smile.

**BENNETT (cuts in, deadly calm)**  
You know. The ones who **float through life**, get invited to secret parties, know **all the right doors** and exactly what’s behind them.  The ones who act like **they’ve never been bad**…But always know **where the bad things happen.**

He leans forward now, slow, deliberate.

**BENNETT (cold)**  
I’m just wondering…

What would happen if a **district attorney** — city, county, or state — took one look at **your sorry, skinny little ass** and asked themselves:

*Why was this girl* —this *five-foot-tall blonde Columbia grad*— able to **navigate an underground sex dungeon** that doesn’t even show up on Google Maps anymore?

**BENNETT (lower, lethal)**  
Wouldn’t that be interesting?

Beat.

**BENNETT (razor sharp)**  
*Wouldn’t that make a narrative?*

Madeline’s breath hitches. Her fingers grip the edge of the table.  But he’s not done.

**BENNETT (soft now, cruelly precise)**  
Are you going to tell me *you didn’t know what that place was, Ms. Quinlan?*

Beat.

**BENNETT (flat)**  
Or do you want me to find out from someone who doesn’t like you as much as I do?

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “No Cameras, No Lies” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

A long, terrible silence.  Then, **Madeline** swallows and glances up, cautious.

**MADELINE (quietly)**  
Am I being recorded?

**Bennett King** doesn’t move for a beat. Then:

**BENNETT (calm, clear)**  
Absolutely not.

He taps the table twice with his knuckles.

**BENNETT**  
If they were recording you right now, I’d get the case thrown out in **under three motions**.  Technicality. Suppression. Inadmissible.

**BENNETT (pointed)**  
*Effortlessly easy.*

Madeline watches him. Eyes locked. Her hands tremble.

**BENNETT (gently, but firm)**  
So if you’ve got anything to say, Ms. Quinlan…*This is the time.*

Beat.

**MADELINE (slowly, carefully)**  
I was… involved in the scene.  The **underground sex scene**.

**BENNETT doesn’t blink.**

**MADELINE (quieter)**  
Especially in that part of the city. Lower Manhattan.  Back when I was in college.

**BENNETT (evenly)**  
Which was when?

**MADELINE**  
Nine years ago. I was nineteen. Maybe twenty when I stopped.

She looks down. Swallows again.

**MADELINE**  
It’s not something I talk about. It’s… over. That was a different life.  I haven’t been part of that world in almost a decade.

Silence.

**BENNETT (nodding slowly)**  
Okay.

**He sits back, processes it.**

**BENNETT (measured)**  
That explains the navigation.  The instincts.  Why you were the only one in the building who *knew where to look*.

**MADELINE**  
Yes.

**BENNETT (still cool)**  
Good.

He looks her over. Voice lower now.

**BENNETT**  
Then we’ll make sure *that* stays in this room.  Because the DA doesn’t need to know what you used to be.  Only that you saved a woman’s life.

Beat.

**BENNETT (final)**  
Now let me go make that the story.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Lava Lamp Lies” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

Madeline exhales, shoulders sagging as if the confession should have lightened her load.  **Bennett King** doesn't move.  He just watches her.

Then:

**BENNETT (quietly)**  
You’re still lying to me.

**Madeline freezes.**

**BENNETT (cool, reflective)**  
Riddle me this.

He leans forward, elbows on the table, voice soft but unrelenting.

**BENNETT**  
*Nine years ago*, Madeline?

**He repeats it. Slower.**

**BENNETT**  
Nine years ago.

Again.

**BENNETT (eyes narrowing)**  
*Nine years ago.*

He nods like he’s mulling it over — then sharpens.

**BENNETT (calmly lethal)**  
When you say *nine years ago*, do you actually mean…*say,* nine **weeks** ago?  Nine **days** ago?

He locks eyes with her now.

**BENNETT (razor-edged)**  
Or nine **hours** ago?

**Madeline doesn’t answer. Doesn’t blink.**

**BENNETT (leaning in, voice velvet)**  
Because that kind of cummy environment —  That scene, that **world** —  it’s ephemeral.  It **oozes**, Madeline.

**BENNETT (building)**  
It quivers.  It melts.  It reshapes.  It reforms.  It wanders left.  Wanders right.  Floats up.  Sinks down.  It’s like a goddamn **lava lamp of sin.**

**BENNETT (flat)**  
And you knew *exactly* where to go.

**Madeline’s lips part. No sound comes out.**

**BENNETT (calm, final)**  
So here’s how this goes:  *You tell me the truth — the real truth —*  Or I walk.

**BENNETT (lower)**  
I will walk out of this room, out of this building, out of this case.  And when I do?

He points at her chest — not hard, but precise.

**BENNETT**  
*You burn.*

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Scene Today” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

The silence stretches between them.  **Bennett’s** finger is still pointed — not as a threat now, but as a **target**.  **Madeline’s eyes brim**, but she doesn’t cry.  She just… speaks.

**MADELINE (quiet, cracked)**  
I’m still in it.

**Bennett doesn't move. Doesn’t react. Just watches.**

**MADELINE (barely a whisper)**  
*Today.*

She takes a breath like it might kill her.

**MADELINE**  
I swear to God, I quit after junior year.  I was done. I left that world behind.  I thought I left it behind.

She laughs once — dry, bitter.

**MADELINE**  
But then I started making real money.  And I had everything I was supposed to want.

Pause.

**MADELINE (flat)**  
Except I didn’t want any of it in bed.

**Bennett’s brow twitches — the smallest movement.**

**MADELINE (faster now)**  
My boyfriend — he was fine. He was sweet. But it was like drinking tap water with every nerve in my body screaming for whiskey.  *I needed the edge again.*

She shrugs helplessly.

**MADELINE (truth laid bare)**  
And the scene? It was still there.  *Still breathing.*  Still velvet and shadows and doors that don’t open for civilians.

She swallows.

**MADELINE**  
I didn’t go back full-time.  Not like before.

But she looks up — finally meets his eyes.

**MADELINE (honest now)**  
But I went back.

**Beat.**

**MADELINE (quiet)**  
That’s why I knew where to go.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Receipts” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

Madeline exhales after her confession. It's quiet for a breath—**Then Bennett explodes into motion.**

**BENNETT (sharp, relentless)**  
Alright. Good. Truth's out.  Now **give me the receipts**.

**MADELINE (startled)**  
What?

**BENNETT (firing)**  
*How’d you pay for this shit, Madeline?*

He stands, pacing now, folder in hand like a weapon.

**BENNETT (biting)**  
You think confession buys you anything if the DA can’t see it on a screen?

**He jabs a finger in the air.**

**BENNETT**  
*I bet you put it on a Visa.*  Maybe Chase Sapphire? Some cashback deluxe card?

**MADELINE (quiet)**  
It wasn’t—

**BENNETT (talking over her)**  
No? Debit card then? Fine. That leaves a trail too.  We’re gonna go through it *line by line*.  *Transaction by transaction.*

**He stops dead, turns to her.**

**BENNETT (cold)**  
You still got your bills? Still get those nice glossy statements emailed every month?

She hesitates.

**BENNETT (sharper)**  
Because when I get you out of here, we’re gonna **look it up**.  Every ATM withdrawal.  Every cab ride.  Every bar tab.

**MADELINE (whispers)**  
Some of it was cash.

**BENNETT (smirks)**  
Oh. *Cash.*

He leans on the table, voice lower — dead serious.

**BENNETT**  
Tell me something, Madeline.  *Were you stupid enough to pay cash for this shit*…And not leave **any kind of paper trail?**  Because if you were **that** stupid?

**He straightens, voice ice cold.**

**BENNETT (final)**  
Ain’t nothing going to help you.

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “Venmo and Weirdos” – NYPD, Secure Interview Room**

**INT. SECURE ROOM – NIGHT**

**Madeline** leans forward, both elbows on the table now, exhausted but **clear-headed** for the first time all night.

**MADELINE (quick, earnest)**  
I used **Venmo**, okay? Not for everything, but enough.  Some door fees. A tip.  I used **Uber** because I **hate** taking cabs.  The cabs out here suck. It’s like roulette with a steering wheel.

**Bennett** raises an eyebrow, scribbling it all down.

**BENNETT (dryly)**  
You and every millennial defendant I’ve ever had.

**MADELINE (thinking aloud)**  
What else… what else backs this up?

She rubs her temple. Then:

**MADELINE (snaps fingers)**  
I haven’t been in the underground for like, *ten days*.  It was the Tuesday before last.

**BENNETT (without looking up)**  
Date?

**MADELINE**  
That’d be… June 5th, I think. Yeah. I remember because I had a *God-awful* conference call that morning. Still had that shaky voice thing going on.

**BENNETT**  
You sleep with anyone?

**MADELINE (shakes head)**  
No. Didn’t even get laid that night.

**She gives a dry, half-laugh.**

**MADELINE**  
I just went to **take the edge off**.  Watched a couple guys jerk off.

**Bennett’s pen stops for half a beat — then keeps going.**

**MADELINE (shrugs)**  
At the end, there was a guy **painting**.  Like… actual oils, canvas, mood lighting and everything.  Weirdly therapeutic.

She shrugs again.

**MADELINE (flat)**  
It’s New York City. It’s not all rotten.  It’s just… weird.

**BENNETT (quietly, with the faintest trace of a smile)**  
Now you’re starting to sound like a witness I can work with.

He taps his pen against the folder.

**BENNETT (firm)**  
We’ll pull your Venmo logs. Uber routes.  If you’ve got screenshots, statements, anything — we want them.

**MADELINE**  
I can get all of that. Easy.

**BENNETT (nodding)**  
Good.

**Beat.**

**BENNETT (cool, steady)**  
Because weird? We can handle.  *Liars?*  They go to prison.

---

# **“Bonded” – NYPD Precinct, Four Hours Later**

**INT. NYPD PRECINCT – LOBBY – DAWN**

The doors buzz open.  **Madeline Quinlan** walks out slowly, escorted by a pair of plainclothes officers and shadowed by the imposing presence of **Bennett King**, coat folded over one arm, leather briefcase in the other.

She looks like a ghost — drained, trembling, mascara long gone. Her wrists still bear the faint red marks from the cuffs.  She pauses just inside the lobby, blinking against the harsh light.

**BENNETT (quietly)**  
You’re out.

Beat.

**BENNETT (firmer)**  
*On bond.*

**EXT. PRECINCT FRONT STEPS – MOMENTS LATER**

The cold morning hits her as they step outside — city sounds humming low in the background, the distant crackle of early morning radio from a squad car.

**Madeline** stands on the concrete like she’s trying to remember how to be upright.

**BENNETT (cool, clipped)**  
You’ve been charged.

**She turns to him, slowly.**

**MADELINE (weak)**  
With what?

**BENNETT (flat)**  
Felony obstruction.  False identification to a peace officer.  Accessory to a sex crime — they’re floating it, not sticking it yet.

He looks at her for a beat.

**BENNETT**  
Bond was set at **two hundred thousand dollars**.

**MADELINE (softly)**  
Jesus…

**BENNETT (without emotion)**  
You posted it.  Courtesy of your employer — and my negotiation.

**She stares at him, stunned.**

**MADELINE**  
I didn’t even—

**BENNETT (sharper)**  
You don’t need to understand.  You need to follow instructions.  You speak to *no one* unless I say otherwise.

Beat.

**BENNETT (eyeing her)**  
No interviews. No texts. No goddamn Instagram “gratitude posts.”  This is not a redemption arc.  This is survival.

He opens the back door of a waiting black SUV. Madeline climbs in, shaky.  **As the car pulls away,** dawn barely breaks through the Manhattan skyline.  She’s free, for now.

But **she’s been marked.**  And the real fight?  **Has just begun.**

---

### **SCENE CONTINUED: “The Invoice” – SUV, En Route from the Precinct**

**INT. BLACK SUV – EARLY MORNING**

**Madeline** sits silently in the back seat, staring out the window. Her face is drawn, blank, wrists still red. The city is barely stirring outside, and **Bennett King** is beside her — perfectly composed, scrolling through messages on his phone like it’s just another Tuesday.

Then he speaks — not loud, not cruel. Just **pointed**.

**BENNETT (without looking up)**  
Ms. Quinlan…

**She turns slightly.**

**BENNETT (still scrolling)**  
Do you realize what that just cost you?

Beat.

**BENNETT (cool, dry)**  
Doing it the hard way?

**He finally glances at her, just once.**

**BENNETT**  
I just made enough money in the last four hours to buy a **BMW**.

Beat.

**BENNETT (flat)**  
*And not the used one that you drive.*

**Madeline doesn’t speak. Just blinks.**

**BENNETT (calmly)**  
You want to keep making it harder? I can upgrade to the X7.

---

### **SCENE: “Drop Point” – Island Records HQ, Early Morning**

**EXT. ISLAND RECORDS HEADQUARTERS – 5:14 A.M.**

The **black SUV** pulls up to the curb outside the massive glass lobby of Island Records. A security guard inside blinks against the early blue glow of Manhattan’s false dawn.  **Madeline Quinlan** sits still in the back seat, her hands in her lap, hair a mess, face unreadable. There are no reporters — *not yet*. Just a quiet street and the soft murmur of a city waiting to spin back to life.

The SUV door opens.

**BENNETT KING** steps out first. He’s already buttoned up again — immaculate suit, briefcase in one hand.  He doesn’t speak. Doesn’t open her door. Doesn’t need to.

Madeline follows, climbing out slowly. She takes two steps toward the building, then turns— **But he’s already putting on his sunglasses.**

**Yes — at night.**  Dark lenses under the fading stars. A statement, not a fashion choice.  He adjusts them with one hand.

**BENNETT (quiet, final)**  
Don’t screw it up again.

Then he turns.

And just like that, **he disappears** down the street —  into the concrete veins of **the city that never sleeps**, the one place where sins vanish and deals are made in the dark.

**Madeline watches him go.**  Then turns…and walks into Island Records.  Where the **real damage control** is just beginning.

---

# **“Alt Accounts and Meltdowns” – Island Records, Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – JUST BEFORE MIDNIGHT**
