**Avril** stares at the ceiling.  Mouth dry. Lips cracked. Oxygen hissing softly beside her.

**AVRIL (murmuring)**  
The points…don’t matter.  The points don’t matter.

**She repeats it twice. Then again.**

**NURSE #1** pauses mid-note on her tablet, glancing over.

**NURSE #1 (flatly)**  
Okay…how the hell do we document *that*?

**NURSE #2 (deadpan)**  
“Patient demonstrating mild auditory-verbal output. Thematic content: television game show catchphrases.”

**NURSE #1 (typing)**  
Oh, that's *perfectly vague*.  You’ve done this before.

**NURSE #2 (tapping her tablet)**  
I once had a guy come out of a seizure yelling *“Deal or No Deal”*.  Wrote it up as “disoriented but engaging with familiar cultural motifs.”

**They both glance at Avril, who now whispers:**

**AVRIL (soft)**  
I’d like to buy a vowel.

**NURSE #1**  
And now we’re on to Wheel! Terrific.

---

### **SCENE: “Get a Shrink” – Bellevue, ICU Hallway**

**INT. ICU HALLWAY – 11:20 A.M.**

**The shift nurse** catches up to the **attending physician**, clipboard in hand, following him at a brisk walk between rooms.

**NURSE**  
Room 217. Lavigne.  She’s awake, vitals stable, verbal — but she’s been mumbling things.  Weird stuff. TV references. *Whose Line.* *Wheel of Fortune.*

**The attending keeps walking. Doesn’t slow.**

**NURSE (continued)**  
She called Drew Carey “God.”  Then said, “the points don’t matter.”  Now she’s trying to buy a vowel.

**The attending stops just long enough to glance sideways. Three seconds of silence.**

**ATTENDING (flat)**  
Is she lucid?

**NURSE**  
Lucid-adjacent.

**ATTENDING (beat)**  
Okay.  Either she’s **free associating** or **pulling your leg**.

**He resumes walking.**

**ATTENDING (over his shoulder)**  
Get a shrink. Stat consult.  Let them figure out if it’s trauma, irony, or brain damage.

**NURSE (muttering)**  
Great. We’re admitting a celebrity game show philosopher.

---

### **SCENE: “The Outside World Is Watching” – Bellevue ICU, Nurses' Station**

**INT. NURSES' STATION – 11:23 A.M.**

The muttering nurse leans back from her screen.  Still thinking about vowels and showcase showdowns.  She sighs, rubs her face, and glances out the **narrow window** at the far end of the corridor.  And stops.

**Outside, lined up against the curb:**

* **WABC**
* **CBS New York**
* **Fox 5**
* **NBC**
* **CNN**
* **TMZ**

All of them with **parked vans**, **rotating satellite dishes**, **cameramen eating bagels**, and **reporters rehearsing into smartphones**.

**NURSE (flat)**  
Jesus.

She steps closer. Counts. Yup. **Six.**

**NURSE (to herself)**  
They outta roll out the red carpet.

**She glances toward Room 217.**  **Where Avril is still half-whispering about Drew Carey and invisible points.**

**NURSE (muttering)**  
The showcase showdown’s gonna be our careers.

---

# **Data Wants to Be Free” – WikiLeaks Backend Ops, Undisclosed Location**

**INT. DARK SERVER ROOM – TIME UNKNOWN**

Screens glow.  Encrypted tunnels buzz to life.  **The Scan-to-Email system pings** with a new inbound:  **43-page PDF**. Anonymously routed.  Medical format. Labeled *“Patient 217 – Lavigne, Avril”*

**An operator leans in. Reads. Skims. Eyes widen.**

**OPERATOR (V.O., cold, amused)**  
Toxicology.  DNA.  Blood alcohol.  Three semen profiles.  Injection site. Vaginal tearing.  Handcuffs.  Hospital notes.  Timeline.  Free association. Drew Carey as God.

**A second monitor loads up background:**  **News headlines.**  **TV vans outside Bellevue.**  **Twitter trending: “#AvrilAwake”**

**OPERATOR (V.O.)**  
It’s her.  It’s real.  And it’s dynamite.

**Beat. Then, the fork:**

**OPERATOR (V.O.)**  
So… Do we sit on it for years?  Let the world forget?  Or do we **shine a light on it right the fuck now**— **and then ask for donations?**

**His hand hovers over the “Publish Now” button.**  **Another hand reaches over — drops a Bitcoin QR code on the template.**

**OPERATOR (V.O., grin spreading)**  
For great justice… and funding.

**CLICK.**

**FILE UPLOADED.**  **MIRRORED. ARCHIVED. DISSEMINATED.**

**The fuse is now global.**  **And it’s burning.**

---

**SCENE: “Leak Ignition” – The Internet, Everywhere and Nowhere**

**INT. CYBERSPACE – MINUTES AFTER PUBLICATION**

**4CHAN – /POL/ THREAD TITLE: “43-PAGER. WIKI JUST DROPPED IT. LAVIGNE’S TOXIC COCKTAIL.”**

* Attached: A Dropbox mirror.
* File name: *AVRIL217__DISCHARGE-FULL.pdf*
* Comments:
  * “YO WTF.”
  * “This is real. Holy shit.”
  * “3 dudes??”
  * “Handcuffed. They *restrained her.*”
  * “This is snuffcore-level dark.”

**Threads erupt.**  **Images from the document are screencapped, reposted, memed.**  **The *Price is Right* moment is already getting layered into 10 different reaction images.**

---

**REDDIT – r/popculture, r/legaladvice, r/AskDocs, r/Conspiracy – 90 SECONDS LATER**

* **“Can anyone verify this Avril leak from WikiLeaks?”**
* **“Medical ethics experts – what does this mean legally?”**
* **“This isn’t a smear. This is a full-bore data exfiltration. Jesus.”**
* **“Someone find her lawyer. Like… now.”**

Threads explode.  Upvotes surge.  **Mod teams panic.**  Comments toggle between *genuine horror*, *cold analysis*, and *barely concealed voyeurism*.

---

**TWITTER/X – #AvrilLeak #Patient217 #DrewCareyIsGod begin trending in under 6 minutes.**

One tweet: **“I wanted Avril Lavigne’s comeback. Not this.”**

---

**SCENE: “When the Normies Wake Up” – Twitter/X, 10 Minutes Post-Leak**

**INT. GLOBAL SOCIAL MEDIA FEED – 11:42 A.M.**

**First Wave:**

* A **journalist from Rolling Stone** tweets:

“There is a *medical PDF* allegedly leaked via WikiLeaks detailing Avril Lavigne’s ICU condition. It is graphic, horrifying, and clearly authentic. I’ve confirmed two internal sources at Bellevue. This is real. #AvrilLeak”

* **A high-profile legal analyst** posts:

“If this 43-page document is legitimate — and I believe it is — it constitutes one of the worst HIPAA violations in U.S. history. There will be *criminal fallout.*”

* **A cultural critic from The Atlantic** retweets with:

“America: where a woman can be raped, drugged, dehumanized — and her trauma turned into clickbait by breakfast. #Patient217”

---

**Second Wave:**

* **Verified alt accounts start rage-baiting both sides:**

“She OD’d. She partied. Stop pretending she’s innocent.”  
“This is why women don’t report anything.”  
“We’ve replaced compassion with screenshots.”

* **Someone tweets a screenshot of the Drew Carey moment.**  
  **Caption:**

“She woke up. Thought Drew Carey was God. This country is broken.”

---

**Third Wave:**

* **CNN producer posts:**

“We are attempting to verify the contents of the WikiLeaks Avril Lavigne drop. We do *not* recommend viewing the file. Viewer discretion advised.”

* **MSNBC. Fox. BBC. Vice.** All begin assembling **emergency news decks**.  
  Some **anchor’s assistant is in a Starbucks bathroom reading this on their phone** while DMing their editor.

---

**And somewhere inside Bellevue, a junior PR staffer opens Twitter,**  
**sees the trending tab,**  **and says softly:**

**“Oh… no.”**

---

**SCENE: “The Silence Cascade” – Island Records HQ, Social Ops Room**

**INT. SOCIAL OPERATIONS – 12:03 P.M.**

**CREMEANS** sits in front of six monitors, each displaying real-time bot activity.

Every one of his **pseudo-intellectual digital constructs** — his **Twitter bots**, his **Reddit debaters**, his **engagement AIs** — are starting to fail.

**SYSTEM STATUS WINDOW:**

* @SongbirdDiscourse: *Nonresponsive*

* @CommutedCentral: *Thread abandoned*

* @ARealCritic: *Argument chain ended*

* @AvrilFansUnited: *No activity in 11 minutes*

* @AI_EngageMod: *Core script exited*

**CREMEANS (murmuring)**  
No. No no no… keep going… redirect.  
Pivot to trauma support. Pivot to privacy ethics.

**He types commands.**  
**Failsafes. Manual prompts.**  
**Nothing responds.**

One by one, the bots revert to **default behavior**:  
**Do. Nothing.**

**CREMEANS (to himself)**  
You’re built for heat. For rage. For rapidfire opinion control.  
Why the hell aren’t you doing anything?

On screen:  
A blinking message in a backend console line.

*“Insufficient moral heuristic to resolve contradiction between public narrative and private data breach.”*  
*“Defaulting to silence.”*

**CREMEANS (staring at it)**  
Oh God.  
You’re human now.

---

**SCENE: “Reboot the Army” – Island Records HQ, 12:34 P.M.**

**INT. SOCIAL OPS HUB – ALONE.**

**CREMEANS** stands in front of his AI stack.  
The 43-page file pulses in a command window.  
A loading bar has just hit 100%.

**SCREEN:**  
*AI PROCESSING COMPLETE. GENERATING RESPONSE TREE…*  
*Estimated runtime: 12.7 seconds.*

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
You’ve seen it all now.

**The screen flickers.**  
**Then begins spitting out headlines:**

* **USE CASE 01: "Trauma Is Not Tabloid – Defending Dignity Online"**

* **USE CASE 06: "Countering Weaponized Voyeurism – Deploy Bots with Empathy Mode 3.1"**

* **USE CASE 12: "Shift Blame to HIPAA Breach – Elevate Institutional Accountability"**

* **USE CASE 18: "Invoke Celebrity Vulnerability Archetypes (cf. Britney, Demi, Kesha)"**

* **USE CASE 24: "Exploit Male Guilt Gaps – Target Progressive Subreddits"**

* **USE CASE 30: "Crowdsource Compassion: Launch #ProtectAvril Hashtag Storm"**

**CREMEANS copies the entire payload.**  
**Pushes it to the Twitter bot backbone.**

**CREMEANS (calmly)**  
Execute.  
Re-engage.  
1PM sharp.

**The AI replies:**

*“Confirmed. Uploading across 217 nodes.”*

---

**1:00 P.M. – TWITTER BEGINS TO SHIFT.**

Dozens of new voices emerge:  
Polite. Concerned.  
Woke, but firm.  
Blending fact, feeling, and subtle deflection.

**The band is still silent.**  
But their digital army?

**It has found its voice again.**  
**And this time, it’s been trained by trauma.**

---

**SCENE: “Waiting for Sarah” – Island Records, 14th Floor Conference Room**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – 14TH FLOOR – 1:11 P.M.**

**The elevator chimes.**

**Bill, Jim, Jeff, and Jeremy** walk out like they’ve just crawled out of a trench.  
No one speaks.  No one jokes.  They’re too tired to be angry, too raw to be numb.

They push through the double doors into the conference room.

And sitting there —  **alone**,  **steady**,  **unsmiling** —  is **Madeline Quinlan**.

Her red heels are kicked off beneath the table.  Her blouse is rumpled.  
Her eyes? **Sharp. Focused. Dangerous.**

In front of her:

* A tray with **five coffee mugs**

* A carafe of fresh black coffee

* A pitcher of **ice-cold milk**

* No fanfare. No donuts. No hope.

**Madeline looks up. Doesn’t smile. Doesn’t speak.**

Just a nod.

**Bill** pours first.  
Then **Jim**.  
**Jeff and Jeremy** follow.  
Nobody uses a coaster.

**Madeline (quietly, without looking up)**  
Sarah’s on her way.

**The four men sit.**  
**The air is thick.**  
**The weight of the leak, the silence, the blood, the bots, and the goddamn rats still hangs in their lungs.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Floor Drops Out” – Island Records Conference Room, 14th Floor**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:14 P.M.**

The four men sit.

The coffee is bitter.  
The milk barely cuts it.  
The silence is just beginning to feel safe.

**MADELINE** opens her laptop.  
Spins it gently around.  
The screen is showing a **dashboard** — media velocity graphs, engagement curves, sentiment heatmaps.

All were **spiking**.

Then at 11:37 AM?  
**They crater.**

**MADELINE (quietly)**  
You were holding decently.  
Even with everything… the narrative was fractured, but manageable.

**She taps the screen.**  
**Zooms in on the dip.**  
**Dead center. 11:37 A.M.**

**MADELINE**  
And then WikiLeaks happened.

**The room freezes.**  
**Four sets of eyes turn to her.**

**BILL (flat)**  
What?

**MADELINE**  
Avril’s medical records.  
All 43 pages.

**JIM (blinking)**  
The whole file?

**MADELINE (nods once)**  
Toxicology. Injuries. Notes.  
The restraint order.  
The part about the rats.

**JEFF** leans back in his chair like he just got sucker-punched.

**JEREMY (soft)**  
You’re not serious.

**MADELINE (looking at all of them)**  
It’s already mirrored to over a hundred sites.  
Indexed. Parsed. Screenshotted.  
Reddit’s on fire. 4chan’s gone nuclear.  
Twitter… well… Twitter is Twitter.

**The screen updates.**  
**A graph pulses upward: #AvrilLeak trending in 41 countries.**

**MADELINE (softly)**  
They know everything.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “I Want to See It” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:17 P.M.**

The silence lingers.  
A few heartbeats too long.

Then **Jeff** sets his coffee down with a clink.  
Leans forward.  
Jaw clenched.

**JEFF**  
I want to read the file.

**Everyone looks at him.**

**JEFF (firm)**  
I’m not going off Reddit threads and media spin.  
I'm going to make my own opinion.  
There's no way 43 pages is her entire medical record.  
There's no way it's got enough data to wreck her.

**Madeline doesn’t argue.**  
**Doesn’t warn.**  
**Just tilts her laptop toward him.**  
**Clicks open the document.**

**MADELINE (flat)**  
Page one. Triage summary.

**She pushes the laptop across the table.**  
**Jeff pulls it toward him.**

He starts to read.

* **Blood alcohol: 0.23**

* **Methamphetamine. Amphetamine. Cocaine.**

* **Three unique semen samples.**

* **Tearing. Restraints.**

* **Delirium. Injection sites.**

* **Disassociation. Fugue state. Drew Carey as God.**

**JEFF (reading softly)**  
Jesus…

He flips to page 2. Then 3.  
His brow furrows.  
Color drains from his face.

**He’s only on page 7\.**  
**He closes the laptop.**  
**Hard.**

**JEFF (quiet)**  
It indicts her.

**No one says anything.**  
**They don't have to.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Legal Strategy, Meet Reality” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:21 P.M.**

**Jeff** is still sitting with the weight of the file on his chest.  
**Bill** and **Jeremy** are frozen.  
**Jim** hasn’t said a word.

**BILL (tentative)**  
So… has the lawyer seen it?

**MADELINE** doesn’t look up.  
She’s already halfway through typing a comms bullet list.

**MADELINE (flat)**  
He most certainly has.

**JEFF (hopeful, stupid)**  
So what’s the plan? Can we issue a takedown?

**MADELINE (still typing)**  
He advised us not to touch it.

**JEREMY** frowns.

**JEREMY**  
Not touch it?

**MADELINE**  
As in, do not acknowledge.  
Do not confirm.  
Do not chase it.

**She stops typing. Finally looks up.**

**MADELINE (with edge)**  
We could start firing off cease and desist letters.  
We’ve already got draft templates.  
But they’re about as effective as a screen door on a space shuttle.

**She lets that sit.**  
**Lets them picture it: all that pressure, all that exposure…**  
**with nothing holding it back.**

**MADELINE (lower, bitter)**  
Every copy you kill, three more go up.  
The Streisand effect is already in full bloom.  
And besides — it’s real.  
They’re not faking this. They’re just…  
**broadcasting it.**

---

**SCENE: “Cremeans Arrives” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:25 P.M.**

The tension is molten.  
Madeline’s gone still.  
Jeff’s still shaken from the file.  
No one’s drinking their coffee anymore.

**The door opens.**  
**Cremeans walks in.**

* **Mountain Dew in his left hand**

* **Another tucked under his arm like a football**

* **A sad-looking plastic bag slung from his wrist** (probably beef jerky, possibly despair)

He doesn’t look at anyone.

Just trudges to the table.  
Drops into the nearest chair like a sack of programming code that just crashed.

**CREMEANS (softly)**  
I know.  
I know.

**He opens the bag.**  
**Pulls out a third Mountain Dew.**  
**Offers it to no one.**  
**No one accepts.**

**CREMEANS (continued)**  
I’ve been up for 42 hours.  
I tried to get ahead of it.  
I tried every counter-narrative in the book.

**He takes a long sip.**  
**The kind of sip that says “I’m going to die with this brand in my blood.”**

**CREMEANS (flatly)**  
But the internet decided to read this one for itself.

**Silence. The guys just stare.**  
**He doesn’t need to elaborate.**

---

**SCENE: “No One to Hang” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:28 P.M.**

The silence stretches thin.  
Cremeans sips his soda. Madeline watches the graphs tick upward.  
Everyone is **simmering**.

**BILL (suddenly, sharp)**  
Then we hang the person.  
The leaker.  
We go after them.  
We make an example.

**JEFF (quiet, resigned)**  
It was from WikiLeaks.

**BILL** turns to him. Waiting for hope.

**JEFF (shaking his head)**  
They’ve definitely taken measures.  
Dead drops. Mirrors. Layers of anonymity.

**He looks down.**

**JEFF (soft)**  
This isn’t a whistleblower we can dox.  
This is digital acid.  
It’s already eaten through everything.

**CREMEANS (half-muttering)**  
I found six mirrors before I even had coffee.

**JEREMY (quietly)**  
And once it’s on 4chan? Reddit?  
It’s not leaking anymore.  
It’s… airborne.

**Bill exhales hard. Puts both palms on the table.  
No target. No one to punch.  
Just **rage with nowhere to go.**

**MADELINE (without looking up)**  
We can still try to trace the leak internally.  
But even if we do…  
They didn’t break her.  
They just lit the match.

**No one disagrees.**  
**Because they all know who’s in that hospital bed.**

And they all know what she’s been doing for the last seven days.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Don’t Sue the Iceberg” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:30 P.M.**

**Bill** is still vibrating with fury.  
**Jeff** is staring into middle distance.  
**Jeremy** is nursing his guilt quietly.

Then **Jim** — who hasn’t said much at all — leans forward.

**JIM (calmly)**  
We don’t need to find the leaker.

**Everyone turns to look at him.**  
**Bill’s about to protest, but Jim raises a hand.**

**JIM (continued)**  
That’s like punishing the iceberg when the Titanic hits it.

**Beat.**

**JIM (cool, flat)**  
Nope.  
We go after the hospital.

**MADELINE (measured)**  
Bellevue?

**JIM (nods)**  
They’re the institution.  
They held the records.  
They had the duty of care.

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
HIPAA. Civil. Criminal.

**JIM** sips his coffee. Finally.

**JIM**  
We go after them for negligence.  
Recklessness.  
Failure to secure private information.

**JEFF (shaking his head)**  
We’d have to prove it came from inside.

**JIM (still calm)**  
We don’t have to prove it in court.  
We just have to prove it on TV.

---

**SCENE: “The General Arrives” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:34 P.M.**

The door swings open.

**SARAH MALCOLM** storms in — no coat, no patience, no time for mourning.  
She’s got a tablet in one hand, her phone in the other, and her **rage weaponized with purpose.**

She hears Jim’s line as she enters:

*“We just have to prove it on TV.”*

She doesn’t miss a beat.

**SARAH (sharp, loud)**  
Proving it on TV is the **truest goddamn thing** any of you fucks have said in the last seven days.

**Everyone turns.**  
**Even Madeline raises an eyebrow.**

**SARAH (to the room)**  
We’re not suing for justice.  
We’re suing for control.  
You don’t win by being right.  
You win by being *louder* and *faster* and *meaner* than anyone else who’s telling your story for you.

**She drops her tablet on the table — screen filled with news alerts, trending tags, and a blinking live feed counter.**

**SARAH (cool, lethal)**  
So get ready.  
Because if we’re gonna hang someone,  
**we're doing it with a camera crew.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “You’re Going to Say What I Tell You” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:36 P.M.**

The tension has shifted.  
Not fear anymore — **strategy. Fire. Revenge.**

Sarah stands at the head of the table now, phone in one hand, media brief in the other.

She points at **Jim** like she’s selecting her next chess piece.

**SARAH**  
Jim, I never knew you were fluent in Korean.

**JIM (wry)**  
I’m not. I just pissed off an entire hemisphere by accident.

**SARAH (deadpan)**  
Well, this time you’re gonna do it *on purpose* —  
and you’re gonna do it with **talking points.**

**She slides a folder across the table — branded, sharp, color-coded tabs.**

**SARAH (continued)**  
You’re the human face of our apology tour.  
You’re relatable.  
You’re funny.  
And — most importantly — you didn’t end up in a holding cell or leak a single thing.

**JIM (eyeing the folder)**  
So I’m the clean one?

**SARAH (nods)**  
You’re the **least radioactive**.  
That’s as close as we get to “clean” right now.

**She opens the folder for him.**

**SARAH (pointed)**  
These are your lines.  
You stay warm, you stay humble, and you don’t improvise.  
Not unless you want to start a diplomatic incident again.

**Cremeans mutters into his Mountain Dew.**

**CREMEANS**  
At least say something nice about bulgogi this time.

**SARAH (without turning)**  
Cremeans, drink your sugar and stay out of this.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Language of Masturbation” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:38 P.M.**

**Sarah** stands poised like a general mid-campaign.  
**Jim** flips open the talking points folder with mild dread.

He gives it five seconds.

Then sighs. Leans back in his chair.

**JIM (dryly)**  
You know, everything I learned about Korean came from *manhwa*.

**SARAH (instantly suspicious)**  
…What kind of manhwa?

**JIM (deadpan)**  
The dirty kind.

**He sips his coffee. Lets that hang.**

**JIM (continued)**  
So I’m… *somewhat fluent* in the language of masturbation.

**A beat.**

**Cremeans snorts loudly. Jeremy chokes on his drink. Jeff leans his forehead against the table. Bill mutters “Jesus Christ.”**

Even **Madeline** cracks the faintest smile.

**SARAH (rubbing her eyes)**  
Okay.  
New rule.  
No ad-libbing.  
You get one joke. You just spent it.  
Next one costs us Seoul.

**JIM (grinning now)**  
Worth it.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “One Extinction Event” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:42 P.M.**

The room has quieted again.  
Jim’s joke has faded. Sarah’s back to organizing the next media blitz.  
But **Cremeans** leans forward. Mountain Dew half-drained, eyes red but lucid.

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
Y’know…

**Everyone looks over. He rarely speaks without sarcasm.**

**CREMEANS (continued)**  
Most bands?  
They get to survive **one** extinction-level event.  
One implosion.  
One scandal.  
One death.

**Beat.**

**CREMEANS**  
We’re on number two.  
And that’s not even counting the pre-tour overdose, or the livestream meltdown, or the… whatever that was in Chicago.

**He looks over at Jeff. Just for a second.**

**CREMEANS (soft)**  
Last time was Kathy.  
She just went into rehab.  
Just for a check-in.  
And then she had a… she had a—

**He stops.**  
**Can’t finish.**  
**Doesn’t have to.**

**The silence lands like a thunderclap.**  
**No one moves.**

**JEREMY (hollow)**  
Stroke.

**CREMEANS (nodding)**  
Yeah.

**He doesn’t say anything else.**  
**Because they all know.**  
**Because this isn’t a press strategy anymore.**  
**This is life and death — again.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “If You Had Acted in ‘98” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:45 P.M.**

**Cremeans** is still quiet.  
Still hearing Kathy’s name in his ears like an echo.

**Jeremy**, suddenly too tired to keep it in anymore, turns to him — voice tight, low, barely a tremor away from something sharper.

**JEREMY**  
If you would’ve acted that night.  
**Ninety-eight.**  
When *120 Minutes* happened.  
When she OD’d in the green room.

**Cremeans looks up. Slowly.**

**JEREMY (continued)**  
If you had taken her to a hospital instead of a hotel room—  
*Maybe* we wouldn’t be here.

**Silence.**  
**The accusation isn’t shouted.**  
**It’s worse.**  
**It’s calm.**

**CREMEANS (quietly)**  
I thought she needed to sleep it off.  
Everyone did back then.

**JEREMY** doesn’t blink. Doesn’t flinch.

**JEFF (interrupting, firmly)**  
That’s an *alternate history*, man.

**JEREMY** turns toward him. Not hostile — just raw.

**JEFF (continued)**  
You can’t map it like that.  
It’s not *cause and effect*.  
It’s not dominoes.

**He gestures vaguely — as if trying to summon the chaos in the air.**

**JEFF**  
There are too many variables.  
You change one thing and you don’t get a better outcome —  
you get a different catastrophe.

**JEFF (continued)**  
First-order effects, second-order effects…  
You don’t *fix* a life by running a better simulation.

**CREMEANS (flatly)**  
And you can’t go back and delete the save file.

**Silence.**  
**Heavy.**  
**A quiet reckoning.**

No one speaks.  
Because **they’ve all got blood on their hands**, one way or another.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Eyes Forward” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:50 P.M.**

**Cremeans** straightens up.  
Still pale.  
Still hollow-eyed.  
But now… back in motion.

**CREMEANS**  
Look, guys.

**He grabs the remote. Switches the screen back to the marketing calendar.**

**CREMEANS (continued)**  
We’ve got to get *“To Show Who We Are”* out the door **this year**.  
That’s the story. That’s the brand. That’s *the spine* of the campaign.

**He clicks forward.**

* A date: *October 14 – Box Set Final Pressing Deadline*

* A logo: *TO SHOW WHO WE ARE – A Retrospective*

**CREMEANS**  
And the box set? That supports the **miniseries**.  
The shelves. The streamers. The reissue vinyl.  
We need the **narrative** ready.  
Because that’s how we frame this whole mess.

**He exhales. Looks at them.**  
**No more jokes. Just reality.**

**CREMEANS (softly)**  
We have to be strategic here.

**Then, as if catching himself — a faint, almost sheepish smile.**

**CREMEANS**  
…Thanks for watching.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Creative Fallout” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:53 P.M.**

**Cremeans** takes a deep breath, steadies himself, and rephrases.

**CREMEANS**  
Okay. Let me back that up—

**He taps the screen again.**  
**Slides to the “Q4 Rollout Strategy” deck.**  
**Up comes the title:**  
***To Show Who We Are – New Double Album***  
**October 2025\.**

**CREMEANS (continued)**  
"To Show Who We Are" isn’t just a title.  
It was **the statement**.  
A double album. First really huge one in almost fifteen years.  
And we finally—**finally**—had something *real* again.

**He looks around the table.**  
**Serious now. No deflection.**

**CREMEANS**  
Avril wasn’t a guest.  
She wasn’t a novelty.  
She was a **strategic contributor**.  
Vocals. Lyrics. Hooks. Conceptual shape.  
She had a hand in the creative DNA.  
We were locked in. It was **electric**.

**He flips to the next slide.**  
**Artwork mockups. Tour projections. Hashtags.**

**CREMEANS (continued)**  
The second project — the **box set** — that’s the *documentary* side.  
It’s going to support the **miniseries**.

**He gestures.**

**CREMEANS**  
The compilation of unused material. Demo tapes.  
Rejected, recycled, warped-over sessions from *To Show Who We Are*.  
That’s **"I Can Take It"**. The whole concept.

**He lowers his voice.**

**CREMEANS**  
It was going to be the **sound of survival**.  
Of failure repurposed.  
Now… we’re dangerously close to turning it into an elegy.

---

**SCENE: “The Motion” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 1:58 P.M.**

The room is buzzing with the weight of Cremeans’ presentation.  
The album. The docuseries. The narrative.

**Then Bill leans back. Crosses his arms.**  
**And drops the bomb.**

**BILL (flat, even)**  
We fire her.

**Everyone freezes.**  
**Cremeans actually blinks.**  
**Madeline looks up. Jeff stiffens.**

**BILL (continued)**  
She’s gone off the rails.  
She’s become a liability.  
She’s threatening the work, the project, the whole fucking thing.

**Beat. He looks at no one in particular.**

**BILL**  
So I’m proposing a motion.  
Under the band’s principles.

**He looks at Jim, Jeremy, Jeff. Pointedly.**

**BILL (firm)**  
This is *our* vote.  
Our call.  
Everyone else can butt out.

**Silence. The room shifts cold.**  
**No shouting. Just stillness.**

**JEFF (quietly)**  
You're serious.

**BILL**  
Dead serious.

**SARAH (interjecting, measured)**  
Bill—this isn't the time for—

**BILL (cutting her off)**  
Not your call.  
This is *band business*.  
**Blood-in, blood-out**.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “This Album Has Power” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:01 P.M.**

The tension hangs thick after Bill's motion.

**Jeff** sets his coffee down with a quiet *thud*.  
He looks across the table at Bill. Not angry. Just deeply, deeply disappointed.

**JEFF (measured, low)**  
You’ve hated her from the beginning.

**Bill stiffens.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
So I gotta ask—  
Why did you even save her life?

**Beat.**  
**No one speaks.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
You’ve read the lyrics, man.  
You’ve seen what she’s been putting in the margins.  
You’ve heard the demos. The way she threads chaos into melody.

**He leans forward. Voice rising, but never shouting.**

**JEFF**  
This double album—  
*This thing we’ve been building*—  
It has **power**.

**He scans the room. Looks each of them in the eye.**

**JEFF**  
It’s gonna kill.  
Not because it’s polished. Not because it’s clean.  
Because it’s raw. Because it’s brutal. Because it’s **true**.

**He taps the side of his head.**

**JEFF**  
It’s all in here right now.  
In notebooks. On scraps. In our fucking heads.

**He nods toward Cremeans.**

**JEFF**  
All we have to do is get it onto tape.  
Just. Get. It. Out.

**He looks back at Bill. Final beat.**

**JEFF**  
You can’t throw that away because you’re scared of where it came from.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “What She Can’t Have” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:06 P.M.**

**Jeremy** hasn’t spoken much.  
But now, he sits forward, arms on the table, and says it flat.

**JEREMY (quietly, with weight)**  
Nope.

**Everyone turns to him.**  
**He doesn’t blink. Doesn’t flinch.**

**JEREMY (continued)**  
This was working.  
This band, this project—  
It was all working *pretty good*…

**His eyes cut sharply across the table.**  
**Right at Jeff.**

**JEREMY**  
Until Avril became obsessed with what she couldn’t have.

**A beat of silence.**  
**Jeff doesn’t look away.**  
**But he doesn’t respond either.**

**JEREMY (continued)**  
And now?  
We’re here.

**He exhales. Runs a hand over his face.**

**JEREMY**  
Look, if we can get her real treatment—  
**Proper medical care.**  
If we can get her what she deserves, *actually deserves*—

**He pauses.**

**JEREMY**  
I don’t even know what that means in Canada.  
How they handle… this.

**He gestures vaguely at the air.**

**JEREMY**  
Severe mental health. Addiction. Disassociation.  
Does she go to a psych ward? A rehab facility?  
Do they medicate her? Detain her?  
*Does anybody even fucking know how Canada handles this?*

**Silence.**  
**No one answers.**  
**Because the truth is: they don’t know.**

**They’ve built albums. Managed crises. Played stadiums.**  
**But they have no clue how to save a human being.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “How Canada Handles the Broken” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:10 P.M.**

**Silence after Jeremy’s question.**  
No one wants to answer.  
But **Madeline** clears her throat — quiet, firm, focused.

**MADELINE**  
They’ll assess her under the Mental Health Act.  
Every province has its own version, but they all have the same backbone.

**All eyes turn to her. She doesn’t flinch.**

**MADELINE (continued)**  
She’ll go into what they call a **Form 1 psychiatric hold** — usually 72 hours, sometimes longer.  
They’ll determine if she’s a danger to herself, or others, or just incapable of caring for herself.

**Beat.**

**MADELINE**  
If they deem her too far gone — delusional, addicted, suicidal —  
they can extend the hold. Form 3.  
That’s two weeks.  
They’ll medicate her. Stabilize her. Possibly restrain her.

**She glances at Jeff. Her tone softens, but only slightly.**

**MADELINE**  
They won’t throw her in a padded room.  
But they *will* put her somewhere sterile.  
Clinical.  
Safe.  
With laminated walls and white blankets.  
No belts. No shoelaces.  
No music.

**A pause. No one breathes.**

**MADELINE (continued)**  
She’ll be evaluated by a tribunal.  
If they think she’s improving, they’ll release her to outpatient care.  
If she backslides…  
they can renew the hold.  
Again. And again.

**She looks at them, all of them.**

**MADELINE (lower, razor-edged)**  
Canadians don’t let you die in the street.  
But they don’t sing you back to life either.

**Beat.**

**MADELINE**  
They observe.  
They document.  
They hold the sunburned ones at arm’s length…  
until they either heal, or fade.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Which System Do You Trust?” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:13 P.M.**

**Jeremy** leans forward, elbows on knees, hands clasped tight.

**JEREMY (quiet, even)**  
So.

**He looks at Madeline, then across the table at Jeff, Bill, Sarah. One by one.**

**JEREMY (continued)**  
Do you want to sentence her to that?

**A pause. No one breathes.**

**JEREMY**  
Canada.  
Tribunals.  
Sterile rooms.  
Stability over soul.

**He lets that sit. Then tilts his head.**

**JEREMY**  
Or do you want to try the American system?  
Right here.  
New York City.

**He shrugs slowly.**

**JEREMY**  
Where you get **48 hours on a gurney**, maybe.  
Where psych holds are overcrowded, underfunded, and **loud as hell**.  
Where she’ll be monitored by guards with zip ties, not doctors with clipboards.  
Where being famous just makes you more **dangerous** to everyone around you.

**Beat. His voice drops.**

**JEREMY**  
Do we try that?

**The table is silent.**  
**The weight of either answer crushing them all.**

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “There Are Two Sets of Rules” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:16 P.M.**

The tension is unbearable.

**Jeff** stands up slowly, looking not at the table, but through it — past the fear, past the bureaucracy, into the engine room of real power.

**JEFF (low, but rising)**  
There are two sets of rules.

**The others glance at him.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
Rules for *us*…  
And rules for *everyone else*.

**He paces once, just enough to burn off the fury underneath.**

**JEFF**  
So we’re going to solve this the way we always do—  
when we’re cornered, when we’re taking it up the ass—  
we’re going to do what this band *does* when the walls close in.

**Beat.**

**JEFF (hard)**  
We open up our goddamn bank accounts…

**He leans forward, voice sharp now, pulsing with purpose.**

**JEFF**  
…and we **start shoveling out cash.**

**Cremeans looks up, startled.**  
**Bill narrows his eyes.**  
**Madeline watches carefully.**  
**Sarah goes very still.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
Private care. Off-books facilities.  
The best shrinks. The best handlers.  
The best lawyers in two countries and the best rehab money can buy.

**He pauses.**

**JEFF (softer, but firm)**  
I’ll be a billionaire before the decade is out.  
It’s time I start acting like it.

---

**SCENE: “I Told You So” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:20 P.M.**

**Jeff** is still on his feet, still simmering from his *"I’ll be a billionaire"* speech.

But now?

**He’s done playing nice.**

He points across the table — at **Bill**.

**JEFF (cutting, precise)**  
If you would’ve done what I said in ‘98—  
when *120 Minutes* imploded and we needed to rebuild instead of retreat—  
we wouldn’t be here.

**Bill blinks. Jeff steps in.**

**JEFF (harder now)**  
If you would’ve done what I said at the start of the Obama administration,  
we’d have turned the brand into a lifestyle label.

**He’s not ranting.**  
**He’s dropping cold, tactical history.**

**JEFF**  
If you’d listened to me about social media  
instead of treating it like a fucking flash mob,  
maybe we wouldn’t be *a punchline in 17 languages* right now.

**He leans in. Pointed. Surgical.**

**JEFF (lower)**  
And if you’d gotten your prick *out of the windmill industry* long enough  
to read a quarterly report?  
Maybe you’d be well and truly rich right about now.

**Beat. No one speaks.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
Some of us read P\&L statements.  
Some of us short ESG and *build empires*.

**He stares Bill down.**

**JEFF (dead serious)**  
One of us is about to be a billionaire.  
The other one makes the rubble bounce  
and the banks quake when they show up with **two tons of gold and a press release.**

**The silence is absolute.**  
**Even Madeline looks up from her laptop.**  
**Sarah exhales. Loud.**

**SARAH (muttering)**  
Goddamn it, not again.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Main Gig” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:23 P.M.**

The tension lingers after Jeff’s fire-breathing rejection of ESG and the windmill crowd.  
The room feels radioactive.

**But Jeff’s not done.**

He takes a breath, steadies, and speaks softer now — not less intense, just more *true*.

**JEFF (measured)**  
Saving souls?

**He shrugs.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
Sure. That’s my **side gig**.

**Some chuckles. A few. Nervous. Dry.**  
**But then he steps forward again, eyes lit. Voice tightening with passion.**

**JEFF**  
But I *never* lose track of the **main gig**.

**Beat.**

**JEFF (building)**  
My job—  *My mission*—  is translating art into music.

**He paces, slower now. Intentional.**

**JEFF**  
Music into fame.  Fame into ticket sales.  And ticket sales?

**He looks around the table, dead in their eyes.**

**JEFF (quiet)**  
Into joy.

**The room goes still.**  
**Because that?**  
**That’s the fucking** thesis.

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Look at the Houses” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:26 P.M.**

**Bill** can’t take it anymore.

**BILL (exploding)**  
I’ve got a very different take on things, Jeff!

**The room jolts.**  
**Sarah closes her eyes like she’s been waiting for this.**

**Jeff?**  **Doesn’t raise his voice.**  **Doesn’t blink.**

**JEFF (even)**  
I can respect that, Bill.

**Beat.**

**JEFF (quiet, lethal)**  
But look at the size of our houses.

**Bill’s jaw clenches.**

**JEFF (calm)**

**He steps closer. Not threatening — surgical.**

**JEFF**  
This is the result of *decisions*.  Of turning noise into movement.  Of putting *strategy* above *sentiment*.

**Beat.**

**JEFF (lower)**  
We’re not here because we feel.  We’re here because we *build*.

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Reset the Tempo” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:29 P.M.**

**The room is scorched.**  Bill’s still bristling.  Jeff is still standing.  Everyone’s on the verge of burnout or bloodshed.

**Then Jim speaks. Calm. Grounded.**

**JIM (measured)**  
Alright, alright—  this is wandering all over the fucking place.

**He sits forward. Not angry. Just done.**

**JIM**  
We’re here to deal with what Bill said.

**A pause.**

**JIM (continued)**

**He sighs. Runs a hand through his hair.**

**JIM**

**He gestures, vaguely — the studio, the rehearsal space, the memory.**

**JIM**  
I haven’t had this much *fun* since the final days of the 20th century.

**He pulls out his phone. Checks the calendar. Deadpan.**

**JIM (mutters)**  
And seeing as it’s 2024…

**He looks up. Shrugs.**

**JIM**  
That’s a long-ass time to be at a job where half the days I’m just going through the motions.

**Beat. He looks at everyone.**

**JIM (softly)**  
She woke something up.

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Motion Fails” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:33 P.M.**

**The room is quiet.**  **Jim’s words hang in the air like smoke from a snuffed-out fire.**

Then **Bill speaks**.  Gravel in his throat.  Pride still intact.  But the edge… dulled just enough.

**BILL (gruffly)**  
I’m voting against my own motion.

**Everyone turns. Even Jeff blinks.**  **Bill doesn’t look at anyone. He just says it.**

**BILL (continued)**  
Because I value *unanimity*.  Always have.  Even when it tastes like shit.

**He exhales. Taps the table once, then adds—flat, emotionless:**

**BILL**  
But she’s still a **cunt**.

**Cremeans half-chokes on his Mountain Dew.**  **Madeline just mutters, “Jesus.”**  **Sarah pinches the bridge of her nose, but doesn’t argue.**

**JIM (without looking up)**  
That’s probably the nicest thing you’ve ever said about her.

**BILL (shrugs)**  
Yeah. Well.  You’re welcome.

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Sarah’s Turn” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:35 P.M.**

**The tension settles.**  
**The motion is dead.**  
**Bill has growled out his olive branch laced with a slur.**  
**Everyone is just… sitting.**

**Then Sarah speaks.**  
**Deadpan.**  
**One eyebrow raised.**  
**Voice like ice water in a whiskey glass.**

Are we allowed to talk now, guys?

**Silence.**  
**Even Cremeans sits up straighter.**  
**Jeff scratches the back of his neck.**  
**Bill doesn’t look up.**  
**Madeline grins, just barely.**

**SARAH (continued)**  
Or should we give you all a few more minutes to measure your pricks?

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Motion Fails” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:37 P.M.**

The silence lingers after Sarah’s careful question.

Then **Bill**, voice quieter than usual, picks it back up.

**BILL (flat, procedural)**  
All in favor of the motion, say aye.

**Silence. Not a breath.**  
**Not a single “aye.”**

**BILL (nods once)**  
Votes against?

**JEFF**  
Nay.

**JIM**  
Nay.

**JEREMY**  
Nay.

**BILL (sighs, mutters)**  
Four nays.  
Motion is failed.

**He leans back, eyes half-closed, and gestures across the table.**

**BILL (continued)**  
Okay.

**He looks at Sarah. Direct. No sarcasm. No edge. Just real.**

**BILL**  
Sarah.  
You were saying?

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Step One Is Avril” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:39 P.M.**

**Sarah** stands slowly.  
No dramatics. Just presence.

Legally—

Get access.

Psychological. Medical. Emotional.

**For *her*.**

Yeah. That’s right.

**SARAH (nods once)**  
Good.

**She exhales, sets her tablet down.**

**SARAH (firm)**  
Step one.  
Is *Avril*.

**SCENE: “Cold as Ice” – Island Records Conference Room**

**INT. CONFERENCE ROOM – 2:42 P.M.**

Sarah has just centered the room with one clear truth:

*Step one is Avril.*

Silence.

Then **Madeleine** speaks.  
Voice like polished steel.

**MADELEINE (calm)**  
This will drive sales.

**Instant tension.**  
**The band stares—glares, really.**  
**Bill looks like he’s ready to flip the table.**  
**Even Jim goes still.**  
**Jeff’s jaw tightens.**

But Madeleine?

**Unfazed.**  
**Unapologetic.**  
**Cold.**

**MADELEINE (dead serious)**  
If. She. Lives.

**A long beat.**  
**The room doesn’t breathe.**  
**But she does.**  
**Slowly. Deliberately.**

You’re thinking in terms of *what’s right*.  
I’m thinking in terms of *what works*.

**She takes a slow step forward.**  
**Not defensive—predatory.**

**MADELEINE**  
You save her?  
You build the story.  
You get the photos, the docuseries, the liner notes that drip with scars and survival.  
You turn the wreckage into a resurrection.

**She scans the table.**

**MADELEINE (cold)**  
But if she dies?  
You get a moment.  
A headline.  
A cautionary tale.

**She shrugs. One shoulder. Impeccably calm.**

I don’t sell cautionary tales.  
I sell legacy.  
I sell control.  
I sell *icons who get back up*.

**Cremeans mutters under his breath.**  
**Jeff doesn’t say a word.**  
**Bill stares at her like he just met her for the first time.**

**MADELEINE (final)**  
You can hate me for saying it.  
But you’ll thank me for making the call.

**SCENE: “Breather in the Bowery” – Night**

**INT. DIVE BAR – THE BOWERY – LATE EVENING**

Low light. Slow jazz from a corner speaker.  
Nobody here’s trying to impress anyone.  
The kind of bar where even the walls feel like they’ve seen too much and won’t tell a soul.

**Bill** and **Jeff** sit at the bar.  
Two fingers of **very expensive bourbon** in front of each.  
No entourage. No noise. Just… a breather.

**BILL (gruff, quiet)**  
That girl of yours… Madeleine.  
She’s a goddamn ice sculpture.

**JEFF (without looking over)**  
Yeah.  
She’s gonna run a Fortune 50 one day.  
Or get us all indicted. Not sure which yet.

**They sip. Long pause. A hint of a smile on Bill’s face.**

**BILL**  
You really think we’re gonna be billionaires?

**JEFF (softly)**  
No.

**He turns to look Bill dead in the eye.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
I know we already are.

**Bill grunts. Raises his glass in mock salute.**

**BILL**  
Well.  
Here’s to surviving the apocalypse.

**JEFF**  
No, man.

**He clinks Bill’s glass gently.**

**JEFF (quiet, final)**  
Here’s to crawling out of it.

**SCENE CONTINUED: “The Succession Question” – Bar in the Bowery**

**INT. DIVE BAR – NIGHT**

**Bill** and **Jeff** sip their bourbons.  
The silence is good. Heavy. But not hostile.

Then **Jeff** breaks it.  
Quietly. Like he’s been thinking it all night.

**JEFF (offhand)**  
You know, it’s my understanding…  
Sarah’s gonna retire soon.

**Bill raises an eyebrow.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
Move down to Florida.  
Husband’s already got a place lined up.  
No winter, no taxes, no headlines.  
Just a happy ending.

**He swirls the bourbon once, sips.**

**JEFF (soft)**  
She’s earned it.

**Bill grunts. Then narrows his eyes.**

**BILL**  
So what?  
You saying the succession plan at Island’s been evolving?

**Jeff just looks at him. Doesn’t answer.

Bill leans in slightly, voice low. Just a little sharp.**

**BILL (continued)**  
You saying Sarah’s been treating **Madeline**  
like a fucking teacher’s pet?

**Beat.**

**BILL**  
Is that where you’re going with this?

**Jeff takes a slow sip.**

**JEFF (flat)**  
I’m saying Sarah’s smart.  
And Sarah doesn’t leave loose ends.

**Beat.**

**JEFF (continued)**  
That sound like her to you?

**Bill exhales through his nose.**  
**No answer.**  
**Because yeah — it does.**

**SCENE: “Edge” – Hotel Room, Manhattan**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

The skyline outside glows faint with the first hints of dawn.  The city is quiet now—resting before the next siren, the next headline.

**Jeff** enters the room and lets the door swing shut behind him.

He drops his jacket on the chair.  
Kicks off his boots with dull thuds.  
No music. No TV. No fanfare.

Just the stillness of exhaustion and a brain that won’t stop grinding gears.

He stands there for a long beat, staring at nothing, jaw clenched.  
The kind of tired that isn’t just physical—**it’s existential**.  
Too many meetings. Too many ghosts. Too much everything.

He moves to the edge of the bed.  
Sits.  
Leans forward with his elbows on his knees.  
Breathes.

And finally, in that quiet, **with no one to impress and no one to perform for**—  
he tries to take the edge off.

Alone.  
Silent.  
Methodical.

There’s nothing sexy about it.  
No fantasy.  
No romance.  
Just a necessary, exhausted ritual—**to still the machine**, if only for a few hours.

When it’s done, he wipes his hand on the white towel left from the shower hours ago.  
No fanfare.  
No shame.

He pulls the blackout curtain tight, kills the light, and collapses face-down onto the bed.

He’s asleep in seconds.

---

**SCENE: “Split Screen” – Hotel Room / Hotel Room**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – JEFF – EARLY MORNING**

The city hums beyond the windows, distant.  
Jeff lies sprawled across the bed, one leg half-draped off the side, finally still.

**SPLIT TO:**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – JIM – SAME TIME**

A different room, different furniture, **same sense of quiet disconnect**.

**Jim** sits in bed with a half-eaten room service tray nearby.  
Bland food. Bland night. Bland silence.

He scrolls his phone for a few minutes, bored out of his mind.  
Instagram. Sports clips. Nothing sticks.  
No messages that matter.

He sighs, sets the phone down.  
Stretches out.

And with no real interest — no passion, no urgency — he decides to **go through the motions**.  
A quiet, half-resentful kind of autopilot.  
Like brushing teeth. Like filing a tax form.

There’s no imagination involved.  
Just the physicality of something familiar.  
Something that still works, even when **nothing else does.**

**CUT BACK TO:**

Jeff, already asleep.  
Dead to the world.

**CUT TO:**

Jim, done.  
Face blank.  
No shame. No triumph. Just… done.

He grabs a tissue. Tosses it in the trash.  
Flips the light off.  
And lies back in bed, eyes open for just a moment too long.

Then closes them.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Split Screen – Three Rooms” – Hotel Rooms Across Manhattan**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – JEFF – EARLY MORNING**  
Jeff lies twisted in tangled sheets, finally asleep.  
Muscles slack. Eyes closed. Nothing left in him.

**SPLIT TO:**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – JIM – SAME TIME**  
Jim rolls over.  
Blank. Quiet. Breathing slowly.  
Sleep finally wins.

**SPLIT TO:**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – CREMEANS – SAME TIME**

A smaller room. No food tray. No mess. Just **neatness** and **ritual**.

**Cremeans** sits upright in bed, back against the headboard, holding **a Gideon Bible** in both hands.

The page:  
**Jeremiah.**  
A chapter about brokenness. Captivity. Restoration that never seems to come.

He reads.  
Line after line.

**No comfort.**  
**No warmth.**  
**Just paper and ink and silence.**

He closes it slowly.  
Sets it on the nightstand with care.  
Reaches for the lamp.

**CREMEANS (quiet, almost to himself)**  
Nothing tonight, huh?

The light clicks off.

He lies back.  
Hands folded over his chest.  
Eyes to the ceiling for one long breath.

And then…

Sleep.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Split Screen – Bill” – Hotel Room, Same Night**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – BILL – EARLY MORNING**

Television flickers across the walls.  
**Bill** slouches on the edge of the bed, remote in hand, shirt half-buttoned.  
A half-drunk soda sweats on the nightstand.  
The glow of **CNN**, then **MSNBC**, then **local news**.

He flips through with practiced indifference.  
Stops on **HBO** out of habit.

Onscreen — a sex scene.  
Not romantic.  
**Raw. Graphic. Real.**

Bill’s eyes hold on it longer than he means to.  
His breath slows. His grip on the remote loosens.

Something **clicks in his brain**.  
Simple. Mechanical. Familiar.

He **doesn’t think twice.**  
He **doesn’t second-guess.**

He slides back on the bed.  
Lets the scene play.

And gets himself off.

No flourish.  
No urgency.  
Just a man chasing **a little dopamine in the dark**.

When it’s done, he exhales.  
Tosses the remote on the floor.  
Wipes his hand with a napkin from the room service tray.  
Turns the TV off.

Darkness.

Sleep.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Split Screen – Jeremy” – Hotel Room, Same Night**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – JEREMY – EARLY MORNING**

**Jeremy** stands at the minibar.  
The fridge light glows when he opens the door.

Miniature bottles gleam like **jewelry for the damned**.  
Vodka. Whiskey. Rum.  
Perfect little doses. Perfect little bombs.

He stares.  
Smells.  
Feels the chill of the glass in his fingers.

**Then he closes the door.**  
**Slowly. Quietly.**

He leans his head against the cabinet for a long breath.

**JEREMY (murmuring)**  
Not tonight.  
Not four years gone for this.

He walks away.  
Strips his shirt off.  
Falls onto the bed.

His body is tense. His nerves are frayed.  
He can still taste the bourbon **he didn’t drink**.

**So he tries something else.**  
**Simple. Stupid. Human.**

**He jerks off.**

Fast. Frustrated. Almost angry.  
No fantasy. No joy. Just **relief from the heat in his blood.**

When it’s done, he exhales hard.

No satisfaction.  
But at least… *not drinking*.

He wipes off with a towel.  
Turns out the light.  
And lets sleep, finally, come find him.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Split Screen – Sarah” – Long Island, Same Night**

**INT. LUXURY BEDROOM – LONG ISLAND – EARLY MORNING**

**Sarah Malcolm’s bedroom is immaculate.**  
Crisp linens. Soft light. A scent of lavender that was probably expensive.

**Sarah is underneath MICHAEL.**  
He’s focused. Steady. Breathing heavy.

**She is not.**

Her eyes are open, staring past him.  
**Her mind is elsewhere.**

The band. The leaks. The plan.  
**Cremeans. Madeline. Jeremy. Avril.**

It’s not pain. It’s not boredom.  
It’s just **disassociation.**

**SARAH (flat, practiced)**  
Oh…  
God…  
Yeah.

**It’s not a cry. Not a gasp. Just a signal.**  
**Enough. Finish. Let this be over.**

**MICHAEL exhales. His face twists. He comes.**  
**Satisfied. Fulfilled. Spent.**

He collapses beside her with a tired groan.

**MICHAEL (half-laughing)**  
Still got it.

**Sarah doesn’t answer.**

She stares at the ceiling.

Her breathing slows.

She reaches down, pulls the sheet up over her chest.  
Her expression doesn’t change.

Eyes open.  
Silent.

---

**SCENE CONTINUED: “Split Screen – Madeline” – Brooklyn Apartment, Same Night**

**INT. MADISON BROWNSTONE – LATE NIGHT**

**Madeline** climbs the stairs to her third-floor apartment, keys jangling with more aggression than she intends.

Inside:  
High-end minimalism. Art on the walls.  
A kitchen that gleams.  
A couch that looks like it cost more than her first year of college.

She drops her bag.  
Sits.  
Stares.

Then slowly—mechanically—she pulls off her jeans.  
Rolls down her panties.  
Reclines.

**Her fingers move.**

Touching herself is easy.  
It’s practiced. It’s muscle memory.

**Feeling good?**  
**Not even close.**

**Six, seven minutes pass.**  
**She changes rhythm. Tries pressure. Tries breath.**  
**Nothing.**

Her head is a noise machine.

**The cop’s voice.**  
**The body cavity search.**  
**The click of latex gloves.**  
**The judgment.**  
**The shame.**  
**The total loss of sovereignty.**

**MADALINE (whispers)**  
Come on. Come *on*.

But it doesn’t happen.

There is no peak.  
No relief.  
Only a growing, angry heat on her skin — **and not the good kind.**

**She winces.**

**MADALINE (flat)**  
Now I’m just giving myself a rash.

She pulls her hand away.

Sits upright.  
Panties still around her knees.  
Breathing heavy, not from pleasure — **from defeat.**

She grabs a blanket.  
Wraps it around herself.  
And doesn’t move.

The room is still.

---

**SCENE: “Bedpan” – Bellevue Hospital, Late Night**

**INT. BELLEVUE HOSPITAL ROOM – 3:44 A.M.**

The fluorescent light above Avril’s bed hums softly.  
The world beyond the window is black glass.  
The monitors beep, slow and indifferent.

**Avril is awake.**  
Eyes open.  
Breath shallow.

A cool band of **steel wraps her ankle**, chained to the frame of the bed.

And now…  
**she has to pee.**

She feels it in her abdomen.  
A dull pressure.  
An ache that’s impossible to ignore.

Her eyes flick to the **call button**.

She knows what happens if she presses it.  
They’ll come.  
Two nurses, maybe three.  
They’ll unlock one link in the chain, escort her to the bathroom.  
**Hover. Watch.**

Like she’s going to sprint down the hallway in a hospital gown.  
Like she’s not bruised, battered, sedated, scraped raw by the city and the night.

Or—

Her eyes shift to the **bedpan on the shelf** near the wall.

Cold. Shiny. Waiting.

**She could do it now.**  
**Alone.**

She could try.  
Slide it into place.  
Relieve herself in silence.  
**Before pressing the button.**

Or—

She could wait.  
Call them.  
Let the professionals help.  
Endure the ritual.  
The hovering.  
The eyes.

**Neither is dignified.**  
**Neither is victory.**  
**It’s just a matter of which shame she wants to own.**

She stares at the ceiling.  
Swallows hard.

**AVRIL (hoarse, to no one)**  
God, I used to fly private.

She reaches slowly toward the call button—  
then pauses.

Then reaches toward the bedpan.

Then pauses again.

**The scene holds.**  
**A woman in a hospital bed, trying to choose the lesser form of degradation.**

And the night drags on.

---

**SCENE: “Gymnastics” – Bellevue Hospital Room**

**INT. BELLEVUE HOSPITAL ROOM – 3:47 A.M.**

**Avril** decides.

She reaches—slow, cautious—for the **bedpan**.  
It’s cold in her fingers. Metal. Impersonal.  
She sets it beside her, winces.

**Her left leg is still partially hooked under the bed’s side rail.**  
An instinctive shift in her sleep earlier —  
and now she’s **twisted**, half-bound, like she’s **knotted into the furniture.**

She tries to swing her leg up.  
The ankle cuff clinks, tightens.  
The bed creaks.

**AVRIL (muttering)**  
Jesus Christ.

She scoots her hips.  
Too far to the left — her back spasms.  
Too far to the right — the bedpan slips off the edge.

She grabs it, breathing hard.  
Tries again.

**AVRIL (to herself, frustrated)**  
It shouldn’t be this hard to take a fucking leak.

She shifts.  
Grimaces.  
**Folds herself in half** like some deranged yoga pose in a hospital gown.

Finally, **finally**, she manages to wedge the pan under herself.  
Precariously. Barely.  
Balanced on pain and willpower.

She breathes.  
Closes her eyes.  
Lets go.

A soft sound. Metallic. Shameful.

When she’s done, her hand shakes as she removes it.  
She doesn’t look.

**AVRIL (whispers)**  
Rock and roll.

She wipes her hands on a tissue.  
Pushes the call button with the back of her wrist.

And lies back.

Eyes open.  
Staring into the dark.

---

**SCENE: “The Writ” – Bennett’s Apartment, Harlem**

**INT. LUXURIOUS APARTMENT – PRE-DAWN HOURS**

High ceilings. Polished hardwood floors. Bookshelves arranged like strategy maps.  
Soft jazz plays low from invisible speakers.

At a long, sleek desk, under a brass lamp, sits **Bennett King**.  
Loosened tie. Rolled sleeves. Expression like granite.

In front of him:  
A **nearly complete writ of habeas corpus**, drafted with elegance, efficiency, and just a whisper of fury.

**BENNETT (quiet, to himself)**  
No charges. No hearing. No freedom.  
Classic fuck-fuck games.

He flips a page. Re-reads a paragraph. Tightens the language.

He reaches for his pen — a **$120 fountain pen** he’s had since law school — and adds a final clause.

But something falters.

**His hand slows.**  
**His breath catches.**  
**He stops.**

He stares at the document.

**He should love this.**  
**This is what he lives for.**

Fighting for the voiceless.  
Punching upward.  
Calling the system out with the same rules it hides behind.

But tonight?

**There’s no rush.**  
**No thrill.**  
**Only weight.**

He caps the pen.  
Sets it down with precision.  
Rubs his temples.

**BENNETT (low)**  
Tomorrow.

He stands.  
Moves through the silence of his apartment like a man walking through fog.  
Pauses in the doorway to his bedroom.

No victory music.  
No righteous fire.

Just exhaustion, tailored and buttoned down.

He turns off the lamp.  
And disappears into the dark.

---

**SCENE: “The Third Cruelty” – Ramos’s Apartment, Staten Island**

**INT. DETECTIVE RAMOS'S APARTMENT – 2:16 A.M.**

The lights come on.

**Ramos** steps inside, lets the door close behind her with a dull **thud**.

She doesn’t toss her things.  
She **removes them.**  
Deliberate. Methodical. Heavy with silence.

**Gun, badge, vest, belt.**  
Each placed with care. Not reverence — **discipline.**

Her shoes go in the closet.  
Side by side. Heels worn down from chasing ghosts through alleys and courtrooms.

**She is furious.**

At the system.  
At the job.  
At herself—for believing in something that keeps failing the people who need it most.

She pours a **glass of red wine**.  
Takes a sip.  
Another.

It doesn’t help.

She unclasps her bra.  
Tosses it on the chair.  
Runs a hand over her breast — not sexual. Just **checking if she’s even real anymore.**

She slides her hand down.  
Into her panties.

**Just to feel something.**  
**Just to take the edge off.**  
**Just to get. one. hit. of dopamine.**  
**Something to shut her brain up long enough to sleep.**

But it’s not working.  
She’s dry.  
Her body is **tight**, not in anticipation, but in **defiance**.

She tries.  
Imagines.  
Strains.

**Nothing.**

No build. No spark.  
Just this **maddening emptiness**.

She pulls her hand out.  
Slams the wine glass down hard enough to rattle.

She blinks up at the ceiling.

The air smells like soap.  
Like aloe and antiseptic.

Her hands rest on her stomach.

Her voice is barely more than a whisper:

**“Do I… smell better?”**

The nurse, still at the sink, doesn’t turn around.

But her voice comes back, steady and simple.

**“Yeah. You do.”**

Avril closes her eyes.  
That’s enough.  
That’s more than enough.

---

**SCENE – Problem Solving**

Sunlight slices through the blinds.

Madeline lounges on the couch in her Brooklyn brownstone,  
a cup of coffee cooling in her hand,  
a low-level ache still burning behind her eyes.

Sleep helped.  
Sort of.

But that feeling from last night?  
Still there.

**The wrongness. The failure. The frustration.**  
She’s never been one to wallow in failure.

She gets up, stretches, breathes.  
Walks back to the bedroom with bare feet across hardwood.

Opens the drawer next to her bed.  
Reaches in.

**“Okay,”** she mutters. **“Let’s stop playing around.”**

She pulls out the **Hitachi Magic Wand**—  
big, white, heavy, and merciless.

She doesn’t romanticize it.  
She doesn’t flirt with it.

This isn’t about *mood*.

This is about **outcome**.

She lays back on the bed.  
Tugs off her shirt.  
Slides her panties down.  
Spreads her legs.

And plugs it in.

*Click.*  
*Hum.*  
The sound is *surgical*.

No candles. No fantasy. No Gilley. No trauma.

Just her, the wand, and the **expectation of results**.

She presses it against her clit—  
direct, firm, no warmup.

Her eyes shut.  
She breathes.  
Waits.

Nothing.

She ups the setting.  
More power.  
More pressure.  
Her thighs tense.

Still—**nothing.**

---

**SCENE – Controlled Detonation**

The hum fills the room like distant machinery.  
Madeline doesn’t flinch. Doesn’t squirm.

She frowns slightly.  
Too weak.

Her thumb flips the switch.  
**Low to high.**

*The buzz becomes a growl.*

The wand in her hand isn’t a toy—  
it’s a tool.  
It obeys.

She adjusts her grip.  
Presses it **directly** against her clit.  
Tilts it just enough to spread the pressure.

No romance. No imagination.  
Just **response**.

Muscle memory engages.  
She knows her body.  
Knows the thresholds.

*One minute, twenty-eight seconds in—first peak approaching.*

She lifts the wand.  
Breathes.  
Waits.

**“Not yet.”**

Reapplies.  
Another rise—sharper this time.  
Legs stiffening. Breathing harder.

She pulls away **three seconds before release**.

*Reset. Edge two.*

Now she’s focused.

Final approach.  
Her jaw clenches.  
She rides the hum like it’s a graph she’s already studied.

And this time—  
**she doesn’t stop.**

Her back arches.  
Her thighs lock.  
She bites her lip as the climax crashes in—**deep, internal, pure signal.**

*A detonation, not a flood.*

No moan.  
Just breath, sharp and broken.  
A tremor down her spine.

Her eyes flutter open.  
Still panting.  
But already recovering.

She lifts the wand away.  
Turns it off.  
The silence feels earned.

Madeline lies back, arm across her forehead.  
Cool. Steady.  
**Satisfied.**

“There it is.”

It wasn’t joyful.  
It wasn’t emotional.

But it was **enough**.

---

**SCENE – Aftermath**

Madeline sits up.  No daze. No flush. No dreamy haze.  She reaches over, unplugs the wand.  The cord coils neatly in her hand.

She eyes the slicked head of the device.

**“That won’t do.”**

She stands, moves to the bathroom.  Opens the cabinet under the sink.  Takes out a clean microfiber cloth and a small bottle of isopropyl alcohol—  **dedicated.**  **Labeled.**  **Stored for this exact purpose.**

She spritzes the wand’s silicone head twice.  Wipes carefully, precisely.  Clockwise. Then counter.  Edges. Seam.
Not a trace left.  She holds it to the light.  Inspects it.

Satisfied, she wraps the cord.  Tucks it back into its drawer.  Closed, sealed, catalogued.

Madeline looks at herself in the mirror.  Not smiling.  But **centered**.  This is control.  This is what she needed.  Now she can start her day.

---

**Bennett King – Profile Overview**

**Role**

* **High-powered criminal defense attorney**, operating out of Harlem.
* Described as a **"white-shoe" lawyer**—meaning elite, polished, and commanding authority in high-level legal circles.
* The go-to lawyer when reputations and fortunes are on the line.

---

**Traits**

* **Sharp, unflinching, and brutally efficient.**  He doesn’t waste time on flowery language. He delivers hard truths with finesse, whether to a DA, a client, or a judge.
* **Expensive—but worth every dollar.**  His rate is $900/hour, and he has the gravitas to justify it. He’s not just smart—he **wins**, and he **knows the system inside and out**.
* **Disciplined and calculating.**    Incredibly methodical—he crafts a defense like a general planning a campaign. He doesn’t rattle, doesn’t rush, and doesn’t bluff without ammunition.
* **Morally pragmatic.**    He doesn’t pretend to be a saint. But he believes in fairness. If someone’s being railroaded, it **pisses him off**, and he’ll throw his entire weight behind the counterattack.
* **Culturally grounded.**  He’s a **Black man in America** who has made it to the top without losing his understanding of what the game really is. He’s aware of how justice bends—by class, race, media, and power. And he uses that knowledge as leverage.

---

**Motivations (as established so far)**

* **To protect his clients, but also to keep the system honest.**    He doesn’t take on cases to get his name in the press. He takes them because they **matter**, and because he **knows how to win**. But also because **fighting injustice makes him feel alive.**

* **To maintain his position of dominance in the legal field.**    Bennett isn’t humble. He’s earned his place, and he’ll protect it. He doesn’t play small, and he’s not afraid to burn bridges if the truth is at stake.

* **To stay clean.**    Bennett operates **above the gutter**. He’s not crooked. He’ll be savage, but not dirty. He’s the man you call when your back’s against the wall, and you want to come out clean—and **still win**.

---

**Long-Term Potential**

You’re smart to consider **folding him into the band’s future**:

* He brings *gravitas* and an outside perspective that the band desperately needs.
* He’s a truth-teller, which is crucial for a group that tends to spiral.
* He could evolve into a **moral anchor**—especially as the band faces future crises, lawsuits, label fights, or even political entanglements.

He’s also got great one-liner energy. The type of character who could **deflate a PR storm with a single sentence** or **shut down a hostile interview with a look**.

---

**BENNETT KING – Character Profile**

**Name: Bennett André King**

**Born:** 1984, Harlem, New York City  
**Age:** 40  
**Ethnicity:** African-American  
**Profession:** High-profile criminal defense attorney, founder and managing partner of **King & Halpern LLP**

**EDUCATION**

* **Undergraduate:**  
  Columbia University, B.A. in Political Science  
  *Class of 2006*

  * Graduated **magna cum laude**
  * Debate team captain; known for never losing a closing argument
  * Internship with the NAACP Legal Defense Fund

* **Law School:**  
  NYU School of Law, J.D.  
  *Class of 2009*

  * Editor, **NYU Law Review**
  * Summer associate at Cravath, Swaine & Moore—declined their offer to join a smaller, mission-driven litigation boutique instead

**CAREER TIMELINE**

* **2009–2013:** Associate at **Mason & DeWitt LLP**, a mid-sized litigation firm known for civil rights and criminal defense

  * Earned a rep as a *courtroom tactician*—clean, brutal, and never grandstanding
  * First major win: acquitted a wrongfully accused teenager of gun charges in the Bronx. Media attention followed.

* **2013–2016:** Partner track, but jumped ship to co-found his own firm

  * Believed big law wasn’t agile enough to fight institutional power
  * **Founded King & Halpern LLP** in Harlem with fellow NYU grad Janine Halpern
  * Took on everything from celebrity cases to activist defense, keeping a spotless win/loss record on high-profile trials

* **2016–Present:**

  * Became known as a **“firewall lawyer”**—the one you call when the press is circling, the cops are hostile, and the court of public opinion has already convicted you
  * Clients range from musicians to CEOs to wrongly accused protestors
  * Named one of NYC’s **“Top 100 Attorneys Under 40”** by *The American Lawyer* in 2020
  * Occasionally lectures at NYU and Columbia Law as a guest speaker on constitutional defense strategy

---

**PERSONALITY & TRAITS**

* **Ethical Hardliner**: Believes in the rule of law—but understands how easily it’s twisted. He will not dirty his hands, but he’ll use every legal inch the system allows.
* **Culturally Aware**: Navigates both the elite white-collar world and the street-level reality of his Harlem roots. Never forgot where he came from.
* **Deadpan & Precise**: Rarely raises his voice. Uses **calm power** to disarm and dismantle. Known for ending interrogations with a single line.
* **Tailored but Sharp-Edged**: Always in immaculate suits—bespoke Harlem tailor—but still carries himself like a man who knows what a precinct back room smells like.

---

**VISUAL PROFILE**

* 6'1", athletic build—ex-basketball player at Columbia
* Always well-groomed: fade haircut, trimmed beard, glasses when reading legal filings
* Signature scent: Tom Ford Noir
* Often wears cufflinks with tiny lions on them—“King,” naturally

---

**PHILOSOPHY / CORE MOTIVATION**

“You don’t beat the system by playing its game. You beat it by understanding every cheat code they think you’ll never learn.”

Bennett King doesn’t fight for the innocent.  He fights for the **accused**—because in America, those aren’t always the same.  He’s driven by a deep awareness of how **race, wealth, and media pressure intersect** to create narratives of guilt. His job isn’t to make you likable—it’s to keep you **free**.

---

**Hooks for Future Development**

* **Possible Confidante of Jeremy or Sarah**: He doesn’t just protect the band legally—he may become a back-channel strategist and moral adviser.
* **Conflict With Madeline**: She's strategic and cold. He’s strategic and principled. They might clash even when on the same side.
* **Target for Media**: A Black attorney defending controversial celebrities? There’s plenty of room for narrative weaponization.

---

**Bennett King’s Voice – Manhattan Black Lawyer Dialect \+ Worldview**

**Tone**

* **Measured, rhythmic, and composed.**  He doesn’t shout. He *lands*. Every word is weighted like a legal precedent.
* **Barbed elegance.**  Polished, but full of bite. He doesn’t raise his voice—he lets **his silence threaten**.
* **Manhattan fluency.**  References *uptown vs downtown*, dismisses “Jersey nonsense,” and regards **Ohio, Nebraska, or anywhere else** with a detached smirk.

**Sample Phrasing / Vocabulary**

* “I’ve lived through three mayors and five DA regimes. I don’t rattle easy.”
* “Let’s not pretend this town is about truth. This is Manhattan—it’s about proof.”
* “Out there, they get drunk and make mistakes. In here? We get indicted for sneezing wrong.”
* “Don’t bring me Midwest morality, sir. This is New York. We *invented* moral ambiguity.”
* “Everything west of the Hudson is theory. In this city? It’s case law.”

**Cultural Markers in His Speech**

* He knows the **subway by line color**, not number.
* Refers to neighborhoods by shorthand: “UWS,” “SoHo,” “Alphabet,” “the Avenues.”
* Doesn’t call it “NYC” or “the city.” He calls it **“this island.”**
* Speaks of Harlem with reverence. The Bronx with caution. Staten Island? “That’s for the Staten Islanders.”

**Worldview Anchors**

* **City \= Empire.**  
  “This island made me. You want to understand power? Look out your damn window. That’s Manhattan. That’s not a skyline. That’s a warning.”
* **Race \= Constant Calculation.**  
  “Being a Black man in this city means knowing when they smile at you, they’re counting the ways they can charge you.”
* **Power \= Leverage.**  
  “I don’t believe in fair fights. I believe in winning with clean hands and a loaded statute book.”

---

**Contrast Point**

Imagine him opposite:

* A **Midwestern character** like Jeff or Jeremy \= instant cultural clash.
* A bureaucrat from *Albany* \= contempt.
* A Southern judge \= slow burn evisceration.

---

**Secret Foundation: Bennett King – Army National Guard Background**

**Military Status**

* **Rank:** Major (O-4)
* **Branch:** Judge Advocate General’s Corps (JAG)
* **Unit:** New York Army National Guard
* **Enlisted:** 2002, as a way to pay for Columbia
* **Commissioned:** 2006, ROTC during undergrad
* **Active in JAG since law school graduation (2009)**

**Why It Works So Cleanly**

* **Covers the cost**: Tuition, room & board, books—covered through a combination of ROTC, state guard scholarship programs, and federal tuition assistance.
* **Explains his posture**: That straight-backed stillness? The pause before he speaks? That’s military bearing.
* **Explains his depth**: While he plays the Manhattan game like a grandmaster, he also shows restraint, sacrifice, and—beneath it all—an *unshakable code*.
* **Gives him access and insight**: He understands bureaucracy, federal systems, and criminal military code—useful when helping celebrities in deep federal or legal muck.
* **Secret edge**: It’s not public knowledge. But the few who know? They respect him on a whole different level.

---

**How He Sees It**

“Harlem made me. Columbia shaped me. Uncle Sam paid for me. So now I pay it forward—with interest.”

He doesn’t brag about it.  He doesn’t hang flags in his office.  But he **shows up for drill.**  He does the work.

And if you’re someone who mocks service, or shrugs at duty?  Bennett King will ice you over **so hard**, you’ll feel it in your marrow.

**Lines He Might Drop Quietly, When It Matters**

* “I didn’t just study law—I enforced it. In uniform. On tarmacs. In courtrooms. Overseas.”
* “Your kid got confused at Coachella. Mine got called up for riot control in Rochester.”
* “I don’t need a lecture on service. I’ve worn the uniform longer than you’ve been licensed.”

**Narrative Opportunities**

* He has strings to pull within **state-level power circles**—military, legal, and political.
* He’s got access to the **National Guard chain of command**, and might owe or be owed favors.
* He may disappear for **two weeks every summer** for training—and only Sarah or Jeremy know why.
* He might be the **only adult in the room** when a real disaster hits (legal or literal).

**It’s a Masterstroke of Contrast**

* **He’s the guy in front of a judge on Friday… **Then **out at Fort Drum** running JAG training by Saturday.
* **He’s in a bespoke navy-blue suit on Monday…**  And in **ACUs (Army Combat Uniforms)** at Camp Smith by Wednesday afternoon.
* **He’s lecturing Columbia Law about the Constitution…**  
  But also knows exactly how to **build a legal case for a convoy commander who shot someone in Fallujah**.

**What That Gives You, Dramatically**

* **Nobody expects it**—not even his clients, who’d drop their espresso if they saw him marching at drill.
* It instantly **shuts up arrogance** in a room. The kind of hedge fund frat boys or influencers who assume he’s “just a lawyer” get humbled real quick.
* It gives him **legitimacy in blue-collar rooms**—cops, veterans, NYPD brass, old-school judges.
* It creates **cross-class and cross-racial connections**: he’s not just "black excellence," he’s “black service.”
* It underlines how **disciplined and battle-tested** he truly is. This is not a guy who bluffs. He makes war in court *because he’s trained to do so*.

---

**Bennett King’s Origin Story – September 11th, 2001**
**Date: Tuesday, September 11th, 2001**
**Age: 17**
**Place: Harlem, Senior Year, Frederick Douglass Academy**

**What Happens**

He’s in **U.S. History class**—ironically, the Constitution unit—when the first plane hits.  The **TV gets wheeled in.** The class goes silent.  He watches **the second plane live**.  He sees the cloud. He sees people running uptown.  
Then he sees the towers fall.  And something **fundamental inside him shatters and reforms**.

**Immediate Emotional Response**

* **Rage. Helplessness. Resolve.**  The world cracked. And nobody looked like they had a plan to fix it.
* His father, a corrections officer, comes home early, shaken.  His mother, a church secretary, is praying.    Bennett? He’s *deciding*.

*“I knew it that night. No college, no city job, no law firm was ever going to make sense until I paid my due to this island. Not America. Not the flag. This island. My people. My city. I made a vow.”*

**Decision & Action**

* He **enlists in the National Guard** before graduation—delayed-entry program
* **ROTC at Columbia**—he’d already gotten early admission
* He knew he was smart. He knew he could be powerful.  But none of that mattered until he proved something deeper: “I didn’t want to be the smartest guy in the room. I wanted to be the guy who could walk through the smoke and keep moving.”

**Narrative Opportunity**

* This can be revealed in a **deep private conversation**—maybe with Jeremy or even Sarah, when they finally ask *why the hell* he still does Guard duty with his career.
* Could come during a high-stress moment—he flashes back to that TV in the classroom, the dust cloud on Broadway, the moment he said, **“I will serve.”**

**How He Frames It**

“I didn’t join to kill anybody. I joined because one day this city cried out, and I wanted to be the kind of man who could answer.”

That’s not patriotism.  That’s **localism, honor, and an oath to the people of New York.**

---

**FLASHBACK: September 11, 2001 – Harlem**

**INT. CLASSROOM – FREDERICK DOUGLASS ACADEMY – MORNING**

The air conditioning hums.  A chalkboard still reads: *The Constitution – Article I.*  Seventeen-year-old BENNETT sits with a history textbook open, but he’s watching the teacher’s lips, not the words.

Then—A RAP at the door.  A student aide, pale and out of breath, whispers something to the teacher.

The room goes still.  Then the teacher crosses to the **rolling TV cart**.  Static flickers. CNN cuts in.  **Tower One is already burning.**

**Then: the second plane. Live.**  Bennett flinches.  A girl behind him gasps, “Oh my God.”  The room explodes into whispers.

But Bennett is silent. Watching.  **Absorbing.**

---

**INT. LIVING ROOM – THAT NIGHT – HARLEM APARTMENT**

His father, CHARLES, a CO from Rikers, pours a heavy drink.  His mother, ELLA, is quiet in the corner, rosary in hand.  

Bennett sits by the window.  Looking **downtown**.  The sun is gone, but the **smoke still rises.**  He watches it curl over the rooftops like **a ghost that won't leave.**  Below, **sirens scream.**  Every five minutes. Another. And another.

---

**INT. BEDROOM – LATER**

Bennett is lying on his back, staring at the ceiling.  Hands behind his head.  Eyes wide open.

“It wasn’t just grief,” he would say years later.  
“It was *shame*. Shame that I couldn’t do a goddamn thing.”

He sits up.  Goes to his desk.  Pulls out a college packet from Columbia.  Then a pamphlet he took from a recruiter three weeks earlier: **“Serve Your State. Serve Your City. Join the Guard.”**

He looks at both.  And then he **makes a vow**—not out loud.  But *in his marrow*.

“One day, this city’s gonna burn again.  And I’m not gonna watch it from a classroom window.”

He folds the Columbia letter.  Puts it away.  Grabs the pamphlet.

---

**INT. FREDERICK DOUGLASS ACADEMY – AUDITORIUM – DAY**
