The **lights are bright**.  The room smells like pencil shavings and gym floor wax.  Front row: kids in hoodies, Jordans, cornrows, pressed button-downs. **AP Government students.** Some skeptical. Some wired. A few curious.

At the podium, **MAJOR BENNETT KING**.  **Black. Immaculate. Tailored gray three-piece suit.** Flag pin. Pocket square folded like origami. Military bearing in every breath.  He doesn’t hold notes.

---

**BENNETT KING’S SPEECH (EXCERPT)**

“I sat where you sit. In that third row, middle seat. I stared out that window and wondered how I was gonna get out of Harlem without getting swallowed whole.”

“Everyone told me to keep my head down. Stay outta trouble. Be safe. But safe don’t build anything. Safe doesn’t shake the world.”

He holds eye contact with the **back row**—where the cynics sit.

“I wanted more. So I made a deal. The Army paid for Columbia. The Guard paid for law school. And I paid it back—in sweat, and in service.”

Beat.

“I wear a uniform. I argue in courtrooms. I do both. Same man. Same oath.”

“Now listen—some of you think the Army is for people who got no options. That’s a lie they sell you to keep you small.”

He steps out from behind the podium. Eyes sharp. Voice low.

“You want to know the real deal? The Army doesn’t give a damn what color your skin is. It cares if you show up. If you fight for something bigger than yourself. You want a place that sees *you* before they see your last name or your zip code?”

Beat.

“Then maybe the National Guard is where you start. Maybe it’s not forever. Maybe it’s your bridge.”

“And maybe—just maybe—you use it the way I did. Not to escape Harlem… but to come back to it as something more.”

**He lets that sit.**

“This island made me.  The Guard trained me.  And law… Law is how I fight for people who don’t even know they’re in a war yet.”

**CUT TO: STUDENTS**

Some are still.  Some nod.  One or two lean forward.

**BENNETT (FINAL BEAT)**

“Look around.  In this city, nothing’s fair.  But everything’s possible.  So make a decision.  Be the person who walks through the smoke.”

---

**Applause. Slow. Then swelling.**

---

**INT. FREDERICK DOUGLASS ACADEMY – AUDITORIUM – AFTER THE SPEECH**

The students are dispersing, buzzing. A few daps. One kid mutters, “Yo, that dude clean.” But two students hang back.

**STUDENT 1: KEESHA**  
17, sharp, skeptical eyes, bubble jacket over an oversized hoodie.  
She’s Harlem to the core. Hair in long red twists. Mistrust of suits in her DNA.

**STUDENT 2: TYRELL**  
16, lean frame, quiet but intense. The kind of kid who doesn’t speak unless he means it. Backpack slung low. Wears ambition like it’s hidden armor.

They walk up.

---

**KEESHA**

"So, you just… wear suits like that on a Tuesday?"

Bennett smiles.

**BENNETT**  
"I wear suits when I want people to know I take myself seriously. And when I want them to take me seriously too."

**KEESHA**  
"Nah, I mean—Harlem don’t look like *that*. You don’t look like us."

Bennett steps in, voice low but strong.

**BENNETT**  
"Sure I do. I’m what happens when Harlem bets on itself. Don’t confuse clean clothes with distance. This suit doesn’t mean I left the block. It means I brought it with me—and leveled it up."

She looks him over again. This time differently.

**KEESHA**  
"Why you come back?"

**BENNETT**  
"Because I remember what it felt like to be underestimated every goddamn day. And I remember what it felt like when someone saw past that."

He nods at her, just once.

**BENNETT** (cont’d)  
"You can look like this, too. Whatever version you want."

Tyrell finally speaks.

**TYRELL**  
"Sir… I didn’t even know the Guard could *do* that. Like—college, law school, all that. I just figured it was for dudes that wanna, you know…shoot stuff."

**BENNETT**  (laughs softly)  
"That’s how they sell it. But the truth is, the Guard’s a system. And systems got doors—if you know how to find the handles."

**TYRELL**  
"Could I do what you did?"

**BENNETT**  
"I hope you do more. Start with CUNY. Or SUNY. Get that scholarship. Then let the Guard foot the rest. Serve your people. Build something real. You don’t need a silver spoon. Just a plan."

Tyrell nods, and you can see the gears turning.

**TYRELL**  
"You got a card or something?"

Bennett reaches into his breast pocket. Pulls out **two**.

**BENNETT**  (to Tyrell)  
"Call me. I'll walk you through it."  

(to Keesha)  
"And if you ever want to talk about power—real power—I’ll buy the coffee."

---

**They walk off.**  Bennett watches them go.  Two seeds, different soil. But **he planted them anyway**.

---

**INT. ADA REYES’S OFFICE – DOWNTOWN MANHATTAN – MORNING**

Reyes doesn’t even look up when the door opens. He hears the shoes—**leather**, not rubber soles. He hears the confidence. He hears **money.**  He chuckles. Low. Like he saw this scene coming three movies ago.

**REYES:**  
“Damn. They really sent *you*, huh?”

**BENNETT KING** steps in, buttoning his jacket like he’s about to speak in front of a Supreme Court justice. He doesn’t smile—but his presence *does.*

**BENNETT:**  
“They didn’t send me. I came on my own. Some things don’t wait for a summons.”

**REYES:** (smirks, looking up)  
“You always dress like Wall Street on a Tuesday, or is this just for me?”

**BENNETT:**  
“I dress like Manhattan, Reyes. You know the deal.”

**REYES:**  
“I *do* know the deal. You scream Tribeca, ten-year bourbon, and Met Gala invites. I scream night school, two trains to the courthouse, and Citi Field in October.”

(leans back in chair)  
“We’re both from the block, Bennett. You just rented the penthouse.”

**BENNETT:**  
“And you stayed behind to fix the pipes. I respect that.”

(beat)  
“But we both still hear the water running, don’t we?”

**REYES:** (laughs once)  
“That line rehearsed or off the cuff?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Does it matter if it works?”

---

**INT. ADA REYES’S OFFICE – TEN MINUTES LATER**

The posturing is done. The coffee is cooling in their hands. Now it's down to business.

**REYES:**  
“She lied to a cop, King. You and I both know that's open and shut. Bodycam’s clean. Audio’s clearer than CNN.”

**BENNETT:**  
“She was under duress.”

**REYES:**  
“She wasn’t being waterboarded, Bennett. She was in the back of a squad car. You think a grand jury’s gonna look at a Black cop, a White woman, and say ‘Oh, sure, that’s a reasonable moment to lie about your name’?”

**BENNETT:**  
“I think they’re going to look at a terrified woman who just pulled a rock star out of a tunnel full of rats. Who saved her life. Who cooperated the second she was in a safe space. I think they’ll call that **human**.”

**REYES:**  
“You’re betting on empathy.”

**BENNETT:**  
“I’m betting on narrative.”

(beat)  
“And if you want to *test* that, I will burn your entire docket calendar for six months in pre-trial motions. I’ll file so many suppression requests you’ll need another assistant DA just to log them.”

**REYES:** (sips coffee)  
“So this is the part where you offer me mercy before you drop the hammer?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Reyes, I respect you too much to threaten you. But I’ll bury you **legally** if you make me.”

(pause)  
“Not because I want to. Because it's what I do.”

**REYES:**  
“You sound like you're about to ask for something big.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Disorderly conduct. One-year conditional discharge. No conviction, no record. She speaks at two high schools about consequences and courage. No media. No cameras. You walk away looking like a DA who believes in *rehabilitation*. And I walk away without declaring war.”

**REYES:**  
“Lying to a cop’s still a felony.”

**BENNETT:**  
“And this city’s still hanging by threads of public trust. Try her, and every progressive lawyer in Manhattan will say you railroaded a woman who saved a life.”

(leans in, voice low)  
“Do not become the guy who punishes the whistleblower while the rapists walk.”

(beat)

**REYES:**  
“If I take this deal—”

**BENNETT:**  
“—you win. Quietly. With dignity. And she disappears from your radar forever.”

(pause)  
“She’s not a threat. She’s not the story. Unless you make her one.”

Reyes leans back. He looks out the window. The city is moving. The gears of justice grinding.

Then:

**REYES:**  
“You write it up. I’ll sign it. But if she slips again?”

**BENNETT:**  
“She won’t. And if she does—*you won’t need me next time.*”

They stand. Shake hands. Not like friends. Like men with **mutual restraint**.  The war just ended before it began. Both of them walk out like generals who **knew the cost of victory**.

---

**INT. ADA REYES’S OFFICE – MOMENTS AFTER BENNETT KING EXITS**

The door shuts behind Bennett with a *click* that sounds more like a gavel than a latch.

REYES exhales. Leans back in his chair. Rubs his temples.

**REYES (to himself):**  
“God damn… thank God I’m in the public sector.”

(beat)  
“I couldn’t do what that man does. Wouldn’t want to. Wouldn’t sleep at night.”

He swivels in his chair and looks out the window. Midtown churns in motion. Yellow cabs. Crowds. Sirens in the distance. The noise of justice, or at least the **attempt** at it.

He picks up a pen, taps it against his notepad.

**REYES (quietly):**  
“But he’s not wrong.”

A beat. His eyes narrow. Decision made.  He pulls over the case folder. Slaps a post-it on the front.

**In bold handwriting:**  **“Modify GJ Submission – Reduce to Misdemeanor. Avoid optics disaster.”**

He circles it twice, then tosses the pen down.

**REYES (to himself):**  
“Give the jury less to work with. Let the city breathe.”

He closes the folder, picks up his coffee, now cold.

**REYES:**  
“And tell Madeline Quinlan she just walked through fire. Let’s pray she doesn’t strike a match again.”

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S CAR – MOVING THROUGH MIDTOWN – MIDDAY**

**Bennett’s on speaker**, his phone propped up on the leather console. The city hums around him—honking, shouting, everything urgent.  He’s calm. Surgical. A scalpel wrapped in silk.

**BENNETT (into phone):**  
“Ms. Quinlan. You answer your phone like you ain’t on the verge of being digested by the system.”

**MADELINE (V.O.):**  
“What happened?”

**BENNETT:**  
“I just walked out of Reyes’ office. The indictments are getting dropped.”

(beat)  
“You're getting twelve months of tightrope instead.”

**MADELINE (V.O.):**  
“Are we talking probation?”

**BENNETT:**  
“We're talking *grace,* Madeline. Conditional discharge. You stay clean, stay quiet, don’t lie to any more cops, and this disappears like a fart in the wind.”

(pause)  
“You slip—and they throw you into the East River with a legal anvil tied to your pretty little ankle.”

**MADELINE (V.O.):**  
“And if I don’t slip?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Then in twelve months, you walk out of this clean.”

(beat)  
“But don’t forget—*I* just saved your skinny white ass.”

He switches off speaker and brings the phone to his ear—more personal now.

**BENNETT (quietly):**  
“I’m not your savior. I’m your mercenary. Paid handsomely. If you screw up again, I’m not diving back into the fire. I’ll sit back and watch the piranha eat.”

(beat)  
“You understand me?”

**MADELINE (V.O.):**  
“…I understand.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Good. Now go be boring for the next year.”

He ends the call.  Takes a long breath.  The light turns green.  The city moves forward.  So does he.

---

**INT. BENNETT’S CAR – CONTINUOUS**

**CALL #1 – SARAH MALCOLM**

He dials. She answers on the third ring—still wound tight.

**SARAH (V.O.):**  
“You got news for me, counselor?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Madeline Quinlan will not be going to trial. Reyes agreed to a conditional discharge. No record. She plays nice, stays clean, the system forgets her.”

(beat)

**SARAH:**  
“Jesus. I… didn’t think you could pull that off.”

**BENNETT:**  
“I didn’t ‘pull it off.’ I arm-wrestled a man who doesn’t blink and made him blink. She’s safe. For now.”

**SARAH:** (quiet)  
“Thank you, Bennett.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Don’t thank me. Just keep her on a leash.”

(beat)

**BENNETT (continued):**  
“And Sarah?”

**SARAH:**  
“Yeah?”

**BENNETT:**  
“She steps one inch out of line again—and next time, I’ll be the one calling the DA. Not negotiating with him.”

Click.

---

**CALL #2 – CREMEANS**

He doesn’t wait for CREMEANS to answer. Just hits redial and lets it ring.

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**  
“Please tell me this is the good call, not the ‘we’re all going to federal prison’ call.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Relax. No prison. Just the kind of invoice that makes CFOs cry.”

(beat)  
“You ready?”

**CREMEANS:**  (as if bracing for gunfire)  
“Go.”

**BENNETT:**  
“$12,000 retainer—burned through it by hour six.”

(pause)  
“Thirty-eight billed hours at eighteen hundred an hour. That’s sixty-eight thousand four hundred. Plus two grand for courier, research, and my paralegal’s bonus because she damn well earned it.”

(beat)

**CREMEANS:**  
“Holy shit.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Oh, I’m not done. I comped the coffee and refused to bill you for emotional damage, which I assure you is extensive.”

(beat)

**BENNETT (continued):**  
“Check’s due by end of week. Wire preferred. I like clean money.”

**CREMEANS:**  
“Anything else?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Yeah. You hire amateurs again, you better have me on speed dial.”

(beat)  
“And put a damn fridge of Mountain Dew in your legal budget. You people are exhausting.”

He hangs up.  Smiles.  Traffic’s easing up. Sun’s out. Manhattan is still his.  **Bennett King doesn’t just close loops. He closes them with receipts.** 

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – EARLY AFTERNOON**

Cremeans sits alone. His tie’s loosened, shirt untucked just enough to register as *disheveled for him.* The *hum* of the air conditioner and the soft *clink* of his Mountain Dew against the table are the only sounds.

He opens the Venmo business app. Hesitates.

**CREMEANS (softly):**  
“All right. We knew it would cost. We just didn’t know how much.”

He enters the numbers with the precision of a man logging radiation levels.

> [!note] V
> **To:** @BennettKingESQ  
> **Amount:** $70,400  
> **Memo:** “Legal services rendered. No complaints. Thank you.”


Pause.

Then, almost as an afterthought: **Emoji:** Scales of justice, handshake, Mountain Dew.  He presses **SEND.**

*Ping.*

A calm settles over him, brittle and brief.  He sighs. Straightens his posture.

**CREMEANS (to himself):**  
“Okay. Time to pivot. Time to be useful again.”

He opens his laptop, cracks another Mountain Dew, and pulls up four browser tabs:

> [!tip] Chrome
> 1. Twitter.
> 2. Legal doc review.
> 3. Newswire feeds.
> 4. A draft statement from the band that hasn’t seen daylight.


The war’s not over. But at least they bought themselves another sunrise.

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S OFFICE – HARLEM – MINUTES LATER**

His phone pings. He glances at it. Sees the notification.

> [!note] V
> **VENMO RECEIVED – $70,400**  
> **From:** Cremeans  
> **Memo:** “Legal services rendered. No complaints. Thank you.”


He smirks. Picks up his phone. No hesitation. No emojis. Just words.

**BENNETT KING (texting):**

> [!note] iMessage
> *“Payment received. Harlem says you good.”*


---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – AFTERNOON**

Sarah has just returned from her office, holding a protein bar and a tablet. Cremeans is perched at the edge of the table like a middle schooler waiting for a report card.

**CREMEANS (half-joking, half-serious):**  
“So, um, question. Do I earn any brownie points for bailing that youthful lady—who, yes, may have told a bold-faced lie to a police officer—out of what I believe the courts refer to as *hard time*?”

**SARAH (not even looking up):**  
“You’re not getting a raise, Cremeans.”

**CREMEANS:**  
“I wasn’t asking for a raise. I was asking for moral points.”

**SARAH (dry):**  
“You don’t get moral points for cleaning up a mess your own team helped create.”

**CREMEANS (meekly):**  
“But it was really expensive cleanup.”

**SARAH (finally looks at him):**  
“And you paid the bill. That’s what grown-ups do. Congratulations.”

She exits. Cremeans stares at the door.

**CREMEANS (under his breath):**  
“That was… not a no on the brownie points.”

He cracks open another Mountain Dew.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

Cremeans is still nursing the tail end of his Mountain Dew. Sarah hasn’t sat. She’s standing at the head of the table—her presence cold, commanding.

**SARAH (level):**  
“You think this is over, Cremeans?”

**CREMEANS (cautious):**  
“I—I just said—”

**SARAH (cutting across him):**  
“No. Let me be perfectly clear.”

She steps forward, controlled. **No shouting.** Just precision.

**SARAH (continued):**  
“Madeline Quinlan will remember this week for the rest of her life. She was treated like a fucking criminal. She had a stranger with latex gloves explore her vagina and her rectum like they were cataloging evidence from a damn crime scene. Because someone somewhere decided she looked guilty enough to strip search.”

(beat)

**SARAH (sharper now):**  
“And while you’re out here tallying brownie points, she’s out there trying to stitch her dignity back together one thread at a time.”

Cremeans looks like he just got hit in the chest with a book.  Sarah doesn’t soften. She leans in.

**SARAH (quiet, deadly):**  
“You may have covered the bill, Cremeans. But that girl paid in blood and skin and humiliation. Never forget that.”

A long silence. You could hear the carbonation in his Mountain Dew fizz.  She turns, already done.

**SARAH (as she exits):**  
“Next time you try to spin trauma into a resume bullet, think twice.”

The door swings shut behind her.  Cremeans is left blinking. Then slowly exhales.

**CREMEANS (to himself, small):**  
“…Noted.”

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – WAR ROOM – EARLY AFTERNOON**

Madeline is seated at the media ops desk. Her phone in one hand, a stylus in the other, two laptops open—one monitoring **Instagram Stories**, the other set to a direct alert feed on **media mentions and trending tags.**

She doesn’t flinch as Sarah walks in. Sarah’s steps are hard. Controlled. Still simmering.

**SARAH (quiet, but barbed):**  
“Tell me we’re not losing the women.”

**MADELINE (eyes still on the screen):**  
“We’re holding. Gaining, actually. Instagram’s leaning pro-Avril. Especially in Germany and Canada. TikTok’s spottier. The bots are starting to backfire. I’ve rerouted to native messaging for now.”

**SARAH (crosses arms):**  
“You're managing a brand. I want to know how you’re managing *you.*”

Madeline finally looks up. Eyes dark-rimmed, expression unreadable.

**MADELINE:**  
“You’re asking if I’ve come unglued?”

**SARAH:**  
“I’m asking if you’ve stopped pretending you’re not.”

A long pause. Madeline clicks off one screen, then the other. Leans back slowly.

**MADELINE (dry):**  
“They took my fingerprints. My mugshot’s in the system. A woman I didn’t know used a flashlight to examine parts of my body that haven’t been touched since senior year. So yes, I’m angry. But anger is not a deficit, Sarah. It’s a data source.”

**SARAH (fury leaking through):**  
“Christ, Quinlan. You sound like a tech stack.”

**MADELINE:**  
“It’s my armor.”

**SARAH:**  
“Your armor makes you look like you’re bulletproof. But even armor has weak spots.”

**MADELINE:**  
“Then teach me how to wear it better. Isn’t that what mentors do?”

That stops Sarah cold for a moment.

She walks over, sets her coffee on the table, and leans against the edge.

**SARAH (measured):**  
“Let me tell you what I learned. The hard way. In this business, men don’t protect you. They profit from you. They will gaslight you, box you in, and when the walls collapse, they’ll ask if you were even in the room. You’ve got brains, Madeline. Razor-sharp ones. But you need more than a dashboard and a database. You need instinct. You need conviction.”

**MADELINE (matching tone):**  
“And you think I don’t have that?”

**SARAH (quieter):**  
“I think you’ve got it. I think you haven’t figured out yet whether to weaponize it or heal with it.”

Madeline swallows that. The silence between them is *tense*, but not toxic.

**MADELINE (after a beat):**  
“Instagram’s not going to save Avril. But it might soften the blow.”

**SARAH (nods, grim):**  
“Good. Then keep your heels on their throats. But next time you walk into a precinct house? Don’t you dare lie about your name.”

Madeline lifts her chin, smirks faintly.

**MADELINE:**  
“You’d have done the same in my shoes.”

**SARAH (deadpan):**  
“I’d have lawyered up faster.”

They lock eyes. And for the first time today, there’s a flicker of **solidarity.**

**SARAH (turns to leave):**  
“Dinner’s on me tonight. And you’re ordering the wine. Expensive.”

**MADELINE (smiling slightly):**  
“Fifth-wave feminist approved?”

**SARAH:**  
“Just don’t hashtag it.”

---

**INT. CAVIAR & STONE – PRIVATE BOOTH – NIGHT**

**A fortress of velvet and champagne.** The kind of restaurant where a basic cocktail is forty bucks and no one blinks.  **Sarah Malcolm** wears an immaculate black blazer over a silk camisole. Diamond studs. Hair tied tight. **Power casual.  Madeline Quinlan** is a precise blade in burgundy. Minimalist. Perfect. Her heels cost more than some apartments in Bushwick.  The waiter pours them each a glass of **Pouilly-Fuissé** without asking. They let it breathe while slicing through **oysters with habanero mignonette**.

**SARAH (coolly):**  
“I ordered the wine. You just looked like the kind of woman who’d judge me if I picked Merlot.”

**MADELINE (not looking up):**  
“I do. And I’d post about it.”

**SARAH (dry):**  
“Jesus. Fifth-wave is mean.”

**MADELINE (without missing a beat):**  
“Third-wave drank cosmos and hoped the boys would catch up. Fifth-wave takes the check, the wine list, and the power.”

They clink glasses. It’s not warm. It’s **mutual recognition.**

**SARAH:**  
“Tell me something, Madeline. Did it ever occur to you that for a girl who’s practically allergic to trust, you threw your entire body into that fire last week?”

**MADELINE (knife-edge calm):**  
“You mean the sex dungeon, or the cops?”

**SARAH:**  
“Yes.”

**MADELINE (shrugs):**  
“I made a choice. Calculated the odds. Had the most to lose. Took the biggest swing. Isn’t that what the big boys always do?”

Sarah leans back. Studies her for a beat. Then nods, like, *touché.*

**SARAH (level):**  
“I’ve eaten men alive for less. I’ve seen girls broken for doing exactly what you did. And you? You walked out of that precinct with your head up.”

**MADELINE:**  
“My head was spinning. My ass hurt. My pride was bleeding. But yeah—I walked.”

**SARAH:**  
“Good. Because walking means you’re not done.”

Pause. Madeline sets down her glass, looks Sarah square in the eye.

**MADELINE:**  
“You think I’m gonna burn out.”

**SARAH (measured):**  
“I think you’re burning brighter than anyone in that damn building. And I think if you don’t figure out who you want to be on the other side of this—branding genius or human being—you’re going to end up dust in someone else’s press release.”

Madeline stares at her. Silent. Then:

**MADELINE (slow):**  
“You don’t just want me to survive this.”

**SARAH:**  
“No, Madeline. I want you to *win.* And not in that cold, surgical, calculated way you cling to. I mean actually win. With blood, and sweat, and something that might even look like joy.”

**MADELINE (quiet):**  
“You believe in me?”

**SARAH (turns):**  
“I’m investing. Belief’s extra.”

Madeline’s lips twitch. A smile? Maybe.

---

**INT. CAVIAR & STONE – PRIVATE BOOTH – NIGHT**

They’ve demolished the oysters, shared a moment of realness without killing each other, and the **check hasn’t come yet**—because **they're not done**.

The waiter reappears, silent as a ghost. Sarah barely looks up.

The check arrives. **$714.00.**

**SARAH (to waiter):**  
“We’re not ready. Dessert menu, please.”

**MADELINE (without missing a beat):**  
“Anything chocolate. And violent.”

The waiter nods like he’s been asked this before and disappears again.

**SARAH (mocking):**  
“Chocolate and violent. Christ. Did fifth-wave invent trauma cuisine?”

**MADELINE (deadpan):**  
“Only the useful kind. Bitterness adds flavor.”

Sarah eyes her for a long moment. The silence is not hostile. It’s **strategic pause.** A fencing match with no winner declared yet.

**SARAH:**  
“So tell me. Honestly. Are you okay?”

Madeline exhales. Not dramatically—**precisely.** Like air leaving a compression chamber.

**MADELINE:**  
“No. But I’m efficient.”

Sarah blinks once. *Brutal.* Accurate. That lands.

**SARAH:**  
“I used to say that too. Before I started crying during elevator rides.”

**MADELINE (soft):**  
“Do you still?”

**SARAH:**  
“No. I got promoted.”

**MADELINE (smirks):**  
“So this is my future?”

**SARAH (leans in):**  
“No, sweetheart. This is your test. And how you come out the other side? That’s your empire.”

The waiter returns and places **a flourless chocolate torte** with burnt caramel drizzle between them, along with **two spoons.** It looks lethal.  They don’t thank him. They’re locked in.  Sarah grabs the first spoonful and passes it across the table.

**SARAH:**  
“Let’s see if you fifth-wave brats can handle something sweet without setting it on fire.”

**MADELINE (taking the spoon, one eyebrow raised):**  
“We’ll see if you third-wave veterans can survive the aftertaste.”

They dig in.  **This is where the next phase begins.** Sugar, strategy, survival.

---

**INT. CAVIAR & STONE – PRIVATE BOOTH – NIGHT – DESSERT COURSE**

The **chocolate torte** is halfway gone, but the real indulgence is the conversation.

**SARAH (casual, but loaded):**  
“Just so we’re clear… I’m 57. I’ll be out of Island before I hit 60. Maybe sooner, if the next tour breaks me. That’s three years. Tops.”

Madeline pauses. Spoons another bite of the rich dessert, eyes on Sarah the whole time. She knows what’s coming. She’s already run the math.

**SARAH (firm):**  
“And if you don’t fuck up—if you keep that blade sharp, and you don’t cut yourself with it—I’ll recommend you for the SVP slot. Corner office. With my blessing.”

**MADELINE (without hesitation):**  
“I already calculated the odds on that.”

Sarah laughs. Full-on. The rare kind.

**SARAH:**  
“Of course you did. Jesus. You really are just like me.”

Madeline doesn’t smile. She nods once. **Acknowledgment. Acceptance.** Not flattery—**fact.**

**MADELINE:**  
“Minus the Long Island real estate, the husband, and the high-functioning ulcer.”

**SARAH:**  
“Give it time.”

They share another moment of quiet. Forks down now. The torte’s mostly untouched.

**SARAH (sincere):**  
“You’re already walking the line, Quinlan. And it’s thinner than you think. You’re brilliant. You’re dangerous. And you’ve got the nerve. But make no mistake—this is your one shot.”

**MADELINE:**  
“I’m aware.”

**SARAH:**  
“Then act like it. You don’t get to be brilliant and careless. Pick one.”

Madeline stares down the last bite of cake like it’s a chess move.

**MADELINE (quietly):**  
“Then I pick brilliant.”

Sarah slides the check to herself. Signed, sealed, expensed.

**SARAH:**  
“Good. Because this world doesn’t need another broken genius. It needs a fucking queen.”

They rise.  Madeline buttons her coat, polished and poised.  Sarah pulls on her gloves, a slow smirk creeping across her face.

**SARAH (as they exit):**  
“You’ll get that corner office, Madeline. Just make sure they don’t bury you in it first.”

**MADELINE:**  
“Already working the math on that, too.”

They step into the night.

---

**EXT. CAVIAR & STONE – SIDEWALK – NIGHT**

The wind bites. The street hums. They're bundled now, heels clicking on pavement, like two CEOs of two different centuries.  Sarah zips up her coat, then looks at Madeline, deadly serious.

**SARAH:**  
“One more thing before you vanish into whatever black helicopter or analytics cave you crawl into.”

**MADELINE (dry):**  
“That narrows it down to three.”

Sarah stops walking. Turns fully to face her.

**SARAH:**  
“Cremeans is taking the band to Tromsø.”

**MADELINE (blinks):**  
“Tromsø. Norway. Sure. Why not Reykjavik or a cave in Kazakhstan?”

**SARAH (shrugs):**  
“Hell if I know. But they want isolation, night skies, silence—probably moody inspiration and that Arctic indie cred. Whatever. I don’t care.”

She leans in.

**SARAH:**  
“You’re going with them.”

Madeline’s eyebrow arches.

**SARAH:**  
“You are the label. Over there, in that cold, black nothing—they are gods with guitars and no impulse control. You are the scalpel. Keep them clean. Ease their way. Cover their bills when appropriate. Forward the receipts. Keep the backend tight so we get a return on investment.”

Madeline gives a single nod. Silent. Calculating.

**SARAH:**  
“When they want to record a song with forty Icelandic throat singers and a feral choir of wolves, throw *commerce* in their face.”

**MADELINE:**  
“And when that fails?”

**SARAH (smiles cold):**  
“Guilt them with the brand. They built a $4 billion superstructure. Your job? Turn that into ten. By 2030. Nine billion minimum. For Island.”

Madeline’s breath forms a fog between them.

**MADELINE:**  
“So I’m not just babysitting artists. I’m running asset optimization for a legacy brand.”

**SARAH:**  
“You’re damn right. If they make noise, *we* make money. Ensure that.”

Beat. Madeline looks up toward the stars just beyond the skyline.

**MADELINE:**  
“What’s the weather like in Tromsø?”

**SARAH (already hailing a cab):**  
“Cold. Black. Expensive. Just like success.”

She climbs in, slams the door. The cab vanishes into traffic.  Madeline stands there for a moment.

**MADELINE (quietly, to herself):**  
“Let’s go make them gods.”

---

**INT. NYC YELLOW CAB – NIGHT**

The city glows outside, neon streaking across the cab window. Sarah Malcolm sits back, one arm draped over her purse, the other tapping silently at her phone.  The high-stakes conversation with Madeline still simmers in her blood. But now it’s just her, the city, and the echo of everything unsaid.

She opens her *HealthFirst* app. Scrolls. Hesitates.

**SARAH (mutters):**  
“Ten days from now. Just a checkup.”

Her thumb hovers, then taps *Confirm Appointment.*

**RECEPTIONIST (V.O. – earlier recorded line):**  
“Dr. Ellen Feinberg – General Practice. Long Island. Confirmed for Tuesday, 10:30 AM.”

Sarah exhales. Closes the app. Stares out the window at the blur of Manhattan retreating behind her.

**SARAH (to herself, low):**  
“No complaints. Just don’t feel right. That’s all.”

She doesn't say it to anyone else. Not yet. Just that quiet little confession into the buzzing void of a New York night.

---

**INT. SARAH MALCOLM’S HOME – BEDROOM – NIGHT**

Sarah is in bed, propped up by pillows, laptop glowing on her lap like a portal to Hell. Her husband is already snoring gently beside her, oblivious. The TV’s on low—muted rerun of *Frasier* nobody’s watching.

She scrolls.

> [!warning] Outlook
> **Inbox (47 Unread)**
> 
> * **SUBJ:** \[URGENT\] Island Legal Counsel \- Status on Avril
> * **SUBJ:** JetBlue receipts Tromsø
> * **SUBJ:** FWD: Unverified footage circulating Twitter
> * **SUBJ:** FYI: Jeff requesting updated NDAs
> * **SUBJ:** Internal: Avril – Bellevue admittance (sealed)


She opens one.

---

> [!note] Email
> **From:** Bennett King  
> **To:** Sarah Malcolm  
> **Time:** 11:47 PM  
> **Subject:** *Habeas filed. Gov’t on borrowed time.*
> 
> Sarah —
> 
> Filed the writ 20 minutes ago. Confirmed delivery to the clerk. They’ve got 72 hours. After that, it’s motion time.
> 
> I’ve been stonewalled by hospital admin. NYPD’s playing dumb. Someone’s tightening the lid on this.
> 
> Your girl’s in there, but she’s not free. Yet.
> 
> — BK


---

Sarah stares at the screen. Her fingers drum silently on the keyboard. She replies:

---

> [!note] Email
> **To:** Bennett King  
> **Subject:** Re: Habeas filed  
> **Sent:** 11:53 PM
> 
> Copy that.
> 
> Keep pressure on.
> 
> — Sarah


---

Then she opens her spreadsheet app.

* **Tromsø Projected Spend: $218,000**
* **Avril Legal Defense: $124,000 and climbing**
* **Public Relations Contingency Fund: Drained**

She scrolls. Reads. Stares.  And then she opens a blank document. Types just one line.

**“The band is burning.”**

She stares at it. Hits save. Closes the lid.

**SARAH (quietly):**  
“Ten more days. Then I figure out what’s wrong with me.”

Lights out.

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S HOME – HARLEM – NIGHT**

Heavy curtains sway gently in the open window. The city hums outside. Inside, *Art Blakey and the Jazz Messengers* pulse from a vintage sound system—brass and snare, slick and alive.  Bennett King—barefoot, in a white dress shirt, sleeves rolled, $200 tie tossed over the couch—is dancing.  Not the awkward kind. The *smooth* kind. The kind of dance that comes when your blood runs warm with victory and your legal mind just dropped a 3-pointer at the buzzer.

He takes a sip of Macallan, neat. He sways.  Documents and court filings are neatly stacked on the desk, lit by soft lamplight. The *writ of habeas corpus* sits front and center—signed, sealed, filed. A masterpiece.

**BENNETT (to himself, low):**  
“Got you in check, motherfuckers.”

His phone buzzes on the desk. He checks it.

**Text from Sarah:**

> [!note] iMessage
> “Keep pressure on.”  
> “— S.”


He smiles. Taps back:  

> [!note] iMessage
> “Pressure’s applied. Clock’s ticking.”


He tosses the phone down, claps once to the beat, spins on his heel, and mouths the next phrase of trumpet solo like he’s on stage at the Blue Note.

**BENNETT (laughing):**  
“Nobody on this island swings like me.”

He raises his glass to no one. Or maybe to the city.

**BENNETT:**  
“Let’s see what the state does with the clock winding down.”

---

**INT. NEW YORK COUNTY DISTRICT ATTORNEY’S OFFICE – CONFERENCE ROOM – MORNING**

The coffee is bitter. The bagels are stale. And the vibe is *tense*.

ADA **MARCOS REYES**, in his signature gray suit and razor-sharp part, stands at the head of the table, a fat manila folder in his hand—labeled **LAVIGNE, A. – CASE 7821-C**.

On the screen behind him, a muted slideshow rotates:  
– A photo of Avril in a nightclub, lips wrapped around a blunt.  
– A trashed hotel room with syringes on the nightstand.  
– A Snapchat screenshot with the caption “woke up still high lol.”  
– A Zoomed-in shot of a small glassine baggie on a bathroom floor.

Reyes scans the room. Legal assistants. A junior ADA. A narcotics liaison. SVU’s liaison detective. One or two people are visibly uncomfortable.

**REYES:**  
“We’ve got four hotel rooms that look like rejected *Breaking Bad* sets. Paraphernalia. Possible coke. Meth. Pills. Edibles. Glass. Ashes. Social media confirms public use.”

He tosses the folder on the table. It hits with a soft, deadly *flap*.

**REYES (cont’d):**  
“But here’s the problem. She’s currently curled up in a hospital bed with a trauma diagnosis and a psychiatrist assigned. Right now, the world sees her as a *victim*. Not a perp.”

Silence.

**REYES (cont’d):**  
“So I’m asking. Not as a headline-chaser. Not as someone with skin in the politics of this office. I’m asking as someone with one bar card and one brain:  *Can we actually prosecute this?*”

**ASSISTANT #1 (30s, tired):**  
“Technically? Yes. We’ve nailed people for less with worse evidence. But this? This’ll be national.”

**ASSISTANT #2:**  
“And international. She’s Canadian, remember. It’s not just U.S. media watching.”

**NARCOTICS LIAISON:**  
“Labs aren’t back yet. You charge now, you’re going in thin. You wait? Story cools. Maybe public’s more open.”

**JUNIOR ADA:**  
“She OD’d. We don’t know how many guys she had sex with. There’s trauma. Potential rape.  If we go after her, the narrative becomes: *‘Manhattan DA criminalizes survivors.’* That’s bad optics.”

**REYES (quietly):**  
“So we’re boxed in by her PR, not her conduct.”

More silence.

**SVU DETECTIVE (finally speaks):**  
“You *can* charge her. But you’ll be crucified in the press, and I’ll be sitting across from you at your next ethics review hearing when the rape angle rears back up. Be smart, Marcos.”

Reyes closes his eyes for a beat. Then he walks to the window, looks down at the rush of New York below.

**REYES (to no one in particular):**  
“She spiraled. She scorched half the city. But now she’s in a hospital gown. And the world loves a redemption arc.”

Beat.

**REYES (turning back):**  
“Okay. We shelve the felony indictments. For now. But we’re keeping this file hot.”

He taps the folder.

**REYES:**  
“If she gets clean? We get closure.  If she doesn’t?  We drop this thing like a fucking hammer.”

---

**INT. DA’S OFFICE – CONFERENCE ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

Reyes turns back to the table, rubbing his temples. He looks less like a prosecutor and more like a man who can hear a freight train approaching in the distance.

**REYES:**  
"Alright. Let’s not pretend we didn’t see this coming. We all got the writ from Bennett King last night. Habeas corpus. It’s locked, loaded, and stamped. So how the hell are we going to process this?"

He walks over, picks up a legal pad, flips a few pages. No answers there either.

**REYES (cont’d):**  
“I can hear the clock. *Tick. Tock.* Can you hear it? I sure as hell can.”

**JUNIOR ADA:**  
“We’ve got seventy-two hours, maybe less. The hospital has her under psychiatric watch, which gives us some wiggle room—mental health codes, involuntary hold. But the writ changes everything. Now we’re going to need to justify every damn second she stays where she is.”

**ASSISTANT #1:**  
“If we don’t push back hard, a judge could hand her over to King with a ribbon on top. And if that happens? We lose any shot at building the case from the inside. She's gone, wrapped in legal silk.”

**SVU DETECTIVE:**  
“And the press’ll eat it up. ‘Justice delayed, justice denied.’ They'll frame it like she was held hostage by the system.”

Reyes looks up—dead serious.

**REYES:**  
“Bennett King didn't file that writ to test our resolve. He filed it because he knows we’re exposed. This is check. Next move is mate.”

He turns to the room.

**REYES (low, calm):**  
“So unless anyone has a judge in their back pocket or a legal rabbit to pull, I need a strategy. I need it *now*. Because when we walk into court tomorrow, we either hold her, or we let the whole damn thing slip away.”

Beat.

**REYES (sharper):**  
“Tick. Tock.”

---

**INT. DA’S OFFICE – CONFERENCE ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

The room is tense. Reyes paces. The air's thick with frustration and strategy. That ticking clock isn't just metaphorical anymore—it’s a drumbeat they’re marching toward.

**ASSISTANT #2 (leaning forward, carefully):**  
"Then we go at it like this—we play guardian angel. We don’t say she’s a criminal. Not yet. We say she’s a danger to herself. Look at the toxicology report—she was hammered as *fuck*. Blood alcohol at .23. Meth. Cocaine. Benzos. Track marks. You name it, it was in her."

Reyes doesn’t move, but he’s listening.

**ASSISTANT #2 (cont’d):**  
"She's a menace. Not to society—yet—but to herself. And that gives us the leverage. We paint ourselves as stepping in *not* to punish, but to protect."

**JUNIOR ADA:**  
"Lean on the public health codes. Emergency commitment. Psychiatric stabilization. Frame it as compassionate. We’re not locking her up, we’re keeping her alive."

**SVU DETECTIVE:**  
"She nearly got eaten by rats. That practically writes the brief for us. You don’t let someone walk out of Bellevue and straight into another overdose."

Reyes finally stops pacing.

**REYES:**  
"Okay. I can sell that—for now. But understand this: we’re walking a razor. If this turns… if even a shred of this feels like persecution to the public, we’ll be crucified in the court of opinion."

Beat.

**REYES (quietly, to himself):**  
"And King knows that. He’s counting on it."

He taps the table twice, decisive.

**REYES (aloud):**  
"Alright, let’s prep it. She’s not a criminal. She’s a patient. A very sick one. And we’re the only thing between her and a body bag. We go to court with that. Let’s see if the judge wants her story ending in a morgue or a hospital bed."

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S HOME OFFICE – EARLY MORNING**

The room is silent, save for the rhythmic clack of mechanical keyboard keys. Jazz plays faintly from a Bluetooth speaker in the corner—Coltrane, because it matches the mood: calm, cool, surgical.  Bennett leans over his desk. Perfect posture. Tailored shirt. $10,000 robe tossed over the chair. The 30-page document on his screen is locked, loaded, and ruthless.

He’s not just writing a motion. He’s sharpening a scalpel.

**BENNETT (murmuring to himself):**  
"She’s not a menace. She’s a citizen. And unless the state can prove imminent harm, they’re overreaching… again."

He scrolls to page 17—footnotes. Ironclad precedent. New York case law, 2014, 2017, and the killer line: *Involuntary hold does not constitute carte blanche to detain an individual indefinitely without clear judicial review.*

Bennett smiles. Just the corner of his mouth lifts.

**BENNETT (to himself, smooth):**  
"Tick-tock, Reyes."

He stands, prints two copies on his personal laser printer. One for court, one for the media—because he knows exactly how this plays if they try to smear his client publicly.

The cover page reads:

> [!abstract] COVER PAGE
> **EMERGENCY PETITION FOR WRIT OF HABEAS CORPUS**  
> On Behalf of Madeline Quinlan & Associates  
> Respectfully Submitted by Bennett D. King, Esq.


He signs the last page in a flourish with his Montblanc. The pen glides. The ink dries. The storm is coming.

He texts his paralegal:  **“Final copy done. Scan, submit, and alert the clerk. This drops in court at 9AM sharp. Make sure the media copy gets to the usual inboxes. Also, let the hospital counsel know—we’re coming.”**

Then he sips his coffee. Black, no sugar. Like the day he’s about to deliver.

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S HOME OFFICE – MOMENTS LATER**

The jazz track is still looping, but now it’s background noise. White noise for an apex mind working at full tilt.  Bennett freezes mid-step on his way to the printer, his mind catching something. He pivots—physically and intellectually.

**BENNETT (low, almost laughing):**  
"Wait a second… she's not a citizen."

He stands still, eyes narrowing. Then the machine turns back on, and the gears start grinding at double-speed. His pulse doesn’t change. His breathing remains controlled. But his brain? Firestorm.

**BENNETT (softly, dangerous):**  
"Avril fucking Lavigne is Canadian."

He walks slowly back to the desk and sits down, a fresh legal pad pulled out. A new tab opens on his screen. He begins typing, scribbling, building a new theory of attack.

**BENNETT (muttering as he types):**  
"Not a citizen. Not protected under Fourteenth Amendment due process the same way. Not subject to all constitutional presumptions… but also…"

He pauses. That predator’s smile creeps back.

**BENNETT:**  
"…also not under the same jurisdictional assumptions. *Any* action taken by the state against her must now be validated through the lens of international law and foreign national protections. She is not an American being held. She is a *Canadian national* being detained on American soil, without charge, without trial, without access to her consulate."

He opens another tab—Vienna Convention on Consular Relations. Article 36.

He highlights:

> [!attention] IMPORTANT
> "If a national of a foreign state is arrested or detained, the competent authorities of the receiving State shall, without delay, inform the consular post of the sending State."


**BENNETT (cold):**  
"And have they done that, Reyes? Have they called Ottawa?"

He starts revising the writ. It’s no longer just about unlawful detention. It’s about *violating international treaty law*. He’s now got standing not just in city court—but potentially federal court, and if necessary, international arbitration.  This is the move no one saw coming. Not the hospital. Not the DA. Not even the press.

He types a note to his paralegal:  **“Change of strategy. Avril Lavigne is a foreign national. Bring me the Vienna Convention and all federal precedents re: international detainees. I want it in my hands in an hour.”**

He smiles, this time with satisfaction.

**BENNETT (softly):**  
"They’re playing checkers. I’m rewriting the fucking rulebook."

---

**EXT. CONSULATE GENERAL OF CANADA – NEW YORK CITY – EARLY AFTERNOON**

A pale limestone building near the UN complex. Polished, quiet, dignified — utterly unprepared for what’s about to arrive.

---

**INT. CANADIAN CONSULATE – VISA & LEGAL SERVICES FLOOR – MOMENTS LATER**

**CONSULAR OFFICER MARIA ST. CYR**, 30s, sharp, bilingual, dressed in the perfectly casual-but-official attire of the diplomatic class, is sipping lukewarm Tim Hortons coffee and fighting inbox fatigue.

Ping.  

**Subject Line:** *URGENT: VIENNA CONVENTION VIOLATION – NATIONAL IN DETENTION*

She clicks.  She reads.  She goes pale.

**ST. CYR (murmuring):**  
“…Avril Ramona Lavigne?”

She reads further. The name *Bennett King* carries weight. The language is acid-dipped legalese — and airtight.

* **Detained without charge.**
* **Denied consular access.**
* **Sexual assault survivor status.**
* **Held under medical supervision without due notification to Canadian authorities.**
* **Potential breach of Articles 36 and 37 of the Vienna Convention.**

**ST. CYR (picking up the phone):**  
“Get me Legal. Now. And someone tell Ottawa we’ve got an international incident. Again.”

---

**INT. CANADIAN EMBASSY – OTTAWA – MINUTES LATER**

A junior attaché drops a file on **DEPUTY FOREIGN MINISTER REBECCA LIU’s** desk. She reads the cover. Then the name.

She stares.

**LIU:**  
“Jesus Christ, someone actually detained Avril Lavigne in New York without calling us?”  

(a beat)  
“This is going to make Hockey Night in Canada look like a church picnic.”

She slams the file shut and starts making calls.

---

**INT. CONSULATE GENERAL – CONFERENCE ROOM – LATER THAT AFTERNOON**

The Canadian legal team is assembled. Their mood? *War room.*

**ST. CYR (clicking through slides):**  
“She's a high-profile national. The optics of this are radioactive. Held without formal charges, no consular contact, and possibly subject to sexual assault or trauma while under medical observation.”

**LEGAL COUNSEL (flipping through papers):**  
“We’ve got a right to demand access. This is textbook violation. And if the NYPD or DA’s office tries to stonewall us…”

**ST. CYR:**  
“Then we take it public. Trudeau won’t let this hang. Not with an election in 18 months and Quebec already screaming about sovereignty.”

**LEGAL COUNSEL (calmly):**  
“Draft the formal diplomatic protest. Reference the Vienna Convention and international precedent. Then deliver it. Tomorrow morning. Face-to-face.”

---

**INT. NYPD HEADQUARTERS – LEGAL AFFAIRS – THE NEXT MORNING**

The knock on the door isn’t loud, but it carries diplomatic weight.

The **Deputy Commissioner of Legal Affairs** opens the door and finds **Consular Officer St. Cyr** and two sharply dressed Canadian attorneys in crisp black suits, holding a leather-bound brief with a gold-embossed maple leaf.

**ST. CYR (firmly):**  
“You are detaining one of our citizens. You have 24 hours to justify that, or Avril Lavigne leaves this city under diplomatic protection. Your move.”

**JUNIOR ADA:**
Uh, you need to talk to my boss.

**ST. CYR (cool, professional):**  
“Perfect. Then please go get them. I’ll wait.”

She offers a tight, diplomatic smile — the kind honed from years of being spoken over by men in gray suits and still coming out ahead. Her Canadian legal team stays silent, but there's steel in their posture. The brief in her hands thumps lightly on the desk — not loud, but deliberate.

**ST. CYR:**  
“Tell them the Canadian government is invoking Article 36 of the Vienna Convention. And tell them this isn't just a detained citizen. It's Avril Lavigne. Our Avril. This has become a diplomatic issue now. So, I hope your boss knows how to play chess. Because we just moved our queen.”

The American officer, caught between protocol and oh-my-God, nods stiffly and bolts from the room.

**CANADIAN LAWYER (quietly, to St. Cyr):**  
“You always this theatrical?”

**ST. CYR (without looking):**  
“She used to be on a postage stamp. I’m playing to win.”

---

**JUNIOR ADA:**
Hey boss, I think we're being invaded.

**REYES (blinking hard, already sipping his morning coffee):**  
"What the *fuck* did you just say?"

The junior ADA, flushed and jittery, shuffles into the doorway like he’s carrying a live grenade.

**JUNIOR ADA:**  
"Uh… not literally invaded, sir. Not, like, tanks or Mounties or anything. But the Canadian Consulate just sent a diplomat. Full diplomatic brief. Lawyered up. Demanding to see Avril. They're citing the Vienna Convention."

**REYES (leaning back, stunned):**  
"Jesus. They *played the Vienna card*? On us? For *her*?"

**JUNIOR ADA:**  
"Sir, they had it ready. Thirty pages. A binder. Color-coded tabs. There’s a woman down there who looks like she personally trained under Chrystia Freeland. She’s got that 'I’m-about-to-ruin-your-career-politely' energy."

**REYES (mutters):**  
"…And here I thought Bennett King was the problem."

**JUNIOR ADA (quiet):**  
"Sir… they brought *two* lawyers."

**REYES (grabs his coat, sighs):**  
"Of course they did. Let’s go meet the nice people who want to burn down the Southern District of New York with courtesy and Commonwealth smiles."

---

**INT. MANHATTAN DISTRICT ATTORNEY’S OFFICE – CONFERENCE ROOM – MORNING**

The glass walls glint with sun, reflecting the buzz of downtown outside. Inside: icy calm.

**REYES** enters with two junior assistants in his wake. He’s cleaned up, composed, but there's a storm behind his eyes.  At the table: **ST. CYR**, Canadian consular officer, calm as a lake in winter. Beside her, a pair of lean, efficient Canadian attorneys — one with a pen poised, the other already tapping something into a tablet.  A manila folder sits before her like a loaded gun.

**REYES (smiling without smiling):**  
“Good morning. ADA Marco Reyes, Southern District. I hear you’ve got some thoughts.”

**ST. CYR (pleasantly):**  
“Indeed. Ms. Lavigne is a Canadian citizen. She has not been formally charged. She has been denied unfettered consular access. She is being medically restrained and observed in a facility without legal representation.”

**REYES:**  
“She’s a danger to herself. That’s why she’s under medical supervision. Not jail.”

**ST. CYR (smooth):**  
“And yet she’s cuffed. Interrogated. Photographed. Subjected to multiple body searches. And your NYPD officers never contacted us. That, Mr. Reyes, is a *serious* breach of Article 36 of the Vienna Convention.”

**REYES (leaning forward):**  
“With all due respect, Consul, this is not an embassy. This is Manhattan. We have protocols. She was recovered from a public health crisis in an abandoned subway station.”

**ST. CYR (ice):**  
“She’s still Canadian. And unless New York has declared independence, your jurisdiction stops at the rights we are guaranteed under international law.”

**CANADIAN LAWYER #1 (adds quietly):**  
"And you’ve already violated them. Multiple times."

**REYES (tight):**  
“You’re really going to take this international? Over a rock star on a weeklong bender?”

**ST. CYR (finally letting the smile fade):**  
“No. Not over a rock star. Over a citizen. That’s the difference between your office and mine.”

Silence.

**ST. CYR (continuing):**  
“We’re requesting immediate access. If denied, this escalates to Ottawa. And from there, to Washington.”

**REYES (mutters, then louder):**  
“Fine. You want access, you’ll get it. But understand something: we’re not intimidated by diplomatic theatrics.”

**ST. CYR (rising):**  
“And we’re not afraid of American paperwork. Have a lovely day, Mr. Reyes.”

She exits. The Canadian lawyers follow without a glance back. The door hisses closed.

**JUNIOR ADA (to Reyes, stunned):**  
“Did we just get our ass handed to us by Canada?”

**REYES:**  
“…Don’t say it out loud.”

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S OFFICE – MIDTOWN MANHATTAN – LATE MORNING**

Immaculate office. Hardwood floors, vintage jazz humming on low from hidden speakers. Bennett, in a deep blue bespoke suit, is sipping espresso from a tiny white porcelain cup, reading the Wall Street Journal on his tablet.

**PHONE VIBRATES.**  
Caller ID: **ST. CYR – CANADIAN CONSULATE**

Bennett smirks and swipes to answer.

**BENNETT KING (cool, crisp):**  
“St. Cyr. I was just about to call. How’d my fine friends treat you?”

**ST. CYR (voice tight with fury):**  
“You let them *body search* her?”

**BENNETT (not surprised):**  
“Oh, *they* did that. I didn’t sign the warrant. I’m just the janitor. I clean up after the mess.”

**ST. CYR:**  
“She’s been chained, examined, interrogated without representation, and now your ADA is trying to play the ‘mental health detainment’ card like this is Arkansas in 1952.”

**BENNETT (calm):**  
“Marco Reyes is overplaying his hand. He wants to charge her with everything except shooting JFK. But I warned him.”

**ST. CYR (sharp):**  
“And now I’ve warned *you*. Ottawa is livid. The Prime Minister’s Office already knows. This is a diplomatic firestorm. If we don’t get resolution within the next 24 hours, this becomes federal. I’m talking State Department, DOD, and the press.”

**BENNETT (chuckles, sips espresso):**  
“Just say the word, and I’ll fax Reyes a copy of the Geneva Conventions, annotated.”

**ST. CYR (not amused):**  
“This is not a game.”

**BENNETT (suddenly serious):**  
“No, it’s not. I’m handling it. But you need to understand something. New York’s a pitbull. You bark, it bites. That’s the rhythm of the city.”

**ST. CYR:**  
“Then tame your pitbull. Or I will.”

**BENNETT:**  
“Not my job.”

Pause. Then:

**BENNETT:**  
“Keep me looped in. I’ve got moves left.”

**ST. CYR:**  
“You’d better.”

Call ends. Bennett sets the phone down. The jazz continues, but he doesn’t hear it.  He leans back. The calm fades.  He knows: **This just went nuclear.**  Cut to him reaching for his *red folder*. The one marked:  **INTERNATIONAL INCIDENT – AVRIL.**

---

**INT. BENNETT KING’S OFFICE – MIDTOWN – 3:53 P.M.**

Bennett King leans back in his leather chair, steeples his fingers, and gazes out over the skyline like a general surveying the battlefield. The Canadian consulate call still lingers in the air, but now he sees a new weapon at his disposal.

**BENNETT (to himself, amused):**  
“International incident by supper. Goddamn. That’s got a ring to it.”

He swivels slowly, opens his desk drawer, and pulls out a clean legal pad. Across the top he scribbles:  
**OPERATIONS – DIPLOMATIC LEVERAGE.**

Beneath that:

1. **Leverage Consulate**

2. **Media Application – Quinlan**

3. **Trigger Press Cascade**

4. **Apply Political Pressure to NYPD & DA’s Office**

5. **Discredit Mental Health Hold as Cover**

He circles #2 twice.

**BENNETT (smiling):**  
“Madeline Quinlan. Sharp as a whip, owes me her freedom, and knows how to move markets with a tweet.”

He picks up his phone and taps her contact. It rings once.

**MADELINE (cool, cautious):**  
“This is Quinlan.”

**BENNETT (silky smooth):**  
“I’ve got a job for you. You’re going to help me bend international public opinion without breaking a nail.”

**MADELINE:**  
“I assume this is about Avril.”

**BENNETT:**  
“You assume correctly. I need a little show of force. Something tasteful. Something terrifying. Something that says, ‘Canada knows. And they’re watching.’ Think you can manage that?”

**MADELINE (deadpan):**  
“Are you asking me to go nuclear?”

**BENNETT:**  
“Nah. Just tactical. Controlled detonation. I need hashtags. I need visibility. I need a journalist or two asking questions at the State Department podium tomorrow morning.”

Pause. Madeline considers.

**MADELINE:**  
“What do I get?”

**BENNETT (grinning):**  
“Your continued freedom. And maybe a corner office someday if Sarah Malcolm doesn’t drop dead first.”

Silence. Then:

**MADELINE:**  
“Check your inbox in 90 minutes.”

Bennett hangs up, still grinning.

**BENNETT (to himself):**  
“Checkmate in three… two…”

He taps his Montblanc pen twice against the legal pad.

**BENNETT:**  
“And Reyes thought he was playing chess. I'm playing Risk, baby. Whole continents at once.”

He reaches for his jacket.

Because it’s 3:57 p.m.  And dinner reservations are at six.  And by then…**This whole fucking city will know.**

---

**INT. MADELINE’S APARTMENT – BROOKLYN – EARLY EVENING**

Madeline Quinlan sits cross-legged on her overpriced designer couch, her MacBook open, her iPhone in one hand, a glass of overpriced Riesling untouched on the table. The screen is a graveyard of failed hashtags.  She taps the back of her phone like it’s a magic eight-ball. No luck.

**MADELINE (muttering):**  
“#CanadaDeclaresWar? On what—bagels and mental health holds?”  
“#YouBeasts? Jesus, what am I, a Tumblr poet?”  
“#SaveOurGirls? Yeah, and bring back Boko Haram flashbacks. No thanks.”

She opens a blank tab, searches: *‘viral protest hashtags that don’t suck.’*

**MADELINE (dryly):**  
“Oh yeah, Google, tell me how to overthrow a system with three syllables and a pound sign.”

She paces. Her eyes land on a framed print on her wall: *“She who controls the narrative controls the world.”*

She stops.

**MADELINE (quiet):**  
“Control the narrative.”

She sits. Types:

**\#NotYourPatient**

She stares at it. Her pupils dilate.

**MADELINE:**  
“Not. Your. Patient.”

Her hands fly.

* *\#NotYourPatient*
* *\#HandsOffAvril*
* *\#ForeignNotFermented*
* *\#InternationalIncident*
* *\#She’sCanadianYouFucks*

She deletes that last one. Sighs. Then retypes it.

**MADELINE (grinning):**  
“Oh, that’s definitely going in the drafts folder.”

She starts scheduling posts using alt accounts, starting slow—whispers, rumors. Then she cues a viral-ready campaign.  She stares out the window, watching the skyline flicker.

**MADELINE (to herself):**  
“Let’s see who notices first—State, X, or the fucking Queen of England.”

The wine stays untouched.  Because she’s not drinking tonight.  She’s launching a war.

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS WAR ROOM – EVENING**

Madeline is alone now. Lights dimmed. Twenty alt accounts are chirping. The dopamine loop is real. Her MacBook pings.

**PING.**  
A notification on her TweetDeck.

She narrows her eyes.  
The royal seal.  
**@ClarenceHouseOfficial.**

**KING CHARLES III HAS RETWEETED #NotYourPatient.**

**MADELINE (in stunned disbelief):**  
“No. No fucking way.”

She clicks through.  Yup. Blue check. Official. It's the real thing.

**KING CHARLES’ COMMENT:**  
*"We must treat all persons with dignity and humanity. Borders do not excuse brutality. #NotYourPatient"*

The internet erupts like a Yellowstone geyser. Alt accounts light up. 4chan’s losing its mind. Reddit front-pages it in three minutes. BBC picks it up. Fox News calls it a false flag. TikTok teens start remixing it to Billie Eilish.  Madeline closes her laptop slowly. Stands up like she’s walking away from a chessboard she just flipped.

**MADELINE (to no one):**  
“Game. Fucking. On.”

Cut to black.  Cue synth.  
Title card: **“INTERNATIONAL INCIDENT: THE DOCUMENTARY”**  

Coming soon.

---

**INT. RED ROOSTER HARLEM – NIGHT**

Bennett King sits at a booth draped in elegance—mahogany and history. He's got the best seat in the house, tailored navy suit sharp as a scalpel, tie relaxed, collar open. Before him: jerk-spiced lamb, plantain mash, and a Bordeaux that costs more than a small car payment.

The jazz band in the corner is smooth and low. The sax breathes like it's seen things. A faint hum of voices surrounds him—tourists, locals, power players, ghosts of Harlem’s past.

**TV overhead flashes:**

*BREAKING: CANADIAN CONSULATE DEMANDS ACCESS TO POP STAR*  
*STATE DEPARTMENT: “NO COMMENT AT THIS TIME”*

He sips. No rush. Flavor blooms. He watches the chyron roll across CNN like it’s the score of a game he’s already won.

**BENNETT KING (murmurs to himself, grinning):**  
“Predictable as a two-card flop.”

He reaches into his inner jacket pocket, retrieves a napkin. Not linen. Not cloth. Paper. White and precise. Scrawled on it: **\#NotYourPatient** — the hashtag that ignited it all.

He didn’t write it. But he knows who did.

He can smell her.

**BENNETT (quietly, like a toast):**  
“You firestarter, you.”

The wine goes down easy. Harlem air is rich with food, sweat, power, and revolution.  He reclines.  Tonight, Harlem eats well.  
Tonight, the world learns the rules were written in Manhattan.

**FADE OUT.**  

**JAZZ CONTINUES.**

---

**EXT. ROOFTOP BAR – LATE AFTERNOON**

The skyline of Manhattan stretches like a jagged heartbeat against the chill blue sky. Bill and Jeff sit with their jackets zipped, tumblers of deep amber bourbon in hand. A single space heater hums beside them, casting a flicker of orange warmth across their faces.

The phones are out. The feeds are flying. Hashtags rage. Canada. Consulates. Charles. Chaos.

**BILL (blinking at the screen):**  
"I didn’t know she had it in her."

**JEFF (raising his glass, just a notch):**  
"Neither did I."

**CREMEANS (off to the side, stepping in with a Mountain Dew in one hand, phone in the other):**  
"I *really* didn’t know she had it in her either."

He takes a sip, then plants his feet like he’s delivering the gospel.

**CREMEANS (matter-of-factly):**  
"She’s a stone-cold killer. She’s John Wick with a social media account. Don’t ever mistake her for anything other than a warlord… ever again, gentlemen."

A gust of wind rolls by. None of them flinch.

They watch the sun dip behind the skyline like it knows something they don’t.

And somewhere in the digital wilds, **Madeline Quinlan** is setting the world on fire—one tweet at a time.

---

**INT. LIRR TRAIN – EARLY EVENING**

Sarah sits by the window, coat draped over her lap, the soft *click-clack* of the train soothing like a pulse. Outside, Long Island blurs by—strip malls, trees half-bare, shadows lengthening as evening creeps in.

Her iPhone glows in her hand. One tab open: Twitter. Another: Telegram. Another: Instagram. All roads lead to one destination—**Madeline Quinlan**, in full flight.

The girl isn't just running hot. She’s in overdrive, dragging hashtags behind her like blades, slicing through institutions, diplomacy, decorum. Tagging everyone from CNN to the Canadian PM to the NYPD with the same ruthless energy. She's not subtle. Not even trying to be. And the responses?  **Viral. Fire. Dangerous. Brilliant.**

Sarah leans her temple against the cool glass of the train window. Watches her reflection tremble in the light.

**SARAH (thinking):**  
*Subtlety?*

She flips back to the home screen. Another post drops. **\#UnshackleAvrilNow**. A slick edit. Madeline's fingerprints are all over it.

Sarah exhales through her nose.

**SARAH (thinking):**  
*No. Not now. This isn’t subtle time. This is burn-it-down time.*

She doesn’t text. Doesn’t call. Doesn’t warn her. She just watches, calm, deliberate. Like a general who sees her protégé go feral in the best possible way.

**SARAH (thinking):**  
*Run the campaign, mini-me. Light it up. Let’s see what you’ve got.*

The train rumbles on into the deepening dusk.

---

**INT. MADELINE’S APARTMENT – BROOKLYN – NIGHT**

Her bare feet pad silently across the hardwood floor. A mug of untouched herbal tea steams beside her laptop. The lights are dim. The screen glow casts harsh shadows on her face—eyelids tight, jaw clenched, pupils sharp. The war room vibe is real.

Madeline Quinlan is not doing this for optics anymore. Not for her resumé. Not for Island Records. Not for the band.

This is personal.

She rolls her neck, cracks her knuckles, and pulls up a split-screen. Eight tabs. Eight regions. North America. EU. UK. Latin America. MENA. South Asia. East Asia. Oceania.

**MADELINE (murmuring):**  
“You want a reckoning? You get a reckoning in eight time zones.”

She begins with **Europe**—classic, clean, political.  Tweets targeted at EuroNews, The Guardian, DW, La Repubblica.  A hard-edged statement: *"When women save lives, the system responds with gloves and suspicion. This is how the West eats its young. #UnshackleAvril #HumanRightsViolated"*

Shift to **East Asia**—she tailors tone and platform. Weibo? Check. LINE for Japan? Check. Twitter/X still hits Korea.  
*"Even K-pop stars get dignity. Where’s Avril’s?* #JusticeForAvril"

Then to **the Middle East and North Africa**—Arabic hashtags, Google Translate with editorial nuance, reposting on Telegram.  
*"A woman suffers, alone and unprotected. How long do we stay silent?"*

**India.**  
A blend of Bollywood and outrage:  *"Avril isn’t just a pop star. She’s a woman with a story. And right now, it’s being silenced. #IndiaSupportsAvril"*

**South America.**  
Drama. Passion. Blunt fire.  *"She was stripped of her rights and her dignity. This is not justice. It’s vengeance."*

**Back to North America.**  
She drafts a full-length blog for Medium. Submits a guest op-ed to the *Toronto Star*. Posts a dramatic video clip—slow motion rat footage from underground New York City. Sliced in with Avril’s tour footage. It’s devastating.

**MADELINE (quietly, to herself):**  
“They strip us down, search us, humiliate us—because we were the ones who didn’t run.”

She pauses. Scrolls through headlines. She sees it growing.

**\#UnshackleAvril**  
**\#CanadaVsNYPD**  
**\#ThisIsWhatWeDoToHeroes**

She’s not satisfied.  No. This isn’t *Pearl Harbor*.  This is *Hiroshima*.  And she's the Enola Gay.

---

**INT. STATE DEPARTMENT – WASHINGTON, D.C. – NIGHT**

The soft whirr of filtered air. Distant phones ringing. And at the center of it all, a man in a tailored navy-blue suit, hunched over his phone under the recessed glow of his office desk.

**Secretary of State Antony Blinken** stares at the trending tab. For a moment, his thumb hovers over the glowing blue button. He reads it again.

**\#UnshackleAvril**

He watches the clip Madeline curated—rat footage, Avril stumbling underground, a slow fade to black. The voiceover? That line: *"We strip our heroes, not for justice, but to remind them they don’t own their bodies anymore."*

It’s potent. Calculated. Brutal.  Blinken leans back. He knows this moment is radioactive. But the optics are clear: human rights. A Canadian citizen. A global icon. And now—viral. He can feel the ground shifting.  He doesn't call his chief of staff.  He doesn’t wait.  He hits retweet.

**@AntonyBlinken:**  
*“Due process must be honored. Human dignity must never be optional. #UnshackleAvril”*

---

Somewhere, Madeline sees the notification. Her eyes widen. Her jaw locks.

**MADELINE (quietly):**  
Checkmate.

---

**INT. DISTRICT ATTORNEY’S OFFICE – LOWER MANHATTAN – NIGHT**

The fluorescent lights buzz softly above the stillness of a once-busy office. ADA **Reyes** is pouring over transcripts and internal memos when his phone rings. The screen flashes:

**DEPUTY MAYOR R. HENDERSON – MOBILE**

He sighs and answers.

**REYES (dryly):**  
“This better be about the Knicks finally winning a playoff game.”

**DEPUTY MAYOR (gravelly, stressed):**  
“Reyes, it’s 11:30. And I just got off a call with someone from the *State Department*, and let me put this as politely as I can…”

**REYES:**  
“Can’t wait.”

**DEPUTY MAYOR:**  
“You’ve got the Secretary of State tweeting hashtags, the *King of fucking England* sharing dissident memes, and a goddamn international incident brewing in Midtown. You wanna throw hands with Ottawa next? Because I don’t.”

**REYES:**  
“She’s got pending toxicology. Multiple hotels worth of evidence. The drugs, the social media—”

**DEPUTY MAYOR (cutting him off):**  
“She’s *Canadian*, Reyes. She’s *handcuffed* to a hospital bed. And now there’s a *global* microscope aimed at your desk. So here’s my suggestion, as someone who enjoys not having protesters camped on the steps of City Hall!

**Find. A. Way. Out.**

**REYES (quiet, seething):**  
“Co-equal branches. Executive, judicial, legislative. You remember that part?”

**DEPUTY MAYOR:**  
“Sure. But only *one* of them gets assassinated by hashtags in real time.”

**(beat)**

**DEPUTY MAYOR (softening, almost fatherly):**  
“You’ve got options. Deferred prosecution. Medical furlough. Some kind of human dignity clause. Just don’t die on this hill. Not when the entire fucking internet is watching.”

**REYES (low, resigned):**  
“Copy that.”

**DEPUTY MAYOR:**  
“Good. Now get some sleep. Tomorrow’s going to be biblical.”

**\[Click.\]**

Reyes leans back. Looks at the wall.

Then mutters, **“…King Charles, though?”**

He shakes his head.

Blackout.

---

**INT. OFFICE OF THE ADA – 4:27 A.M. – LOWER MANHATTAN**

The fluorescent lights flicker on, and the groggy faces of a half-dozen legal staff, investigators, and assistants shuffle into the room, bundled in hoodies, windbreakers, and sour expressions.

**REYES** is already there, suit pressed, tie on, sipping from a black thermos that reads *“TRUST ME, I’M THE LAW.”* He looks at the wall clock.

**REYES:**  
“Three minutes, people. If this was a bust, you'd be cuffing someone right now.”

A beat.

**REYES (continuing):**  
“I said 4:30. Not 4:31. Not ‘I stopped for a bacon, egg, and cheese’ time. Not ‘my cat knocked over my alarm’ time.”

**ASSISTANT ADA (half-awake):**  
“I brought donuts. Real ones. From Astoria.”

**REYES (nods):**  
“You’re safe.”

He paces the front of the room, dropping folders on the table.

**REYES:**  
“We’ve got the Canadians breathing down our necks, State Department signaling through Twitter, and a goddamn royal family member playing PR chess from across the Atlantic.”

**(Beat)**

**REYES:**  
“She’s still in the hospital, still under observation, still Canadian, and still technically not charged with a goddamn thing.”

Someone opens a box of coffee. The smell briefly revives the room.

**REYES (flatly):**  
“We’ve got a decision to make. And we’ve got about 90 minutes before the sun comes up and we all get dragged on *Morning Joe.*”

He flips open a file folder.

**REYES:**  
“Now. Let’s talk options. Let’s talk optics. And let’s make sure when the world wakes up—we don’t look like a bunch of colonial jackasses hogtying a Canadian pop star.”

The room rustles. Laptops boot. Coffee is poured.

It's gonna be *that* kind of morning.

**REYES (rubbing his temples):**  
"Okay. We lost the media cycle. We’re getting our teeth kicked in by a Twitter hashtag, a monarchy, and a goddamn Floridian with a passport stamp. So here’s what we do."

He slams a fresh file on the table, hard enough to jolt a junior ADA’s coffee.

**REYES:**  
"Option one — we release her. Not full walkout-the-front-door. Controlled. Monitored. Medical transfer. We make it look like we’re listening to international concern, humanitarian voices, diplomacy. She’s still technically under investigation. She’s still our case. But we take her off the stage."

**INVESTIGATOR (groggy, flipping pages):**  
"House arrest. Private facility. Still in our jurisdiction. We get a judge to sign a modified protective custody order. Make it airtight."

**REYES:**  
"Exactly. We still get weekly check-ins. We lock her legal status in place, but we stop looking like 1980s East Germany."

**ASSISTANT ADA (perks up):**  
"And we announce it with a joint statement. Emphasize cooperation with the Canadian consulate, respect for international law, patient dignity. Let them own the optics. We own the legal territory."

**REYES (pointing):**  
"Bingo. We hand them the ribbon to cut. Let their ambassador get a photo op while we put a leash on the girl behind the curtain. That way, Bennett King doesn’t get to run the table again before lunch."

**INVESTIGATOR:**  
"And if she bolts?"

**REYES (flat):**  
"Then we go full Terminator. She skips, we drop the hammer, and the entire international narrative becomes *she betrayed our generosity.* We turn the tide."

**REYES (leaning forward):**  
"But we’ve got to move fast. Before the next royal cousin or foreign minister logs on and makes us the villain in their little indie documentary. Somebody wake up the judge we need. Someone draft the language for the release order. I want soft custody with firm edges and zero PR fingerprints."

**(Beat)**

**REYES:**  
"Also. Someone bring me a fresh shirt. I’m about to go on NY1 and I smell like defeat."

The room nods, fires up. They’ve got a plan. Now they just have to sell it. Before 5:00 a.m. Before the world logs back in.

---

**EXT. NY1 STREET INTERVIEW SETUP – 5:17 A.M. – STILL DARK, COLD NEW YORK MORNING**

Reyes stands in a perfectly pressed white shirt, looking like he hasn’t slept (because he hasn’t), but appearing calm, measured, and in control. Behind him, the early rumble of a city that never sleeps but often snoozes plays like white noise. A red NY1 mic is inches from his face. Lights on. Cameras rolling.

**REYES (to camera, tone measured):**  
"Good morning, New York. I want to make one thing abundantly clear: we are not in the business of spectacle. We are in the business of justice. Of public safety. Of doing right by this city—by *all* its residents, and by those who visit us and fall under our care."

**(Beat. He lets that simmer. Then pivots—gracefully.)**

"We've heard the voices. From the public. From our friends in Ottawa. From the broader global community. And while the work of justice must be deliberate—it must also be humane."

**REYES (camera gets a little tighter on his face):**  
"Ms. Lavigne is being transitioned from hospital custody to a private medical facility. This change will ensure her continued care in a setting that respects her dignity, while allowing this office to pursue ongoing legal inquiries without interference or delay."

**(He pauses. Deliberate now. He knows how the clip will play online.)**

"This isn’t surrender. This is strategy. This is the City of New York doing what it’s always done—adapt, assess, respond."

**(He softens just a touch.)**

"And to our neighbors north of the border: we hear you. We respect our international relationships. And we hope for nothing more than a full recovery for Ms. Lavigne—and clarity, wherever the evidence leads us."

**NY1 REPORTER (off-camera):**  
"Do you feel pressure from the public campaign?"

**REYES (grins dryly):**  
"I feel pressure every day. From my conscience. From the law. But no—Twitter doesn’t prosecute cases. DAs do."

**NY1 REPORTER:**  
"And Bennett King?"

**REYES (beat, then laughs softly):**  
"Bennett King plays the game better than anyone I know. And this time? He played it clean. That’s what stings."

**(He nods. Camera pans out.)**

**REYES:**  
"Now if you’ll excuse me, I’ve got a city to run and a case to win."

He walks off, the camera following just long enough to catch the tension in his shoulders as he vanishes into a waiting black SUV.

**OFF-CAMERA VOICE (back in the studio):**  
"That was ADA Reyes of Manhattan’s District Attorney’s office. Flipping the script on the unfolding story…"

And just like that, the tide begins to shift. Maybe.

---

Madeline closes her laptop, her fingers finally still after hours of relentless tapping. The glow from her multiple screens bathes her face, tired but satisfied. Her war—the one she'd launched from behind the curtain—had struck like lightning, loud, bright, and impossible to ignore.

She stands slowly, letting the silence of the room settle over her. The adrenaline is fading, and beneath the steel armor she wears for the world, fatigue creeps in like a tide. She brushes her teeth with the precision of someone who quantifies even her hygiene, then climbs into bed, slipping beneath sheets she barely remembers pulling up the night before.

She lies still in the dark.  For the first time in what feels like days, Madeline doesn’t calculate. She doesn’t strategize. She doesn’t plan. She exhales slowly.  Her eyes close.

Sleep comes easy.

Warriors need rest, too.

---

# **FIN**

---
